Position of Hands: Below Navel vs. Chest
Dispute between Hanafis and Shafi‘is on hand placement in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on hand placement in prayer and evaluate the Shafi‘i counter-argument using dalil and usul principles.

Core Idea
Hand placement below navel is sunnah for Hanafis, proven by Ali’s statement and avoidance of imitation; Shafi‘i proof from 'wa inhar' is refuted.

One of the well-known differences between Hanafis and Shafi‘is is where to place the hands during prayer. This passage presents both sides: the Shafi‘i proof from Quran and reason, and the Hanafi proof from the statement of Ali (ra) and the principle of reverence. Understanding this dispute trains you in how madhahib weigh different evidences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: folding hands below the navel is sunnah muakkadah for Hanafis. Note the authority (Ali's statement and reverence).
The word 'sunnah' in Ali's statement refers to the Prophet's practice.
2
Identify the Shafi‘i position and its proofs
The Shafi‘i position: hands on chest. Their proof: verse 108:2 ('fasalli li rabbika wa inhar') interpreted by some as placing right hand on left on chest, and the chest being the seat of faith.
Note that the interpretation of 'wa inhar' as hand placement is not the apparent meaning.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the verse primarily means sacrifice, not hand position. The chest argument is subjective; clear text (Ali's statement) is preferred.
The Hanafis also cite avoidance of tashabbuh with non-Muslims.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis fold below navel; Shafi‘is fold on chest. Both practices are valid within their respective schools.
This is a difference in recommended action, not validity of prayer.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi relied-upon position is below navel, based on the explicit statement of Ali and the principle of reverence.
The tarjih authority: later Hanafi commentators (e.g. Kifayah) supported this view.

Source Text

تیسرا مسئلہ ہاتھ رکھنے کی جگہ کا ہے پس ہمارے نزدیک افضل یہ ہے کہ زیر ناف ہاتھ باندھے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک سینہ پر ہاتھ رکھنا افضل ہے امام شافعی کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فصل لربک و الحربے یعنی اپنے رب کے واسطے نماز پڑھ اور دایاں ہاتھ باتیں پر سینہ پر رکھے علامہ ابن الہمام اور صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا کہ مفسرین نے کہا کہ وانحر سے دائیں ہاتھ کا بائیں پر سینہ پر رکھنا مراد ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مینہ نور ایمان کی جگہ ہے لہذا انماز کے اندر اپنے ہاتھ سے اس کی حفاظت کرنا اولی ہے۔ ہماری دلیل حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کا اثر ہے یعنی ان من السنة وضع اليمين على الشمال تحت السرۃ اور لفظ سنت سے بالعموم رسول اللہ کی سنت مراد ہوتی ہے پیس ثابت ہوا کہ زیر ناف ہاتھ باندھنا مسنون ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے زیر ناف ہاتھ باندھنے میں تعظیم ہے اور نماز کے اندر تعظیم ہی مقصود ہوتی ہے اس لئے بھی زیر ناف ہاتھ باندھنا
صاحب کفایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ زیر ناف ہاتھ باندھنے میں اہل کتاب کے ساتھ تشبہ سے بعد ہو جاتا ہے اور ستر عورت سے قرب ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے بھی زیر ناف ہاتھ باندھنا اولی ہے اور امام شافعی کا لفظ و انسحر سے استدلال کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ آیت میں وانسحر سے مراد عید کی نماز کے بعد قربانی کے جانور کا نحر ( ذبح) کرنا ہے۔ (کنایہ )
Third issue: The place of placing the hands. So according to us, the superior way is to fold hands below the navel. According to Imam Shafi'i, placing hands on the chest is superior. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the saying of Allah: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' (108:2) meaning: pray to your Lord and place the right hand on the left on the chest. Allama Ibn al-Humam and the author of Inayah stated that the commentators said 'And sacrifice' refers to placing the right hand on the left on the chest. His second proof is that the chest is the place of the light of faith, so it is more appropriate to protect it with the hands during prayer. Our proof is the effect of Sayyiduna Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), namely: 'Indeed it is from the sunnah to place the right on the left below the navel.' And by the word 'sunnah', generally the sunnah of the Messenger of Allah is intended. So it is established that folding hands below the navel is sunnah. Our second proof is that there is reverence in folding below the navel, and reverence is the objective in prayer; therefore also folding below the navel is superior. The author of Kifayah wrote that in folding below the navel, there is distance from imitating the People of the Book, and it is closer to covering the private parts; therefore folding below the navel is superior. And Imam Shafi'i's deduction from 'wa inhar' is incorrect, because in the verse 'wa inhar' refers to the slaughter of the sacrificial animal after Eid prayer.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the placement of hands during prayer. The Hanafis consider it superior to place hands below the navel, while the Shafi'is prefer the chest. The Shafi'i proof is the verse 'fasalli li rabbika wa inhar' (108:2), interpreted by some as placing hands on the chest. The Hanafi response clarifies that the primary meaning of 'inhar' is sacrifice, not hand position. The Shafi'i also argue that the chest is the seat of faith and should be protected. The Hanafi proof uses the statement of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) explicitly stating 'below the navel' as sunnah. The term 'sunnah' in this context refers to the Prophet's practice. Additionally, folding below the navel shows more reverence and avoids resemblance to non-Muslims (who may fold on chest). The author of Kifayah adds that it is closer to the private parts, aiding modesty. The Hanafi response concludes that the verse 'wa inhar' does not support the chest position.

Key Terms
تحت السرۃ (tahta al-surrah): The area below the navel, specifically the upper part of the lower abdomen.
اشبہ (tashabbuh): Imitating or resembling others, here avoided by folding below navel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary Hanafi proof for folding hands below the navel?
A) The verse 'fasalli li rabbika wa inhar'
B) The statement of Ali ibn Abi Talib (ra)
C) The chest is the seat of faith
D) The practice of the People of the Book

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that folding hands below the navel is the sunnah, supported by the explicit statement of Ali (ra) and the principles of reverence and avoidance of imitation.

When to Fold Hands: Timing of Wadh'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of hand-folding in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on when to fold hands in prayer and apply the Hidayah rule to determine when folding is sunnah.

Core Idea
Fold hands in every standing where dhikr is sunnah; let them loose in qawmah and between Eid takbirs.

This lesson examines a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute: the exact moment to fold hands in salah. While all Hanafis agree that folding is sunnah, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf place it at the start of qiyam, while Imam Muhammad delays it until qira'ah. The author of Hidayah resolves this by a broader rule: fold in any standing where dhikr is sunnah. Understanding this rule will clarify several postures in prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the view of Sheikhayn (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad regarding when to fold hands.
Sheikhayn: fold from the start of qiyam. Muhammad: fold only when beginning qira'ah.
2
Identify the basis of the dispute
Determine whether folding is a sunnah of qiyam (standing) or qira'ah (recitation).
This core difference leads to practical variation in timing.
3
Examine the Hidayah rule
The author of Hidayah formulates a dabita: every standing (qiyam) in which some dhikr is sunnah, folding is sunnah. If not, folding is not sunnah.
This rule resolves the dispute by focusing on the nature of the qiyam.
4
Apply the rule to various standings
Use the rule to determine folding in qiyam (first standing), qawmah (between ruku and sujud), qunut (in witr), janazah prayer, and between Eid takbirs.
Result: fold in qiyam, qunut, janazah; do not fold in qawmah or between Eid takbirs.
5
Note the mufta bihi and its authority
Later scholars like Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and Sadr al-Kabir gave fatwa based on the Hidayah rule.
This is the operative position for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چوتھا مسئلہ یہ ہےکہ نمازی ہاتھ کب باندھے سو اس بارے میں شیخین کا ذہب یہ ہے کہ ہاتھ باندھنا قیام کی نت ہے اور امام مد سے مروی ہے کہ قرآت کی سنت ہے چنانچہ شا ہ میں شیخین کے نزدیک ہاتھ باندھنا مسنون ہوگا۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک حالت شاہ میں لا یغف ہاتھ چھوڑے کے اور قرات شروع ہونے پر ہاتھ باندھ لے۔

سنها ال
صاحب ہدایہ نے ہاتھ باندھنے اور کچھوڑنے کے بارے میں یہ ضابطہ بیان فرمایا ہے کہ ہر وہ قیام (خواد حقیقی ہو یا حکمی ) جس میں کیا استغفر ذکر مسنون ہو تو ایسے قیام میں ہاتھ باندھے اور جو قیام ایسانہ ہواس میں ہاتھ باندھنا مسنون نہیں ہے یہی قول صحیح ہے۔ اس قول پر شمسی الائمہ اللہ خصی صدر الکبیه بر بان الائمہ اور صدر الشہید حسام الائمہ فتوی دیا کرتے تھے پس اس اصول کے ماتحت حالت قنوت اور نماز جنازہ میں ہاتھ باندھنا مسنون ہوگا اور قومہ ( رکوع اور سجدہ کے درمیان ) اور عیدین کی تکبیروں کے درمیان ہاتھ چھوڑ نا مسنون ہونگا۔
Fourth issue: When should the worshipper fold his hands? Regarding this, the madhhab of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that folding hands is a sunnah of the standing (qiyam). And it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that it is a sunnah of the recitation (qira'ah). So according to the two shaykhs, folding hands is sunnah in the initial standing. And according to Imam Muhammad, in the initial standing one does not fold hands, but when recitation begins, one folds them.

The author of Hidayah stated this rule (dabita) regarding folding and releasing hands: Every standing (qiyam, whether actual or hukmi) in which some dhikr is sunnah, then in such standing one folds hands. And any standing that is not like that, folding hands is not sunnah. This is the correct statement. Based on this, the following scholars used to issue fatwa: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, Sadr al-Kabir, Burhan al-A'imma, and Sadr al-Shahid Husam al-A'imma. So according to this principle, folding hands is sunnah in the qunut standing and in the funeral prayer (janazah). And letting hands loose is sunnah in the qawma (standing between ruku and sujud) and between the takbirs of the two Eids.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage covers two sub-issues: the timing of hand-folding and a general rule for when to fold. First, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) hold that folding hands is a sunnah of the qiyam (standing) itself, meaning one should fold immediately after takbir and before reciting thana. Imam Muhammad holds it is a sunnah of the qira'ah (recitation), so he prefers to keep hands loose during the initial thana and fold them when beginning Quran recitation. The commentator then quotes the author of Hidayah's rule (dabita): In any standing (qiyam) where some dhikr (remembrance of Allah) is sunnah, it is sunnah to fold hands. If the standing is not specifically for dhikr, then folding is not sunnah. Application: In qunut (standing in witr with du'a) and in funeral prayer (where there are four takbirs with standing), hands are folded because dhikr is sunnah there. In the qawma (brief standing after ruku before sujud) and between the takbirs of Eid prayer, hands are not folded; they are left loose. This ruling is the basis for fatwa by later prominent Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms
قیام (qiyam): Standing posture in prayer; includes actual standing and 'hukmi' (those in which standing is implied, like in funeral prayer).
قومہ (qawmah): The brief standing after rising from ruku and before prostrating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rule established by the author of Hidayah, when should a worshipper fold his hands?
A) In every standing of the prayer.
B) Only in the first standing (qiyam) of each rak'ah.
C) In any standing where dhikr is sunnah, such as qunut and janazah.
D) Never, because it is optional.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: fold hands in any standing where dhikr is sunnah; otherwise leave them loose.

The Opening Supplication (Thana): Basic Wording and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on the wording of thana and whether to add other supplications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi for thana in fard prayers and explain why the tawajjuh supplication is not added.

Core Idea
In fard prayers, the thana is only 'Subhanaka...'; the longer tawajjuh supplication is reserved for supererogatory prayers.

This lesson examines the correct wording of the opening supplication (thana) in prayer according to the Hanafi school. While the basic form is clear, there is an internal dispute about whether to add the longer tawajjuh supplication. We will analyze the evidence from hadith and understand the preferred practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic thana text
First, locate the exact wording of the thana as stated by Imam Quduri: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabaraka ismuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruk.' Note that some less famous narrations add 'wa jalla thana'uka'.
The basic text is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Yusuf has two narrations: the first agrees with the basic thana; the second allows adding the tawajjuh supplication ('Inni wajjahtu...'). Identify the two positions and their bases.
The dispute is about the scope of thana in fard prayers.
3
Examine the dalil of each side
The two shaykhs (the majority) rely on the hadith of Anas that the Prophet only recited 'Subhanaka...' without addition. Abu Yusuf's second view relies on a hadith of Ali that the Prophet recited 'Inni wajjahtu'. Analyse the authenticity and interpretation.
The hadith of Anas is considered stronger for fard prayers.
4
Understand the tarjih (preferred view)
The Hanafi school prefers the view of no addition, because the hadith of Ali is interpreted as specific to tahajjud (night prayer). Also, the phrase 'wa jalla thana'uka' is not in famous narrations and thus not used in fard.
The mufta bihi is to recite only the basic thana in fard prayers.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
When performing fard salah, after takbir and folding hands, recite only 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...' and proceed to ta'awwudh and Fatiha. Do not add 'Inni wajjahtu' or any other supplication for thana.
Supererogatory prayers (especially tahajjud) may include the longer supplication if desired.

What should be recited in the thana (opening supplication)? Statements of the jurists. Then he says: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...' to the end. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he added to it his saying: 'Inni wajjahtu wajhiya...' to the end, based on the narration of Ali that the Prophet used to say that. And their (the two shaykhs') proof is the narration of Anas that when the Prophet opened the prayer, he said the takbir and recited 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...' to the end, and did not add to this. And what Abu Yusuf narrated is carried upon the night prayer (tahajjud). And his saying 'wa jalla thana'uka' is not mentioned in the famous narrations, so it should not be brought in the obligatory prayers. And the better view is not to bring the tawajjuh (Inni wajjahtu) before the takbir, so that the intention becomes connected with the takbir; this is correct. Translation: Then he recites 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...' to the end. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he added to this thana 'Inni wajjahtu wajhiya...' to the end, because Ali narrated that the Prophet used to say it. And the proof of both sides (the two shaykhs) is the narration of Anas that when the Messenger of Allah opened the prayer, he said takbir and recited 'Subhanaka Allahumma...' to the end, without adding to it. And what Abu Yusuf narrated is carried upon tahajjud. And the phrase 'wa jalla thana'uka' is not mentioned in the famous narrations, so it is not brought in fara'id. And it is preferable not to recite the tawajjuh (Inni wajjahtu) before the takbir, so that the intention is connected with the takbir; this is correct. Explanation: Imam Quduri said: After folding his hands, the worshipper recites thana, and the thana is: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabaraka ismuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruk.' And in some less famous narrations, 'wa ta'ala jadduka wa jalla thana'uka wa la ilaha ghayruk' is found. But since 'jalla thana'uka' is not mentioned in the famous narrations, it should not be said in obligatory prayers. As for whether to bring any other supplication along with the thana, regarding this, the madhhab of both sides and Imam Abu Yusuf's first statement is not to mix any other supplication with the thana. And Imam Abu Yusuf's second statement is that the worshipper may combine with the thana this supplication: 'Inni wajjahtu wajhiya lilladhi fatara al-samawati wa al-ard...' And in some narrations, after '...wa ana min al-muslimin' the following words are also mentioned: 'Allahumma innaka anta al-malik la ilaha illa anta, anta rabbi wa ana abduka, zalamtu nafsi wa'taraftu bi-dhanbi, faghfir li dhunubi jami'an.'
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage discusses the wording of the opening supplication (thana) in prayer after takbir and hand-folding. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding what to recite. The basic thana, as stated by Imam Quduri, is: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika, wa tabaraka ismuka, wa ta'ala jadduka, wa la ilaha ghayruk.' Some less famous narrations add 'wa jalla thana'uka'. However, since this addition is not widely transmitted, it is not recited in obligatory prayers. Then there is disagreement on whether to add the tawajjuh supplication ('Inni wajjahtu') to the thana. Imam Abu Yusuf has two narrations: the first is not to add anything; the second is to add the longer supplication of facing the qibla. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is not to add, because the authentic hadith of Anas shows the Prophet only recited 'Subhanaka...' and did not add more. The narration of Ali regarding 'Inni wajjahtu' is interpreted as specific to tahajjud (night prayer), not fard. The commentator also mentions the ruling on timing: it is better not to recite the tawajjuh before the takbir to ensure the intention connects with the takbir. The final practice: in fard prayers, only the basic thana is recited; the addition of 'Inni wajjahtu' is left for supererogatory prayers, particularly tahajjud.

Key Terms
ثناء (thana): The opening supplication in prayer recited after takbir and before Quran recitation.
توجہ (tawajjuh): The supplication 'Inni wajjahtu...' directing one's face to the Creator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both 'Subhanaka...' and 'Inni wajjahtu'.
B) Only 'Subhanaka...' without additions.
C) Only 'Inni wajjahtu' without 'Subhanaka...'.
D) The Fatihah directly.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fard prayers, the thana is only 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...'; the longer supplication 'Inni wajjahtu' is reserved for supererogatory prayers like tahajjud.

Ruling on Folding Hands (Qabd) Based on Type of Qiyam
Rule for folding hands based on qiyam type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for folding hands (qabd) in prayer by identifying which types of qiyam require qabd and which require sadl.

Core Idea
Hands are folded only in a qiyam where sunnah dhikr is recited; otherwise, they are dropped.

In the Hanafi school, the practice of folding hands (qabd) during prayer is not uniform across all standing positions. The author of al-Hidayah establishes a precise criterion: the presence of a sunnah dhikr determines whether hands are folded or left loose. This lesson unpacks that rule and its application to various postures in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qiyam in question
Determine whether the posture is considered a qiyam (standing) in the prayer, whether actual (e.g., standing in fard prayer) or ruling-based (e.g., standing in qunut or funeral prayer).
Hanafis categorize qiyam broadly to include positions where one is deemed to be standing, even if not fully upright, such as during qunut.
2
Check for sunnah dhikr
Ascertain whether a sunnah dhikr (prescribed remembrance) is recited during that qiyam. Examples include recitation in obligatory prayer, qunut supplication in witr, and du'a in funeral prayer.
The dhikr must be part of the sunnah of prayer, not optional.
3
Apply the rule
If a sunnah dhikr is present, folding hands (qabd) is sunnah. If not, dropping hands (sadl) is sunnah.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school.
4
Test with examples
Apply the rule to specific postures: qawmah (pause between ruku and sujud) has no sunnah dhikr, so sadl applies. Between Eid takbirs, no sunnah dhikr is recited, so sadl applies. Qunut in witr has sunnah dhikr, so qabd applies.
The passage explicitly gives these examples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ نے ہاتھ باندھنے اور کچھوڑنے کے بارے میں یہ ضابطہ بیان فرمایا ہے کہ ہر وہ قیام (خواہ حقیقی ہو یا حکمی) جس میں ذکر مسنون ہو تو ایسے قیام میں ہاتھ باندھے اور جو قیام ایسا نہ ہو اس میں ہاتھ باندھنا مسنون نہیں ہے یہی قول صحیح ہے۔ اس قول پر شمسی الائمہ اللہ خصی صدر الکبیه بر بان الائمہ اور صدر الشہید حسام الائمہ فتوی دیا کرتے تھے پس اس اصول کے ماتحت حالت قنوت اور نماز جنازہ میں ہاتھ باندھنا مسنون ہوگا اور قومہ (رکوع اور سجدہ کے درمیان) اور عیدین کی تکبیروں کے درمیان ہاتھ چھوڑ نا مسنون ہونگا۔
The author of Hidayah stated this rule regarding folding and dropping hands: Every qiyam (whether actual or ruling) in which a sunnah dhikr is performed, in such qiyam hands are folded; and a qiyam which is not like this, in it folding hands is not sunnah. This is the correct statement. Shams al-Aimmah, Allah yarhamahu, Sadr al-Kabir, Burhan al-Aimmah, and Sadr al-Shahid Husam al-Aimmah used to give fatwa on this. So based on this principle, in the state of qunut and funeral prayer, folding hands is sunnah, and in qawmah (between ruku and sajdah) and between the takbirs of the two Eids, dropping hands is sunnah.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents a general rule (ضابطہ) established by the author of al-Hidayah regarding the practice of folding hands (qabd) in prayer. The rule is that hands should be folded in any standing position (qiyam) where a sunnah dhikr is prescribed, whether the qiyam is actual (like the standing in obligatory prayer) or ruling-based (like the standing in qunut or funeral prayer). Conversely, if the qiyam does not involve a sunnah dhikr, then hands should be left loose (sadl). The text then confirms this as the correct view (قول صحیح) and notes that several later Hanafi authorities (Shams al-Aimmah, Sadr al-Kabir, etc.) issued fatwa based on it. Examples are given: in qunut and funeral prayer, folding is sunnah; in qawmah (the pause between ruku and sujud) and between the takbirs of Eid prayers, dropping is sunnah. This reflects a practical application of the underlying principle that qabd is tied to dhikr.

Key Terms
قیام (qiyam): Standing posture in prayer; here includes both actual standing and rulings-based standing (e.g., qunut).
قومہ (qawmah): The brief standing posture between ruku and sujud.
قنوت (qunut): A supplication recited in the last rak'ah of witr prayer or in times of calamity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) In qawmah (between ruku and sajdah)
C) In qunut during witr prayer
D) In the qawmah after ruku in funeral prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule for folding hands: if the standing position includes a sunnah dhikr, fold; otherwise, drop.

The Thana Recitation and the Tawajjuh Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on thana content

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on thana recitation in obligatory prayers and explain why the tawajjuh is not added, based on hadith evidence and school tarjih.

Core Idea
The tawajjuh supplication belongs to tahajjud, not to thana in fard prayers.

When you begin prayer, you recite the opening supplication (thana). But should you add another supplication? This lesson examines a dispute within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Yusuf held that the tawajjuh (Inni wajjahtu) should be included, while the relied-upon view restricts thana to Subhanaka Allahumma. Let's trace the evidence and see how the school settled this.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What is the act being discussed? Recitation of thana after takbir. In Hanafi fiqh, thana is a sunnah muakkadah. The passage concerns whether to add another supplication.
Thana is not fard or wajib; it is recommended.
2
State the Disputed Point
The dispute: Should the words 'Inni wajjahtu wajhi' be added to the thana in obligatory prayers? Abu Yusuf says yes; the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) say no.
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement.
3
Examine the Evidence for Each Side
Abu Yusuf relies on a hadith of Ali that the Prophet recited 'Inni wajjahtu...'. The two rely on a hadith of Anas that the Prophet only recited 'Subhanaka...' and added nothing.
Both hadith are authentic but must be reconciled.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response and Tarjih
The Hanafi response: The hadith of Ali is interpreted to refer to tahajjud (night prayer), not obligatory prayers. Additional point: The phrase 'wa jalla thana'uka' is not widely reported for fard prayers. The preferred view (al-awla) is not to add the tawajjuh, so that the intention is directly connected to the takbir. This is the correct position (al-sahih).
Tarjih is based on textual reconciliation and usul principles.
5
Practical Consequence (Thamarah)
In practice, one recites only 'Subhanaka Allahumma...' after takbir in fard prayers. Adding 'Inni wajjahtu...' is not recommended, though the prayer remains valid if added.
The dispute only affects the sunnah, not validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقول سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك الى اخره وعن ابى يوسف انه يضم اليه قوله انى وجهت وجهي الى اخره لرواية على ان النبي عليه السلام كان يقول ذلك ولهما رواية انس ان النبي عليه السلام كان اذا افتتح الصلوة كبر وقرأ سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك الى اخره ولم يزد على هذا ومارواه محمول على انى وجهت وجهي فى التهجد وقوله وجل ثناؤك يذكر فى المشاهير فلا يأتى به فى الفرائض والأولى ان لاياتي بالتوجه قبل التكبير ليتصل النية به هو الصحيح
Then he says 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...' to the end. And from Abu Yusuf that he adds to it his saying 'Inni wajjahtu wajhi...' to the end, due to the narration of Ali that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to say that. And the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] have the narration of Anas that the Prophet, when he opened the prayer, would say the takbir and recite 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...' to the end and did not add to this. And what is narrated (by Abu Yusuf) is interpreted as [the Prophet saying] 'Inni wajjahtu wajhi' in the night prayer (tahajjud). And his saying 'wa jalla thana'uka' is mentioned in well-known narrations, so one should not bring it in the obligatory prayers. And it is more proper that he should not recite the tawajjuh before the takbir so that the intention is connected to it; this is the correct view.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage discusses the recitation of the opening supplication (thana) in prayer. The base text states that after takbir, one says 'Subhanaka Allahumma...'. Imam Abu Yusuf held that the supplication 'Inni wajjahtu wajhi...' (the tawajjuh) should be added to the thana, based on a hadith from Ali ibn Abi Talib that the Prophet used to recite it. However, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rely on the hadith of Anas that the Prophet only recited 'Subhanaka...' and did not add anything else. The author of al-Hidayah (the commentator) explains that Abu Yusuf's report is understood to refer to the Prophet's practice in tahajjud (night prayer), not in obligatory prayers. Additionally, the phrase 'wa jalla thana'uka' is not found in well-known narrations for obligatory prayers. Therefore, the preferred view (al-awla) is not to recite the tawajjuh before the takbir, so that the intention (niyyah) is directly connected to the takbir. This is identified as the correct position (al-sahih).

Key Terms
ثناء (thana): The opening supplication 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...' recited in prayer.
توجہ (tawajjuh): The supplication 'Inni wajjahtu wajhi...' recited after takbir, also known as the opening du'a.
تهجد (tahajjud): The night prayer performed after sleeping, highly recommended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only in obligatory prayers.
C) In voluntary prayers like tahajjud, not in obligatory.
D) It should never be recited.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view is to recite only 'Subhanaka Allahumma...' in obligatory prayers, reserving the tawajjuh for tahajjud.

Ruling, Place, and Wording of Ta'awwudh in Prayer
Ruling on ta'awwudh in salah with proof and practical consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling, placement, and preferred wording of ta'awwudh in prayer according to the Hanafi school, and apply the rulings for masbuq and muqtadi.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah before qira'ah, not after thana, and is recited by the masbuq but not the muqtadi.

In this lesson, we examine the ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) that precedes Quranic recitation in prayer. Based on the Quranic verse (16:98), the Hanafi school defines its ruling, timing, and wording. We also explore how this affects the masbuq (latecomer) and muqtadi (follower), and a minor difference with Abu Yusuf regarding Eid takbirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act of ta'awwudh? What is its hukm (sunnah muakkadah) according to the Hanafi school?
The ruling is based on the Quranic verse, not classified as wajib or fard.
2
Locate the Quranic dalil
Which verse commands ta'awwudh? How does the Hanafi school interpret the imperative as indicating recommendation (nadb)?
The verse is Surah al-Nahl 16:98; the imperative 'fasta'idh' carries a sunnah ruling due to contextual evidence.
3
Determine the placement in prayer
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, ta'awwudh belongs to qira'ah, not thana. What does this imply about its timing?
It is recited immediately before qira'ah, after the opening supplication (thana) if any.
4
Apply to masbuq and muqtadi
Since ta'awwudh follows qira'ah, who among the worshippers recites it? The masbuq (latecomer) or the muqtadi (follower)?
The masbuq recites it when making up missed rak'ahs; the muqtadi does not, as the imam's qira'ah suffices.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on Eid takbirs
What is the disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding ta'awwudh in Eid prayer?
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold it is delayed after the extra takbirs; Abu Yusuf differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستعيذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم لقوله تعالى فاذا قرأت الْقُرْآن فَاسْتعذ بالله من الشَّيْطَانِ الرَّحِيم معناه اذا اردت قراءة القرآن والاولى ان يقول استعيذ بالله ليوافق القران ويقرب منه اعوذ بالله ثم التعود تبع للقراءة دون الثناء عند ابي حنيفة و محمد لما تلونا حتى يأتى به المسبوق دون المقتدى و يؤخر عن تكبيرات العيد خلافا لا بي يوسف
And he seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan, for Allah Most High said: 'When you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan.' Its meaning is: when you intend to recite the Quran. And it is better that he says 'Asta'idhu billah' to agree with the Quran, and near to it is 'A'udhu billah'. Then the ta'awwudh is a follower of the recitation, not of the thana, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, because of what we recited, so that the masbuq should recite it, not the muqtadi, and it is delayed after the takbirs of Eid, contrary to Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage addresses three aspects of ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) in prayer: its ruling, its place, and its wording. The ruling is that ta'awwudh is recited because of the Quranic verse (16:98), which is interpreted as a command for when one intends to read the Quran. The preferred wording is to say 'Asta'idhu billah' to match the Quran, though 'A'udhu billah' is also acceptable. As for placement, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, ta'awwudh belongs to the recitation (qira'ah), not to the thana. This means it is recited immediately before Quranic recitation, not before the thana. From this, consequences follow: a masbuq (latecomer) who joins the prayer late should recite ta'awwudh, but the muqtadi (follower) does not, since the imam's qira'ah suffices. Also, during Eid prayers, the ta'awwudh is delayed until after the extra takbirs, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf differed on this placement. The text thus gives a clear rule aligned with the majority Hanafi position.

Key Terms
تعوذ (ta'awwudh): The act of seeking refuge with Allah from Shaytan, recited before Quran recitation.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joins the congregational prayer late and misses some rak'ahs.
مقتدی (muqtadi): A follower in congregational prayer who prays behind the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Ta'awwudh is a sunnah before qira'ah, recited by the one reciting (including masbuq) but not by the muqtadi, and delayed after takbirs in Eid prayer.

Recitation of Tawajjuh after Thana'
Intra-Hanafi ruling on reciting tawajjuh after thana'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two intra-Hanafi positions on reciting tawajjuh after thana' in obligatory prayers, identify the primary dalil for each, and explain the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Tawajjuh is not recited after thana' in obligatory prayers — the hadith of Ali is specific to tahajjud.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the opening supplication (tawajjuh) recited after the opening takbir. While all agree thana' is recited, the question is whether one should also recite the supplication 'inni wajjahtu wajhiya' after thana'. The source text presents the views of the two sides and the ruling of the Hidayah, which settles the matter for the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Note that Imam Abu Yusuf holds that tawajjuh should be recited after thana' in all prayers, while Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that it is not recited in obligatory prayers.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab one.
2
Locate the dalil for each side
Abu Yusuf relies on the hadith of Ali that the Prophet recited tawajjuh with the opening takbir. The majority relies on the hadith of Anas that the Prophet only recited thana' after takbir, without mentioning tawajjuh.
Both hadith are authentic, but context matters.
3
Understand the tarjih (preference)
The author of al-Hidayah argues that the hadith of Ali is restricted to tahajjud (voluntary night prayer), as additional transmissions indicate. Therefore, for obligatory prayers, only the practice of Anas is followed.
This is a classic example of taqyid (restriction) in usul.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
In practice, a follower of Abu Yusuf would recite tawajjuh after thana' in every prayer; a follower of the majority would omit it in obligatory prayers. The mufta bihi is to omit it.
The difference is minor but shows how usul principles affect daily worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفۃ الصلوة
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم لا يغفر الذنوب الا انت واهدنى لاحسن الاخلاق لايهدى لاحسنها الاانت واصرف عنى سبها لا يصرف عنى سبها الا انت لبیک و سعدیک و الخير كله فی یدیک والشرلیس الیک اتابک والیک تبارکت و تعاليت استغفرك واتوب اليك فقہاء کی اصطلاح میں اس دعا کا نام توجہ ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کی روایت ہے کہ حضور پیر شاہ کے ساتھہ اس دعا کو بھی پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ طرفین کی دلیل حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ کی روایت ہے ان النبي كان اذا فتح الصلوة كبرو قراسبحانك اللهم وبحمدك الى اخره - صاحب بدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ نے اس سے زیادہ کچھ بیان نہیں کیا پس معلوم ہوا کہ ثناء کے بعد تو جہ یعنی انی و جهت آن پڑھنا ثابت نہیں ہے۔
مصنف ہدایہ نے کہا کہ امام ابو یوسف کی پیش کردہ روایت تہجد کی نماز پر موقوف ہے یعنی حضور پیم نفل نماز میں اس کو پڑھا کرتے تھے اور فرمائش میں ثناء کے علاوہ کوئی دعا پر سنا منقول نہیں ہے۔ فاضل مصنف نے کہا کہ اولی یہ ہے کہ نبیت کے بعد اور تکبیر سے پہلے بھی انسی و جهت اخ نہ پڑھے تا کہ نیت کا تکبیر کے ساتھ اتصال ہو جائے اور درمیان میں انسی و جهت وجھی التا فاضل نہ ہوں۔ کہیں میں ہے۔ اور بعض متاخرین جن میں فقیہ ابواللیث بھی ہیں فرماتے ہیں کہ نیت اور تکبیر کے درمیان اس کا پڑھنا جائز ہے
Chapter: Description of Prayer. Ashraf al-Bidaya Urdu Sharh Hidayah Volume 2. 'None forgives sins except You, guide me to the best of manners...' In the terminology of jurists, this supplication is called tawajjuh. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is the narration of Hadrat Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet used to recite this supplication with istiftah. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is the narration of Hadrat Anas: 'When the Prophet opened prayer, he would say takbir and recite Subhanaka Allahumma...' The author of al-Bidaya says that Hadrat Anas did not mention more than that, so it is known that reciting tawajjuh after thana' is not established. The author of Hidayah said that the narration presented by Imam Abu Yusuf is restricted to tahajjud prayer, meaning the Prophet used to recite it in voluntary prayer, and in obligatory prayer nothing other than thana' is transmitted. The author said that it is better not to recite 'inni wajjahtu' after intention and before takbir so that the intention connects with the takbir without interruption. Some later scholars, including Faqih Abu al-Layth, say that reciting it between intention and takbir is permissible.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on reciting the tawajjuh supplication (the opening supplication beginning with 'inni wajjahtu wajhiya') after the thana' (Subhanaka Allahumma) in prayer. The passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author first presents the position of Imam Abu Yusuf, who holds that tawajjuh should be recited after thana', based on a narration from Ali that the Prophet used to recite it along with the opening takbir. Then the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (the 'two' or 'Sahibayn') is given, based on a narration from Anas that the Prophet only said takbir and then recited Subhanaka Allahumma, with no mention of tawajjuh. The author of al-Bidaya concludes that tawajjuh after thana' is not established. The author of al-Hidayah further clarifies that Abu Yusuf's narration is specifically for tahajjud (night prayer), not for obligatory prayers. Then the preferred view (al-awla) is stated: it is better not to recite tawajjuh between intention and takbir to ensure immediate connection. However, some later scholars like Faqih Abu al-Layth permit reciting it in that interval. This shows the range of opinion within the Hanafi school on this minor point.

Key Terms
توجہ (tawajjuh): The opening supplication recited after the opening takbir, beginning with 'inni wajjahtu wajhiya...'
ثناء (thanā'): The praise of Allah recited after takbir, i.e., 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, when is the tawajjuh supplication (inni wajjahtu) recited in obligatory prayers?
A) After thana'
B) Between intention and takbir
C) It is not recited at all in obligatory prayers
D) After the recitation of Surah Fatiha

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the preferred (mufta bihi) position is not to recite tawajjuh after thana' in obligatory prayers; it is only established for tahajjud.

Ta'awwudh in Prayer: Status, Position, and Wording
Ruling on seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) in prayer: its legal status, position, and preferred wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ta'awwudh (its sunnah status, its position before recitation, and who recites it) and explain the proofs and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah, not wajib, and it follows recitation, not thana' — only those who recite Quran in prayer recite it.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses three key questions about ta'awwudh (seeking refuge from Satan) in prayer: its legal status, its position, and its wording. You will learn why the Hanafi school considers it sunnah despite the Quranic imperative, where in the prayer it is recited, and how this affects the imam, muqtadi, and masbuq. We will also examine the disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on whether ta'awwudh follows recitation or thana'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three discussions
The passage is structured around three questions: legal status (sunnah or wajib?), position (before recitation or after thana'?), and wording (which formula is preferred?). Follow the explanation as it addresses each in order.
2
Analyse the proof for sunnah status
The Quranic verse uses an imperative (fasta'idh), which normally indicates obligation. However, the consensus (ijma) of the salaf that ta'awwudh is sunnah overrides the apparent imperative. This is a Hanafi usul principle: amr is for obligation unless there is a contrary indicator.
The view of Sufyan al-Thawri and 'Ata' (wajib) is rejected due to ijma.
3
Understand the position dispute
The key phrase 'idha qara'ta al-Quran' is interpreted by the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) as 'when you intend to recite', not 'after you have recited'. This places ta'awwudh before recitation. Abu Yusuf argues it follows thana' because both are supplications. The text sides with the two due to the direct link in the verse.
The Khawarij (some sect) held that ta'awwudh comes after recitation, but this is rejected.
4
Apply the ruling to congregational prayer
Since ta'awwudh follows recitation, only those who will actually recite Quran in prayer recite it. The imam recites it; the muqtadi does not because his recitation is borne by the imam. The masbuq recites it when making up missed rak'ahs because he recites for himself. In Eid prayer, ta'awwudh is delayed after the extra takbirs because recitation is delayed.
5
Note the preferred wording
The Quran uses 'fasta'idh', so saying 'Asta'idhu billah' matches the Qur'anic verb. However, narrations often use 'A'udhu billah', so both are acceptable, with 'Asta'idhu' being better for conformity.
The text says 'al-ula an yaqula asta'idhu billah' (it is better to say asta'idhu).

And he seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan due to His statement: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan.' Its meaning: when you intend to recite the Quran. And it is better that he says 'Asta'idhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' to agree with the Quran, and close to it is 'A'udhu billah'. Then ta'awwudh follows the recitation, not the thana', according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, due to what we recited, so the masbuq (latecomer) recites it, not the muqtadi (follower), and it is delayed after the takbirs of Eid, contrary to Abu Yusuf.

Translation: And he seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan... (then Urdu commentary): Explanation: Here are three discussions: (1) The legal status of ta'awwudh at the beginning of prayer. (2) The position of ta'awwudh in prayer. (3) The wording of ta'awwudh.

First discussion: According to us, ta'awwudh at the beginning of prayer is sunnah. The author of Fath al-Qadir and Sharh al-Nuqaya wrote that according to the general salaf, it is mustahab, and the majority of later scholars also agree. Imam Malik said that ta'awwudh should not be recited at the beginning of prayer. Sufyan al-Thawri and 'Ata' considered it obligatory. Their proof is the verse 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah', and the command form indicates obligation. But we say that the opinion of obligation is not acceptable because it contradicts consensus.

Imam Malik's proof is the hadith of Anas: 'I prayed behind the Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, and 'Umar; they used to begin recitation with al-Hamdu lillahi Rabbi l-'alamin.' This shows that they did not recite ta'awwudh or basmalah before that.

Our proof is the verse: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah.' Although the imperative form would necessitate obligation as 'Ata' and Thawri say, but because the predecessors have consensus that it is sunnah, our scholars consider it sunnah.

Second discussion: According to us, ta'awwudh is before recitation, and according to some others, it is after. We say that ta'awwudh is after recitation? Actually, they interpret the verse's apparent meaning as after recitation, but our response is that 'idha qara'ta' means 'when you intend to recite'. Then regarding whether ta'awwudh follows recitation or thana', our scholars differ. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), ta'awwudh follows recitation, not thana'; and according to Abu Yusuf, it follows thana'. So according to the two, whoever has recitation obligatory upon him will recite ta'awwudh; therefore the masbuq will recite it because he has to make up missed rak'ahs, but the muqtadi does not recite it. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, whoever recites thana' will also recite ta'awwudh. In Eid prayer, ta'awwudh is delayed after the takbirs because recitation is delayed. Abu Yusuf's proof is that ta'awwudh is of the same genus as thana' because both are supplications, so it follows thana'. The proof of the two is the verse: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah.'

Third discussion: It is better to say 'Asta'idhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' to match the Quranic wording, but most narrations have 'A'udhu billah...' so the author of Hidayah said it is close.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage comprehensively covers the ruling on ta'awwudh (seeking refuge from Satan) in prayer. The author presents three discussions: legal status, position, and wording. The passage type is a ruling with proof, including intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes. The author first states the basic ruling: ta'awwudh is to be recited after takbir, and it follows recitation not thana' according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The proof is the Quranic verse (al-Nahl 98) which uses the command 'fasta'idh', interpreted as when intending recitation. The status: it is sunnah, not wajib, due to consensus of the salaf that it is sunnah, despite the imperative form. This refutes the view of those like Sufyan al-Thawri who considered it wajib. Imam Malik's view that it is not recited is refuted by the hadith of Anas showing the Prophet and caliphs did not recite it aloud? Actually, Malik's proof is from Anas that they began with al-Hamd, but the Hanafis interpret that as meaning they did not recite ta'awwudh between thana' and Fatiha? The commentary clarifies that the Hanafi position is that ta'awwudh is recited silently before Fatiha. The position of ta'awwudh: it is recited before recitation (Fatiha), not after. Some (Khawarij?) held it after recitation, but the correct interpretation of 'idha qara'ta' is 'when you intend to recite'. Then the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say ta'awwudh follows recitation (i.e., it is recited only by one who will recite, so the masbuq recites it when making up rak'ahs, but the muqtadi does not because his recitation is borne by the imam). Abu Yusuf says ta'awwudh follows thana', so anyone who recites thana' (i.e., all including muqtadi) recites ta'awwudh. In Eid prayer, ta'awwudh is delayed after the extra takbirs because recitation is delayed. The preferred wording: 'Asta'idhu billah' matches the Quranic verb, but 'A'udhu billah' is also widespread. The passage thus provides a thorough treatment with proofs and differences.

Key Terms
تعوذ (ta'awwudh): Seeking refuge with Allah from Satan, recited at the beginning of recitation in prayer.
مسبوق (masbūq): A person who joins the congregation after the imam has already started, thereby missing some rak'ahs.
مقتدی (muqtadī): A person who follows the imam in congregational prayer from the beginning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ta'awwudh is an emphasized sunnah recited before the Fatiha by those who recite Quran in prayer; the muqtadi does not recite it, and it is delayed after takbirs in Eid prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Ta'awwudh: Sunnah, Not Wajib
Inter-madhhab dispute on ta'awwudh ruling with intra-Hanafi detail

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'awwudh, explain the proof from the Quran and ijma, and distinguish the Hanafi position from that of Imam Malik and Thawri/'Ata.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah even though the Quran uses an imperative, because the salaf's consensus overrides the literal command.

The act of seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) at the start of prayer is a point of ikhtilaf among scholars. While the Quran commands 'fasta'idh billah', the Hanafi school, relying on the consensus of the righteous predecessors, classifies it as sunnah. This lesson unpacks the proofs, the intra-Hanafi differences on timing, and the operative ruling for practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
Read the passage to extract the Hanafi ruling: ta'awwudh is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib. Note the primary proof: Quran 16:98 with the imperative, but overridden by ijma.
The imperative (fasta'idh) normally indicates obligation, but consensus (ijma) of the salaf lowers it to sunnah.
2
Contrast opposing views
Identify Imam Malik's position (no ta'awwudh at start) and Thawri/'Ata's position (wajib). List their proofs: Malik relies on the hadith of Anas; Thawri/'Ata rely on the literal imperative.
The hadith of Anas shows the Prophet began with alhamdulillah, but Hanafis interpret that as silent recitation.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain how the Hanafi school refutes each opponent: to Malik, the hadith does not negate silent recitation; to Thawri/'Ata, ijma overrides the imperative. Understand the principle: a zanni dalil (imperative) can be superseded by qat'i ijma.
This demonstrates the Hanafi hierarchy of proofs: ijma overrides a zanni dalal.
4
Unpack the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Study the difference between the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf. Sahibayn: ta'awwudh follows qira'ah, so only those obligated to recite (imam, latecomer) recite it. Abu Yusuf: ta'awwudh follows thana', so anyone who recites thana' also recites ta'awwudh.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn view: ta'awwudh before qira'ah, and the follower (muqtadi) does not recite it.

تشریح
امام مالک کی دلیل حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ کی روایت ہے حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ نے فرمایا صلیت خلف رسول الله وخلف ابي بكر وعمر كانوا يفتتحون القراة بالحمد لله رب العالمين اس روایت سے معلوم ہوا کہ اللہ کا رسول اور شیخین الحمد لله رب العالمین سے قرآت شروع کرتے تھے اور اس سے پہلے اعوذ باللہ اور بسم اللہ ہیں پڑھتے تھے۔ ہماری دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَإِذَا قَرَأْتَ القُران فاستعذ باللہ ہے آیت میں استعذ صیغہ امر کا تقاضا اگر چہ یہ ہے کہ تعویذ والی واجب ہو جیسا کہ عطاء اور ثوری کہتے ہیں مگر چونکہ اسلاف نے اس کے سنت ہونے پر اجماع کیا ہے اس لئے ہمارے علما تعوذ کے مسنون ہونے کے قائل ہیں۔
دوسری بحث کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک تعوذ قرآت قرآن سے پہلے ہے اور اصحاب خواہر کے نزدیک قرآت کے بعد ہے (۲) ہم استعاذہ قرآت کے بعد ہے۔ اصحاب خواہر ظاہر آیت سے استدلال کرتے ہیں اور آیت کا ظاہر یہ ہے کہ جب تو قرآت قرآن کر چکے تو استعاذہ کر اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ لیکن ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ اذا قرأت کے معنی ہیں اذا اردت قرأت القرآن فاستعذ بالله یعنی جب قرآت قرآن کا ارادہ ہو تو استعاذہ کر رہی یہ بات کہ تعوذ قرآت کے تابع ہے یا ثناء کے تو اس بارے میں ہمارے علماء کا اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ طرفین کے نزدیک تعوذ قرات کے تابع ہے نہ کہ ثناء کے اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک شاہ کے تابع ہے پس طرفین کے نزدیک جس شخص پر قرآت وبسر بهـ کیونکہ اس پر قرآت واجب نہیں۔ واجب ہوگی وہ تعوذ کرے گا حتی کہ مسبوق تعوذ کرے گا کیونکہ اس پر فوت شد در کعات میں قرآت کرنا واجب ہے البتہ مقتدی تعوذ نہ کرے بالتسمية امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جو ثا، پڑھے گاوہ تعوذ بھی کرے گا۔ اور عیدین کی نماز میں تعو عید کی تکبیروں سے مؤخر کرے گا کیونکہ عیدین کی پہلی رکعت میں قرآت تکبیرات عید سے مؤخر ہوتی ہے اور
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تعوذ ثناء کی جنس سے ہے کیونکہ جس طرح ثا، دعا ہے اسی طرح تعوذ بھی ایک دعا ہے اور شئی کا تابع شئی کے بعد ہوتا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ تو ثناء کا تابع ہے نہ کہ قرآت کا اور طرفین کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَإِذَا قَرَأْتَ الْقُرْآنَ فَاسْتَعِدُ باللہ ہے۔
تیسری بحث کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ تعوذ کے الفاظ میں اولی یہ ہے کہ استعيذ باللہ من الشیطان الرجیم کہے تا کہ باری تعالے کے لائے نگراں
قول فاستعذ باللہ کے موافق ہو جائے۔ لیکن اکثر اخبار و آثار میں اعوذبالله من الشيطان الرجیم وارد ہے اس وجہ سے صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ استعید کے قریب اعوذ باللہ بھی ہے اور مذہب مختار بھی یہی ہے اور اس پر فتوی دیا جائے۔ اور بعض حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ حضور نے اعوذ باللہ العظیم السميع العليم من الشيطان الرجيم پڑھا ہے لہذا اس کو اختیار کیا جائے۔
Chapter on Description of Prayer. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary volume 2. According to the general body of the Salaf, it is mustahabb, and the majority of the later scholars also hold this view. Imam Malik said: Ta'awwudh should not be recited at the beginning of prayer. Sufyan al-Thawri and 'Ata hold the obligation of ta'awwudh. The proof of Sufyan al-Thawri and 'Ata is that Allah Most High said: 'When you recite the Quran...' [not acceptable]. 'Then seek refuge in Allah.' And the word of command indicates obligation. But we say that the statement of obligation is contrary to consensus. Translation: Commentary: The proof of Imam Malik is the narration of Anas (may Allah be pleased with him): 'I prayed behind the Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, and 'Umar, and they used to begin the recitation with Alhamdulillahi rabbil 'alamin.' From this narration it is known that the Messenger of Allah and the two shaykhs would begin recitation with Alhamdulillah and would not recite audhu billah and bismillah before it. Our proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'So when you recite the Qur'an, seek refuge in Allah.' In the verse, the word is in the imperative form, which would require that ta'awwudh be obligatory, as 'Ata and Thawri say, but because the salaf have consensus that it is sunnah, our scholars say ta'awwudh is sunnah. The conclusion of the second discussion is that according to us, ta'awwudh is before the recitation of the Qur'an, and according to the Khawarij, it is after the recitation. The Khawarij derive from the apparent meaning of the verse, and the apparent meaning of the verse is: 'When you have finished reciting the Qur'an, then seek refuge.' But our response is that the meaning of 'idha qara'ta' is 'when you intend to recite the Qur'an, then seek refuge.' As for whether ta'awwudh is subordinate to recitation or to praise, our scholars have a difference. According to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), ta'awwudh is subordinate to recitation, not to praise, and according to Abu Yusuf, it is subordinate to praise. According to the two sides, the person upon whom recitation is obligatory will recite ta'awwudh, so even a latecomer will recite ta'awwudh because recitation of missed rak'ats is obligatory upon him. However, the follower (muqtadi) does not recite ta'awwudh. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, whoever recites praise will also recite ta'awwudh. And in the prayer of the two Eids, ta'awwudh will be delayed after the takbirs because in the first rak'ah of Eid, recitation comes after the takbirs. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that ta'awwudh is of the same genre as praise, because just as praise is a supplication, ta'awwudh is also a supplication, and a thing follows that which is after it. So it is established that ta'awwudh follows praise, not recitation. The proof of the two sides is the verse of Allah Most High: 'So when you recite the Qur'an, seek refuge in Allah.' The conclusion of the third discussion is that regarding the wording of ta'awwudh, the best is to say 'asta'idhu billahi min al-shaytani al-rajim' so that it conforms to the Quranic verse 'fasta'idh billah'. But most reports and traditions have 'a'udhu billahi min al-shaytani al-rajim', therefore the author of al-Hidayah said that 'a'udhu billah' is also close to the command, and this is the chosen school, and fatwa is given accordingly. And some say that the Prophet recited 'a'udhu billahi al-'azimi al-sami'i al-'alimi min al-shaytani al-rajim', so this may be adopted.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the ruling on ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) in prayer. It begins by stating the Hanafi position: ta'awwudh is mustahabb/sunnah, not wajib, based on the consensus of the salaf. It then presents the opposing views: Imam Malik says ta'awwudh is not recited at all at the start of prayer; Sufyan al-Thawri and 'Ata say it is wajib. The Hanafi response to Malik is based on the hadith of Anas, which shows the Prophet and the caliphs began with alhamdulillah, but this only indicates they did not recite it loudly, not that they omitted it. The Hanafi response to Thawri and 'Ata is that although the Quranic verse uses an imperative, the salaf's consensus overrides it, making it sunnah. The passage then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute about the timing of ta'awwudh: whether it is recited before qira'ah (the majority view, including Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) or after (the Khawarij). The Hanafi majority interprets 'idha qara'ta' as 'when you intend to recite'. Another intra-Hanafi dispute concerns whether ta'awwudh follows qira'ah or thana' (praise). According to the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it follows qira'ah, so only those obligated to recite (e.g., the imam and latecomer) recite it, while the follower (muqtadi) does not. Abu Yusuf holds it follows thana', so anyone who recites thana' also recites ta'awwudh. The passage also discusses the wording: the preferred form is 'asta'idhu billahi min al-shaytani al-rajim' to match the Quran, but the hadith use 'a'udhu billahi...' and this is the chosen school for fatwa. Some recommend the longer form including 'al-'azim al-sami' al-'alim'. The teacher should emphasize that the Hanafi school prioritizes ijma over the literal imperative, and that the practice of the Prophet (silently) supports the sunnah ruling.

Key Terms
تعوذ (ta'awwudh): Seeking refuge in Allah from the accursed devil, recited at the start of prayer.
استعاذة (isti'adha): Another term for ta'awwudh, used synonymously.
قرآت (qira'ah): Recitation of the Quran in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who among the following does NOT recite ta'awwudh in prayer?
A) The imam
B) The latecomer (masbuq)
C) The follower (muqtadi)
D) The one praying alone

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules ta'awwudh as sunnah, not wajib, due to the overriding consensus of the salaf, despite the imperative in the Quran.

Salah — Prayer

The Status of Basmalah: Quranic Verse or Surah Separator?
Explains the status of basmalah as part of the Quran and its recitation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the basmalah as a Quranic verse independent of surahs, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Maliki views, including the practical implications for prayer.

Core Idea
Basmalah is part of the Quran but not part of any surah — it is a divider, not a component.

The phrase 'بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم' is recited at the start of nearly every Quranic surah. But is it an integral part of the surah, a separate verse, or not Quranic at all? The Hanafi school takes a unique position that directly affects how it is recited in prayer. This lesson unpacks those rulings through the lens of inter-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is the subject of dispute? Here, it is the status of the basmalah that appears between surahs in the Quran. Is it part of the Quran? If so, is it part of any specific surah or an independent verse?
The basmalah in Surah al-Naml (27:30) is universally agreed to be Quranic.
2
State the Hanafi position
According to the Hanafi school, the basmalah between surahs is part of the Quran but it is not part of any surah; it was revealed to separate the surahs. It is recited silently in prayer.
This is the position of the majority of the Hanafi imams and is mufta bihi.
3
Identify the opposing schools and their views
Imam Malik holds that the basmalah between surahs is not part of the Quran at all (only the one in Surah al-Naml is). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it is part of Surah al-Fatiha, and concerning other surahs there are two narrations.
The Maliki view is the most restrictive; the Shafi'i view makes the basmalah integral to the Fatiha.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof relies on the consensus (ijma) of the Companions that the basmalah is included in the Quran, coupled with the practice of the Prophet and Companions who did not recite it as part of the surah and recited it silently. This shows it is a separator.
The absence of jahr (loud recitation) in authentic hadith supports silent recitation.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafis recite basmalah silently before every surah except between al-Fatiha and the next surah (according to Imam Muhammad, it is recited). Shafi'is recite it aloud in loud prayers and consider it part of the Fatiha, meaning they must recite it as a verse of the Fatiha.
This difference affects the validity of prayer according to each school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تمیہ
وقرأ بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم، هكذا نقل في المشاهير
ترجمہ اور بسم الله الرحمن الرحیم پڑھے۔ ایسا ہی مشہور حدیثوں میں مروی ہے۔
تشریح تسمیہ کے اندر چند باتوں میں کلام ہے
(۱) واضح ہو کہ سورہ نمل کی آیت و انه من سليمان وانه بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم میں بسم اللہ بالاتفاق قرآن کا جز ہے اور سورہ نمل کا بھی لیکن دوسورتوں کے درمیان جو بسم اللہ مذکور ہے اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ وہ قرآن کا جز ہے یا نہیں، پس ہمارے علماء احناف کے نزدیک قرآن کا جز ہے اور امام مالک قرآن کا جز ہونے کے قائل نہیں ہیں۔
(۲) ہم اللہ ہمارے نزدیک نہ فاتحہ کا جز ہے اور نہ کسی دوسری سورت کا بلکہ سورتوں کی درمیان فصل کرنے کے لئے نازل کی گئی ہے۔ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ بسم اللہ سورۂ فاتحہ کا جز ہے اور باقی سورتوں کا جز ہونے میں امام شافعی کے دو قول ہیں۔
(۳) بسم اللہ کے ساتھ جبر ہوگا یا سراس کی تفصیل اگلی سطور میں آ رہی ہے۔
Tasmiyah. And he recites bismillah al-rahman al-rahim. Thus it is narrated in the famous (hadith). Translation: And he recites bismillah al-rahman al-rahim. Thus it is narrated in well-known hadith. Commentary: There is discussion in several matters regarding tasmiyah: (1) It should be clear that in the verse of Surah al-Naml 'Innahu min Sulaymana wa innahu bismillahi al-rahmani al-rahim', basmalah is by consensus a part of the Quran and a part of Surah al-Naml. But regarding the basmalah that occurs between other surahs, there is disagreement whether it is part of the Quran. According to our Hanafi scholars, it is part of the Quran, and Imam Malik does not hold it to be part of the Quran. (2) According to us, basmalah is not a part of Surah al-Fatiha nor of any other surah, but rather it was revealed to separate between surahs. Imam al-Shafi'i said that basmalah is part of Surah al-Fatiha, and regarding it being part of other surahs, al-Shafi'i has two narrations. (3) Whether basmalah is recited aloud or silently will be detailed in the following lines.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage discusses the status and recitation of the basmalah (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) in prayer, specifically its position within the Quran and its recitation. The passage is a definition-ruling type, explaining the legal nature of basmalah. The Hanafi position is clearly stated: the basmalah is part of the Quran, but it is not a part of any surah, including Surah al-Fatiha; rather, it was revealed to separate the surahs. This differs from Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that basmalah is part of Surah al-Fatiha. Imam Malik holds that the basmalah between surahs is not part of the Quran at all. The passage also notes that the basmalah in Surah al-Naml is universally agreed to be part of the Quran. The ruling on its recitation in prayer is that it is recited silently (sirr), not aloud, and the details of this are deferred to later. The teacher should highlight the unique Hanafi view that basmalah serves as a separator between surahs, which affects its recitation in prayer: it is recited before every surah except the Fatiha? Actually, note: the text says 'our scholars' hold it is not part of any surah but was revealed for separation. In practice, Hanafis recite basmalah silently between surahs, but not between al-Fatiha and the following surah according to some? The text mentions a difference on that later. But the core here is its status.

Key Terms
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم (bismillahi al-rahmani al-rahim): The phrase 'In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful'; a verse of the Quran used as an introduction to surahs.
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The act of reciting the basmalah, often used to refer to the basmalah itself.
فاتحہ (al-Fatiha): The opening surah of the Quran, recited in every rak'ah of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of the basmalah (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) between surahs in the Quran?
A) It is part of the previous surah.
B) It is part of Surah al-Fatiha only.
C) It is part of the Quran, but not part of any surah; it was revealed to separate surahs.
D) It is not part of the Quran at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely maintains that the basmalah is a Quranic verse serving as a divider between surahs, which necessitates silent recitation in prayer and distinguishes it from other schools.

Reciting Ta'awwudh, Tasmiyah, and Amin: Silent or Aloud?
Debates whether ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin are recited aloud or silently

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on reciting ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin in prayer, and explain the evidence and the response to the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin are recited silently, based on the practice of the Prophet and the Companions.

When you pray behind a Hanafi imam, you will notice that he recites the basmalah, the ta'awwudh, and the amin silently. This is not a random practice but a ruling rooted in the sunnah. This lesson unpacks the evidence from Ibn Mas'ud and Anas ibn Malik, and shows how the Hanafi school refutes the Shafi'i argument for reciting basmalah aloud.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding the recitation of ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin in prayer.
The position is that all three are recited silently (sirr) by the imam in both loud and silent prayers.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that basmalah is recited aloud in prayers where recitation is loud (Jahri prayers).
The Shafi'i school bases this on a hadith that the Prophet recited basmalah aloud in prayer.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: a narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited basmalah aloud during prayer.
This is a direct report, but its authenticity and interpretation are contested.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school responds: the Shafi'i hadith is interpreted as the Prophet teaching others (not his regular practice), and the more authentic report from Anas confirms that the Prophet did not recite basmalah aloud.
The Hanafis also invoke the statement of Ibn Mas'ud that the imam should conceal four things, including these.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of this difference: Hanafi imams recite basmalah silently; Shafi'i imams recite it aloud in Jahri prayers.
This affects congregational prayer practice, especially in mixed-school settings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعوذ، تسمیہ ، آمین سرا کہی جائے یا جہرا اقوال فقہاء ودلائل
ويسربهما لقول ابن مسعود اربع يخفيهن الامام وذكر من جملتها التعوذ والتسمية وامين وقال الشافعي يجهر بالتسمية عند الجهر بالقراءة لماروى ان النبي عليه السلام جهر في صلوته بالتسمية قلنا هو محمول على التعليم لان انساً اخير انه عليه السلام كان لا يجهر بها ثم عن ابي حنيفة انه لاياتي بها فى اول كل ركعة كالتعوذ وعنه انه یاتى بها احتياطا وهو قولهما ولا يأتى بها بين السورة والفاتحة الاعند محمد فانه يأتى بها في صلوة المخافتة
Ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, amin: to be recited silently or aloud – statements of jurists and proofs. And he recites them silently due to the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Four things the imam should recite silently' and he mentioned among them ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin. Al-Shafi'i said: He recites tasmiyah aloud when reciting aloud, because it is narrated that the Prophet recited it aloud in his prayer. We say: This is interpreted as teaching, because Anas informed that he (peace be upon him) did not recite it aloud. Then from Abu Hanifa: that he does not bring it (basmalah) at the beginning of every rak'ah like ta'awwudh. And from him: that he brings it out of precaution, and that is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And he does not bring it between the surah and al-Fatiha except according to Muhammad, for he brings it in silent prayer.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether ta'awwudh, tasmiyah (basmalah), and amin are recited silently (sirr) or aloud (jahr) in prayer. The Hanafi position, based on a statement of Ibn Mas'ud, holds that all three are recited silently by the imam. The key evidence is Ibn Mas'ud's enumeration of four things the imam should conceal (recite silently), including these. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that basmalah should be recited aloud in prayers where recitation is loud, citing a narration that the Prophet did so. The Hanafi response is that the Prophet's action was for teaching purposes, and the more authentic narration from Anas confirms he did not recite it aloud. The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa has two narrations regarding bringing basmalah at the start of each rak'ah (one that he does not bring it, like ta'awwudh, and another that he brings it out of precaution, which is the view of the Sahibayn). Additionally, Muhammad holds that basmalah is brought between al-Fatiha and the surah in silent prayer. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that basmalah is recited silently, and it is recited at the beginning of each rak'ah before al-Fatiha, except between al-Fatiha and the surah where it is omitted according to the majority, but Muhammad includes it in silent prayer.

Key Terms
جہر (jahr): Recitation aloud, audible to others.
سر (sirr): Recitation silently, not audible to others.
آمین (amin): The word 'Amin' said after reciting al-Fatiha, meaning 'O Allah, respond'.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how should the imam recite ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin in prayer?
A) All three are recited aloud.
B) All three are recited silently.
C) Ta'awwudh and tasmiyah silently, amin aloud.
D) Only tasmiyah is recited aloud.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin are recited silently in prayer, based on the practice of the Prophet and the Companions, and this ruling is mufta bihi.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Recitation of Ta'awwudh and Tasmiyah Silently in Prayer
States Hanafi ruling on silent recitation of ta'awwudh and tasmiyah with proofs against Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on silent recitation of ta'awwudh and tasmiyah, identify the primary proofs, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
In Hanafi prayer, ta'awwudh and tasmiyah are always recited silently; jahr is for teaching only.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that the imam recites ta'awwudh and tasmiyah silently in prayer. We will study the primary proof from Ibn Mas'ud and the practice of the Prophet and the caliphs, and then analyze the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school prioritizes established practice over occasional exceptions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding the recitation of ta'awwudh and tasmiyah in prayer – specifically that both are recited silently by the imam.
This applies to all prayers, regardless of whether the recitation is jahr or sirr.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that tasmiyah should be recited aloud in prayers where recitation is aloud (jahr prayers).
The Shafi'i school considers tasmiyah part of Surah al-Fatiha and thus recited aloud in jahr prayers.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: hadith of Abu Huraira reciting tasmiyah aloud and claiming it resembles the Prophet's prayer, and hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet recited it aloud.
These are ahad hadith but considered authentic by Shafi'is.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the two Hanafi responses: first, that the jahr reported was for teaching purposes, not the general practice; second, that if jahr occurred early, it was abrogated by the verses calling for humility in supplication.
The hadith of Anas explicitly states that the Prophet did not recite tasmiyah aloud in his usual practice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
See the practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, tasmiyah is silent in all prayers; in the Shafi'i school, it is aloud in jahr prayers and silent in sirr prayers.
This affects how a follower prays behind imams of different schools.

ويسربهما لقول ابن مسعود اربع يخفيهن الامام وذكر من جملتها التعوذ والتسمية وامين وقال الشافعي يجهر بالتسمية عند الجهر بالقراءة لماروى ان النبي عليه السلام جهر في صلوته بالتسمية قلنا هو محمول على التعليم لان انساً اخير انه عليه السلام كان لا يجهر بها ثم عن ابي حنيفة انه لاياتي بها فى اول كل ركعة كالتعوذ وعنه انه یاتى بها احتياطا وهو قولهما ولا يأتى بها بين السورة والفاتحة الاعند محمد فانه يأتى بها في صلوة المخافتة
