تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ تسمیہ اور تعوذ میں سر کرے یعنی نماز کے اندر ان کو آہستہ پڑھے۔ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ جبری نماز میں بسم اللہ کو جہر کے ساتھ پڑھے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ نے روایت کیا کہ حضور 16 اپنی نماز
میں بسم اللہ کو باخبر پڑھتے تھے چنانچہ صیح ابن خزیمہ ابن حبان اور نسائی میں نعیم انجر سے روایت ہے کہ صلیت وراء ابی ھریر رضى الله تعالى عنه فقراء بسم الله الرحمان الرحيم ثم قراء بام القرآن حتى بلغ ولا الضالين فقال أمين ثم يقول اذا سلم والذي نفسي بيده انى لا شبهكم صلاة برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم (فتح القدير ) يعني نعيم المحميرت روایت ہے کہ میں نے حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کے پیچھے نماز پڑھی پس ابو ہریرہ نے بسم الله الرحمن الرحیم پڑھی پھرا القرآن یعنی سورۃ فاتحہ اچھی حتی کہ ولا الضالین پر پہنچے تو آمین کہی پھر سلام کے بعد کہا کہ اس ذات کی قسم جس کے قبضہ میں میری جانا ہے کہ میں نماز میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زیادہ مشابہ ہوں۔ یہ حدیث اس بات پر دلالت کرتی ہے کہ حضرت ابو ہریرہ نے بسم اللہ سورۂ فانو اور آمین تینوں میں جہر کیا کیونکہ ابو ہریرہ اگر جہر نہ فرماتے تو نعیم اشمیر کو کس طرح علم ہوتا اور چونکہ ابو ہریرہ نے کہا کہ میری نماز رسول اللہ کی نماز کے مشابہت رکھتی ہے اس سے معلم ہوا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بھی ان چیزوں کو بالحجر پڑھا ہے۔
اور دار قطنی نے سعید بن جبیر سے روایت کی ، عن ابن عباس رضى الله تعالى عنهما قال كان النبي يجهر في الصلاة ببسم الله الرحمان الرحيم ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما نے کہا کہ حضور نماز میں بسم اللہ بالجبر پڑھتے ہے۔
ہماری دلیل ابن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کا قول ہے کہ چار چیزیں ایسی ہیں جن کو امام آہستہ پڑھے وہ چار چیزیں یہ ہیں تعوذ تسمیر تحمید ( ربنا لک الحمد ) آمین۔ صاحب شرح نقایہ نے بجائے تحمید کے شاہ ذکر کیا ہے کیونکہ امام محمد نے آثار میں روایت کی ہے عن ابي حنيفة عن حماد عن ابراهيم النخعى انه قال اربع يخفيهن الامام التعوذ وبسم الله الرحمان الرحیم وسبحانك اللهم وبحمدک و امین (شرح نتای)
بسم اللہ کو بالاسر پڑھنے پر حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کا قول بھی معتدل ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے صلیت خلف رسول اللہ صلی ا
الله عليه وسلم وخلف ابي بكر و عمر وعثمان فلم اسمع احدا منهم يقرا بسم الله الرحمن الرحیم اور مسلم کی ایک روایت میں ہے فلم اسمح احدا منهم يجهرون ببسم الله الرحمن الرحیم ۔ حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پیچھے اور ابوبکر عمر اور عثمان کے پیچھے نماز پڑھی پس میں نے ان میں سے کسی کو بسم اللہ کے ساتھ جہر کرتے نہیں سنا۔ حضرت امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ روایات بالحجر کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کبھی کبھی لوگوں کی تعلیم کے واسطے بسم اللہ کے ساتھ جم فرمایا ہے ورنہ آپ کی عام عادت بسم اللہ کے ساتھ جبر کرنے کی نہ تھی چنانچہ حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ نے خبر دی کہ آنحضر تا بسم اللہ نے نماز کے اندر بالحجر نہیں پڑھتے تھے دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ ابتداء اسلام میں آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم بسم اللہ کے ساتھ جہر کرتے تھے لیکن
ادْعُوا رَبَّكُمْ تَضَرُّعًا و خُفیہ کے ذریعہ جبر منسوخ ہو گیا۔ صاحب شرح نقایہ ما علی قاری نے نسخ کی تفصیل اس طرح بیان کی ہے: عن سعيد بن جبيرانه قال كان المشركون يحضرون المسجد واذا قرأ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قالو اهذا محمد يذكر رحمن اليمامة يعنون مسيلمة الكذاب فامران يحافت بسبم الله الرحمن الرحيم ونزلت ولاتجهرُ بصلوتك ولا تخافت بها (رواه ابوداؤد)
And he recites them silently due to the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Four things the Imam conceals' and he mentioned among them ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin. Al-Shafi'i said: 'He recites tasmiyah aloud when reciting aloud' because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited tasmiyah aloud in his prayer. We say: this is interpreted as teaching because Anas informed that he (peace be upon him) did not recite it aloud. Then from Abu Hanifa: he does not bring it at the beginning of every rak'ah like ta'awwudh; and from him also that he brings it as a precaution – that is the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And he does not bring it between Surah al-Fatiha and another surah except according to Muhammad, for he brings it in silent prayer.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute concerning the recitation of ta'awwudh (اعوذ بالله) and tasmiyah (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) in prayer – specifically whether they are recited aloud (jahr) or silently (sirr). The author presents the Hanafi ruling first: both ta'awwudh and tasmiyah are recited silently by the imam. This is based on the statement of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that four things are to be concealed by the imam, including ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin. The Hanafi proof is also supported by the hadith of Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) that he prayed behind the Prophet, Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman and did not hear any of them recite tasmiyah aloud. Al-Shafi'i argues that tasmiyah should be recited aloud in prayers where recitation is aloud, citing hadiths where the Prophet recited tasmiyah aloud and where Abu Huraira recited it aloud and claimed his prayer resembled the Prophet's. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, those instances of jahr were for teaching purposes, as the Prophet's general practice was silence – Anas explicitly stated that the Prophet did not recite tasmiyah aloud. Second, if jahr occurred early in Islam, it was later abrogated by the verse 'Call upon your Lord in humility and privately' (al-A'raf 55) and by the revelation 'And do not recite aloud in your prayer nor silently' (al-Isra 110), as explained by Sa'id ibn Jubayr. Within the Hanafi school, there is an intra-madhhab difference: Abu Hanifa has two narrations – one that tasmiyah is not recited at the beginning of each rak'ah (like ta'awwudh) and another that it is recited as a precaution. The latter is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). Additionally, Muhammad holds that tasmiyah is recited between Fatiha and another surah in silent prayers. These differences affect the practical application of the prayer. The passage also clarifies that tasmiyah is part of the Quran according to the Hanafis, but not part of Surah al-Fatiha itself – rather it is a separator between surahs. This contrasts with the Shafi'i view that it is part of Fatiha. The chapter thus provides a comprehensive treatment of the ruling with all relevant proofs.

Key Terms
تعوذ (ta'awwudh): The phrase 'أعوذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم' recited at the beginning of prayer before recitation.
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The phrase 'بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم' recited before Surah al-Fatiha.
جہر (jahr): Audible recitation that can be heard by others.
سر (sirr): Silent recitation, audible only to oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting tasmiyah (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) in prayer?
A) It is recited aloud in all prayers.
B) It is recited silently in all prayers.
C) It is recited aloud only in jahr prayers.
D) It is not recited at all.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi prayer, ta'awwudh and tasmiyah are always recited silently; any hadith suggesting otherwise is interpreted as teaching or abrogated.

Jahr vs Ikhfa of Bismillah: The Hanafi Position
Dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on reciting Bismillah aloud or silently.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on reciting Bismillah aloud or silently in salah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
The Prophet's consistent practice was silent recitation of Bismillah; loud recitation was occasional and later abrogated.

The recitation of 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' in prayer is a point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. This lesson examines the proofs each school presents and the Hanafi response, clarifying why the Hanafi school maintains that the imam recites Bismillah silently in all prayers. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh textual evidence, distinguish between regular practice and occasional teaching actions, and appreciate the role of abrogation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act and positions
Recognize that the dispute is about whether the imam recites 'Bismillah' aloud (jahr) or silently (ikhfa') during prayer. The Hanafi school holds ikhfa'; the Shafi'i school holds jahr.
2
Examine Shafi'i proofs
Review the hadiths: Abu Hurairah recited Bismillah aloud and claimed his prayer resembled the Prophet's; Ibn Abbas reported that the Prophet recited it aloud. These are the primary Shafi'i evidences.
3
Analyze Hanafi proofs
Study the Hanafi evidences: (1) The statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (via Ibn Mas'ud) listing Bismillah among four things the imam recites quietly; (2) The hadith of Anas that he did not hear the Prophet or the caliphs recite it aloud.
These are considered stronger due to multiple corroborations and the absence of contrary reported practice.
4
Understand Hanafi responses to Shafi'i proofs
Learn two Hanafi responses: (a) The Prophet's loud recitation was occasional for teaching, not his regular practice; (b) Any initial loud recitation was abrogated by the verse 'Call upon your Lord humbly and secretly' and by the incident of polytheists mocking 'Rahman of Yamama', after which the Prophet recited Bismillah quietly.
5
Assess the thamarah al-khilaf
Realize the practical consequence: In Hanafi congregations, the congregation does not hear 'Bismillah'; in Shafi'i congregations, they hear it. This affects the follower's awareness but not the validity of the prayer.

اشرف الهداية شرح اردو هداية جلد ثانى
باب سنته الصلوة
اشرف الهدای شرح اردو بدایت جلد
میں بسم اللہ کو باخبر پڑھتے تھے چنانچہ صحیح ابن خزیمہ ابن حبان اور نسائی میں نعیم مجمر سے روایت ہے کہ صلیت وراء ابی ھریرة رضى الله تعالى عنه فقرأ بسم الله الرحمان الرحيم ثم قرأ بأم القرآن حتى بلغ ولا الضالين فقال أمين ثم يقول اذا سلم والذي نفسي بيده انى لا شبهكم صلاة برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم (فتح القدير) يعني نعیم المجمر روایت ہے کہ میں نے حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کے پیچھے نماز پڑھی پس ابو ہریرہ نے بسم الله الرحمن الرحیم پڑھی پھر أم القرآن یعنی سورۃ فاتحہ پڑھی حتی کہ ولا الضالین پر پہنچے تو آمین کہی پھر سلام کے بعد کہا کہ اس ذات کی قسم جس کے قبضہ میں میری جان ہے کہ میں نماز میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زیادہ مشابہ ہوں۔ یہ حدیث اس بات پر دلالت کرتی ہے کہ حضرت ابو ہریرہ نے بسم اللہ سورۂ فاتحہ اور آمین تینوں میں جہر کیا کیونکہ ابو ہریرہ اگر جہر نہ فرماتے تو نعیم مجمر کو کس طرح علم ہوتا اور چونکہ ابو ہریرہ نے کہا کہ میری نماز رسول اللہ کی نماز کے مشابہت رکھتی ہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بھی ان چیزوں کو بالجہر پڑھا ہے۔
اور دار قطنی نے سعید بن جبیر سے روایت کی، عن ابن عباس رضى الله تعالى عنهما قال كان النبي يجهر في الصلاة ببسم الله الرحمان الرحيم ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما نے کہا کہ حضور نماز میں بسم اللہ بالجہر پڑھتے تھے۔
ہماری دلیل ابن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کا قول ہے کہ چار چیزیں ایسی ہیں جن کو امام آہستہ پڑھے وہ چار چیزیں یہ ہیں تعوذ تسمیہ تحمید (ربنا لك الحمد) آمین۔ صاحب شرح نقایہ نے بجائے تحمید کے سجدہ ذکر کیا ہے کیونکہ امام محمد نے آثار میں روایت کی ہے عن ابي حنيفة عن حماد عن ابراهيم النخعى انه قال اربع يخفيهن الامام التعوذ وبسم الله الرحمان الرحیم وسبحانك اللهم وبحمدك و آمین (شرح نقایہ)
بسم اللہ کو بالاسر پڑھنے پر حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کا قول بھی معتدل ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے صلیت خلف رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم وخلف ابي بكر و عمر و عثمان فلم اسمع احدا منهم يقرأ بسم الله الرحمن الرحیم اور مسلم کی ایک روایت میں ہے فلم اسمع احدا منهم يجهرون ببسم الله الرحمن الرحیم۔ حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پیچھے اور ابوبکر عمر اور عثمان کے پیچھے نماز پڑھی پس میں نے ان میں سے کسی کو بسم اللہ کے ساتھ جہر کرتے نہیں سنا۔ حضرت امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ روایات بالجہر کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کبھی کبھی لوگوں کی تعلیم کے واسطے بسم اللہ کے ساتھ جہر فرمایا ہے ورنہ آپ کی عام عادت بسم اللہ کے ساتھ جہر کرنے کی نہ تھی چنانچہ حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ نے خبر دی کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم بسم اللہ سے نماز کے اندر بالجہر نہیں پڑھتے تھے دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ ابتداء اسلام میں آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم بسم اللہ کے ساتھ جہر کرتے تھے لیکن ادْعُوا رَبَّكُمْ تَضَرُّعًا و خُفْيَةً کے ذریعہ جہر منسوخ ہو گیا۔ صاحب شرح نقایہ ملاعلی قاری نے نسخ کی تفصیل اس طرح بیان کی ہے: عن سعيد بن جبير انه قال كان المشركون يحضرون المسجد واذا قرأ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قالوا هذا محمد يذكر رحمن اليمامة يعنون مسيلمة الكذاب فامر باخفاء بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم ونزلت ولاتجهر بصلاتك ولا تخافت بها (رواه ابوداؤد)
سعید بن جبیر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے مروی ہے کہ فرمایا کہ مشرکین مکہ مسجد حرام میں حاضر ہوتے تھے اور جب آنحضرت قرآت کرتے تو کہتے کہ یہ محمد ہیں یمامہ کے رحمن یعنی مسیلمہ کذاب کا ذکر کرتے ہیں پس آپ کو حکم دیا گیا کہ بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم کے ساتھ اخفاء کریں اور ولاتجهر بصلاتك آیت نازل ہوئی۔ اس واقعہ سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ بسم اللہ اور قرآت قرآن میں جہر فرماتے تھے لیکن اس واقعہ کے بعد جہر کا حکم منسوخ ہو گیا۔ اور ابو داؤد کی ایک روایت میں ہے فخفض النبی بسم الله الرحمن الرحیم یعنی اس واقعہ کے بعد اللہ کے پاک نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بسم اللہ کو پست آواز کے ساتھ پڑھا یہ بھی جہر کے منسوخ ہونے پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔
علامہ ابن الہمام نے نعیم مجمر کی روایت کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ ممکن ہے ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کے اخفاء کے باوجود نعیم مجمر نے سن لیا ہو کیونکہ اگر مقتدی امام سے قریب ہو اور امام نے اخفاء میں مبالغہ نہ کیا ہو تو بھی سنا تحقیق ہو سکتا ہے۔
Chapter on the Description of Prayer. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya Volume Two. Chapter on its Sunnahs. They used to recite Bismillah aloud, as in Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah, Ibn Hibban and Nasa'i from Nu'aym al-Mujmir: He prayed behind Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him), who recited 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim', then recited Umm al-Quran until he reached 'wa la al-dalleen', then said 'Ameen', then after the salam said: 'By Him in Whose hand is my soul, I am the most similar of you in prayer to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' (Fath al-Qadir). Meaning Nu'aym al-Mujmir narrates: I prayed behind Abu Hurairah, and he recited Bismillah, then Surah al-Fatihah until 'wa la al-dalleen', then said Ameen, then after salam said that his prayer resembles the Prophet's. This hadith indicates that Abu Hurairah recited Bismillah, al-Fatihah, and Ameen aloud, because if he had not done so, Nu'aym would not have known. And since Abu Hurairah said his prayer resembles the Prophet's, it is known that the Prophet also recited these aloud. And al-Daraqutni narrated from Sa'id ibn Jubayr from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) that the Prophet used to recite Bismillah aloud in prayer. Our evidence is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Four things the imam recites quietly: al-Ta'awwudh, al-Tasmiyah, al-Tahmid (Rabbana lakal hamd), and Ameen.' The author of Sharh al-Niqayah mentioned 'sajdah' instead of 'tahmid' because Imam Muhammad narrated in al-Athar from Abu Hanifah from Hammad from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that he said: 'Four things the imam recites quietly: al-Ta'awwudh, Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim, Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika, and Ameen.' (Sharh al-Niqayah). The statement of Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) is also evidence for reciting Bismillah quietly: He said: 'I prayed behind the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and behind Abu Bakr, Umar and Uthman; I did not hear any of them recite Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim.' In a narration of Muslim: 'I did not hear any of them recite Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim aloud.' The response to the narrations presented by Imam al-Shafi'i about loud recitation is that the Prophet sometimes recited it aloud to teach people; otherwise, his usual practice was not to recite it aloud. Indeed, Anas informed that the Prophet did not recite Bismillah aloud in prayer. The second response is that in early Islam, the Prophet used to recite it aloud, but then loud recitation was abrogated by the verse 'Call upon your Lord humbly and secretly' (7:55). The author of Sharh al-Niqayah, Mulla Ali al-Qari, explained the abrogation in detail: From Sa'id ibn Jubayr: The polytheists would attend the mosque, and when the Messenger of Allah recited, they said: 'This is Muhammad mentioning the Rahman of Yamama', meaning Musaylimah the liar. So he was commanded to recite Bismillah quietly, and the verse 'And do not recite aloud in your prayer nor too quietly' (17:110) was revealed. (Abu Dawud). It is narrated from Sa'id ibn Jubayr that the polytheists of Mecca would attend the Masjid al-Haram, and when the Prophet recited, they said: 'This is Muhammad mentioning the Rahman of Yamama, meaning Musaylimah the liar.' So he was commanded to conceal Bismillah, and the verse 'And do not recite aloud in your prayer nor too quietly' was revealed. From this incident, it is known that the Prophet used to recite Bismillah and the Quran aloud, but after this, the command for loud recitation was abrogated. In a narration of Abu Dawud: 'The Prophet lowered (his voice) with Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim', meaning after this incident, the Prophet recited Bismillah quietly. This also indicates the abrogation of loud recitation. Ibn al-Humam responded to the narration of Nu'aym al-Mujmir by saying that it is possible that despite Abu Hurairah's quiet recitation, Nu'aym heard it, because if the follower is close to the imam and the imam did not exaggerate in quietness, then hearing can occur.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute regarding the recitation of 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' in prayer: whether the imam recites it aloud (jahr) or silently (ikhfa'). The Shafi'i school holds that it is recited aloud, citing hadiths from Abu Hurairah and Ibn Abbas. The Hanafi school holds that it is recited silently, relying on the statement of Ibn Mas'ud (who listed Tasmiyah among four things the imam recites quietly) and the hadith of Anas, who explicitly stated that he did not hear the Prophet or the Rightly Guided Caliphs recite it aloud. The Hanafi commentators address the Shafi'i proofs with two responses: first, the occasional loud recitation by the Prophet was for teaching purposes, not his regular practice; second, any initial loud recitation was abrogated by the verses commanding humility and by the incident of the polytheists' mockery, after which the Prophet consistently recited quietly. The Hanafi authority Ibn al-Humam further explains that the hadith of Nu'aym may not prove loud recitation, as close proximity could allow hearing even a quiet recitation. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the imam recites Bismillah silently in both silent and loud prayers.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation by the imam that is audible to the congregation.
إخفاء (ikhfa'): Silent or low-voice recitation, only audible to the reciter or those very close.
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم (Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim): The Basmalah, recited before al-Fatihah in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how does the imam recite 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' in prayer?
A) Loudly in all prayers
B) Silently in all prayers
C) Loudly in loud prayers and silently in silent prayers
D) Only recited in the first rak'ah silently

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that 'Bismillah' is recited silently in prayer, based on the consistent practice of the Prophet and the Sahaba, with loud recitation being occasional and later abrogated.

Recitation of Bismillah in Every Rak'ah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Bismillah recitation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi narrations on reciting Bismillah in prayer and state the mufta bihi position, including the subsidiary ruling on reciting between al-Fatihah and the surah.

Core Idea
Precaution (ihtiyat) resolves an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf: recite Bismillah in every rak'ah.

A common question in practice is whether the Basmalah before al-Fatihah must be repeated in every rak'ah. Within the Hanafi school, there is an internal difference attributed to Imam Abu Hanifah himself. This lesson examines the two narrations, their proofs, and the preferred position that has become the mufta bihi, including a related subsidiary ruling on reciting between al-Fatihah and the surah.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the contested point: whether Bismillah is recited before al-Fatihah in every rak'ah or only once at the start of prayer.
The dispute is internal to the Hanafi school, not between madhhabs.
2
Identify the two narrations
List the two narrations from Abu Hanifah: (1) via Hasan ibn Ziyad: once suffices; (2) via Abu Yusuf: every rak'ah.
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) adopt the second view.
3
Analyze each proof
For each narration, extract the dalil: first argues Bismillah is not part of al-Fatihah and prayer is a single act; second argues precaution due to scholarly disagreement over whether it is part of al-Fatihah.
The second narration invokes ihtiyat to avoid differing with those who consider it part of al-Fatihah.
4
Understand the tarjih
Explain why the Sahibayn's view is preferred: it is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the precautionary position, avoiding potential deficiency.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah confirms this as the mufta bihi.
5
Apply the subsidiary ruling
Note the additional issue: whether Bismillah is recited between al-Fatihah and the surah. Imam Muhammad permits it in silent prayers but not in loud prayers.
This is a separate application of the same principle of caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رہی یہ بات کہ بسم اللہ ہر رکعت میں سورۃ فاتحہ سے پہلے پڑھے یا فقط پہلی رکعت میں اس بارے میں حضرت امام اعظم سے دو روایتیں ہیں۔ حسن بن زیاد کی روایت تو یہ ہے کہ بسم اللہ کو ہر رکعت میں نہ پڑھے بلکہ نماز کے شروع میں فقط ایک مرتبہ پڑھ لینا کافی ہے جیسا کہ تعوذ صرف پہلی رکعت میں پڑھنا کافی ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بسم اللہ سورہ فاتحہ کا جز نہیں ہے بلکہ افتتاح صلوۃ کے لئے پڑھی جاتی ہے اور صلوۃ واحد فعل واحد کے مانند ہے اور فعل واحد کے لئے ایک مرتبہ بسم اللہ پڑھنا کافی ہے لہذا صلوۃ واحدہ کے لئے بھی ایک مرتبہ بسم اللہ پڑھنا کافی ہو گیا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ سے دوسری روایت ابو یوسف کی ہے کہ ہر رکعت میں بسم اللہ پڑھے احتیاط اس میں ہے کیونکہ بسم اللہ کے فاتحہ کا جز ہونے میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے اور فاتحہ کا ہر رکعت میں پڑھنا ضروری ہے۔ لہذا بسم اللہ کا پڑھنا بھی ہر رکعت میں ضروری ہوگا۔ تا کہ اختلاف سے بچا جا سکے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہر رکعت میں بسم اللہ پڑھنا صاحبین کا قول ہے۔ پھر فرمایا کہ سورت فاتحہ اور سورت کے درمیان بسم اللہ نہ پڑھے البتہ امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ سری نماز میں بسم اللہ فاتحہ اور سورت کے درمیان پڑھ سکتا ہے لیکن جہری نماز میں نہ پڑھے۔
As for the issue of whether Bismillah is recited before Surah al-Fatihah in every rak'ah or only in the first rak'ah, there are two narrations from Imam al-A'zam (Abu Hanifah). The narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad is that he does not recite Bismillah in every rak'ah; rather, reciting it once at the beginning of the prayer is sufficient, just as reciting al-Ta'awwudh only in the first rak'ah is sufficient. Its proof is that Bismillah is not a part of Surah al-Fatihah; rather, it is recited for opening the prayer, and the prayer is like a single action, and for a single action, reciting Bismillah once is sufficient. Therefore, for a single prayer, reciting Bismillah once is sufficient. The second narration from Imam Abu Hanifah is from Abu Yusuf: that he recites Bismillah in every rak'ah. Caution requires this because there is disagreement among scholars whether Bismillah is part of al-Fatihah, and reciting al-Fatihah in every rak'ah is necessary. Therefore, reciting Bismillah will also be necessary in every rak'ah in order to avoid disagreement. The author of al-Hidayah says that reciting Bismillah in every rak'ah is the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Then he said: He should not recite Bismillah between al-Fatihah and the surah. However, Imam Muhammad says that in silent prayer, one may recite Bismillah between al-Fatihah and the surah, but in loud prayer, he should not recite it.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recitation of 'Bismillah' in prayer. The issue is whether Bismillah should be recited before Surah al-Fatihah in every rak'ah or only once at the beginning of the prayer. Imam Abu Hanifah has two narrations: one transmitted by Hasan ibn Ziyad, where Bismillah is recited only once, based on the reasoning that Bismillah is not part of al-Fatihah but is for opening the prayer, and the entire prayer is considered a single act, so a single Basmalah suffices — similar to Ta'awwudh. The other narration, transmitted by Abu Yusuf, holds that Bismillah should be recited in every rak'ah as a precautionary measure, because there is an ikhtilaf (disagreement) among scholars whether Bismillah is part of al-Fatihah, and since al-Fatihah is obligatory in every rak'ah, reciting Bismillah before it in every rak'ah avoids the dispute. The author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) states that reciting Bismillah in every rak'ah is the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), which is the relied-upon position. Additionally, there is a subsidiary issue: whether to recite Bismillah between al-Fatihah and the additional surah. Imam Muhammad allows it in silent prayers but not in loud prayers.

Key Terms
تعوذ (ta'awwudh): The phrase 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim', recited at the beginning of prayer.
احتیاط (ihtiyat): Legal precaution: adopting the more cautious ruling to avoid potential invalidity or disagreement.
جز (juz): Part or component; here, whether Bismillah is a part of Surah al-Fatihah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi Hanafi position on reciting Bismillah before Surah al-Fatihah in prayer?
A) Recited only in the first rak'ah
B) Recited in every rak'ah
C) Not recited at all
D) Recited only in silent prayers

Key Takeaway
Recite Bismillah before al-Fatihah in every rak'ah to follow the mufta bihi Hanafi position based on precaution.

Is Reciting al-Fatihah and an Additional Surah a Rukn? Hanafi vs Shafi'i and Maliki
Dispute on the ruling of reciting al-Fatihah and additional surah in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies reciting al-Fatihah and an additional surah as wajib (not rukn) and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
Reciting al-Fatihah is wajib, not rukn, because rukn requires definitive proof; ahad hadith cannot establish a rukn.

This passage addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: are the recitations of al-Fatihah and an additional surah integral pillars (arkaan) of prayer or merely obligatory elements (wajibat)? The Hanafi position, grounded in a distinction between certainty (qat') and probability (zann), holds that these acts are wajib, not rukn. This has practical implications: omission requires sajdah al-sahw rather than invalidating the prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: both reciting al-Fatihah and adding a surah are wajib, not rukn. Note the distinction between wajib and rukn in Hanafi fiqh.
Rukn is established by qat'i evidence (Quran or mutawatir sunnah); wajib by zanni evidence (ahad hadith).
2
Identify the opposing views
Recognize that al-Shafi'i considers al-Fatihah a rukn, and Malik considers both al-Fatihah and the additional surah as rukn.
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof
Examine the Quranic verse (73:20) and the Hanafi reasoning: the general command 'faqra'u ma tayassara' indicates any recitation suffices, so specific requirement from ahad hadith can only impose wujub.
The imperative indicates obligation, but the lack of specificity means the particular recitation of al-Fatihah is not an absolute pillar.
4
Compare the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical consequence: in Hanafi, omission of al-Fatihah requires sajdah al-sahw; in Shafi'i, it invalidates the prayer.
This difference arises from the epistemological weight assigned to the hadith.

ترجمہ پھر سورۂ فاتحہ پڑھے اور کوئی سورت یا تین آیات جس کسی سورت میں سے چاہے پس ہمارے نزدیک قرآت فاتحہ کا رکن ہونا متعین نہیں ہے۔ اور یہی اس کے ساتھ سورت ملانے کا ہے۔ سورۃ فاتحہ میں امام شافعی کا اور سورۃ فاتحہ اور سورت دونوں میں امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ نماز نہیں مگر فاتحہ کے ساتھ اور اس کے ساتھ سورت کے۔ اور امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ نماز نہیں مگر فاتحہ کے ساتھ۔
Then he recites Surah al-Fatihah and a surah or three verses from whichever surah he wishes. The recitation of al-Fatihah is not determined as a rukn according to us, nor is joining a surah with it. Contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding al-Fatihah (he considers it a rukn) and to Malik regarding both (he considers both rukn). For Malik, his proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no prayer except with al-Fatihah and a surah with it.' For al-Shafi'i, his proof is the saying of the Prophet: 'There is no prayer except with al-Fatihah.' For us (Hanafis), the proof is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran.' (73:20) And increasing upon it with a khabar wahid is not permissible, but it necessitates action, so we said both are wajib (obligatory). Translation: Then he recites Surah al-Fatihah and a surah or three verses from whichever surah he wishes. According to us, reciting al-Fatihah is not specified as a rukn, and similarly joining a surah to it. There is ikhtilaf from al-Shafi'i regarding al-Fatihah and from Malik regarding both (al-Fatihah and the surah). Malik's proof is that the Prophet said: 'There is no prayer except with al-Fatihah and a surah with it.' And al-Shafi'i's proof is that the Prophet said: 'There is no prayer except with al-Fatihah.'
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal status of reciting Surah al-Fatihah and an additional surah (or three verses) in prayer. The Hanafi school holds that reciting al-Fatihah is not a rukn (pillar) of prayer; rather, it is wajib (obligatory). Similarly, adding a surah after it is also wajib, not a rukn. This contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i, who considers reciting al-Fatihah a rukn (so missing it invalidates the prayer), and Imam Malik, who considers both al-Fatihah and an additional surah as rukn. The Hanafi proof is the general Quranic command: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' (73:20). This verse indicates that any Quranic recitation suffices for the obligation of qira'ah. The specific hadiths requiring al-Fatihah and a surah are ahad (solitary) reports; while they are not strong enough to make it a rukn (since rukn is established by definitive evidence), they are strong enough to impose an obligation (wujub). Hence, the Hanafis say both are wajib: if omitted, the prayer is valid but requires sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). The text then provides the proofs of the opposing schools: for Malik, a hadith requiring both al-Fatihah and a surah; for Shafi'i, a hadith requiring only al-Fatihah.

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): A pillar or integral part of an act of worship; omission invalidates the act (batil).
واجب (wajib): An obligatory element whose omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary hadith, transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Hanafi worshiper prays without reciting Surah al-Fatihah, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil)
B) The prayer is valid but requires sajdah al-sahw
C) The prayer is invalid only if fatihah is omitted intentionally
D) The prayer is valid and no compensation is needed

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, reciting al-Fatihah and an additional surah are wajib (obligatory) but not rukn (pillars), because rukn can only be established by definitive evidence, while the specific hadiths are ahad.

Salah — Prayer

Hanafi Fiqh: Quran Recitation in Prayer – Fard vs. Wajib
Inter-madhhab dispute on the amount of Quran recitation mandatory in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Quran recitation in prayer, distinguish between fard and wajib in this context, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i and Maliki proofs.

Core Idea
Any Quran recitation is fard; Fatihah and an additional surah are wajib, not rukn.

In this lesson, we examine a key inter-madhhab dispute: how much Quran recitation is obligatory in prayer? The Hanafi school distinguishes between fard (proven by definitive evidence) and wajib (proven by speculative evidence). The opposing schools of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik consider Surah al-Fatihah (and an additional surah) as integral components (rukn) that invalidate the prayer if omitted. Understanding this difference is crucial for correctly applying Hanafi fiqh in salah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two levels: reciting any Quran verse is fard (proven by Quran), while reciting Surah al-Fatihah and an additional surah are wajib (proven by ahad hadith).
Hanafi usul: fard requires qati evidence; wajib requires zanni evidence.
2
Identify the opposing positions
Imam Shafi'i holds that reciting Surah al-Fatihah is rukn (invalid without it). Imam Malik holds that both Fatihah and an additional surah are rukn.
For both, omission invalidates the prayer.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i relies on the hadith 'La salata illa bi-Fatihati al-kitab'. Maliki relies on 'La salata illa bi-Fatihati al-kitab wa suratin ma'aha' and other narrations.
These are ahad hadiths (zanni al-thubut).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: rukn must be proven by qati evidence (Quran or mutawatir). Ahad hadiths cannot establish rukn; they only establish wujub. Also, khabar wahid cannot add to the Quran (73:20).
Hence Fatihah and extra surah are wajib, not fard.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If a person recites only a short verse (e.g., 'Qul huwallahu ahad'), the prayer is valid in Hanafi (fard fulfilled) but requires sajdah al-sahw for missing wajib. In Shafi'i/Maliki, the prayer is invalid.
This difference affects daily practice, especially for those who follow Hanafi.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دو
دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول ہے کہ نماز نہیں ہے مگر سورۂ فاتحہ کے ساتھ ۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالٰی نے فرمایا کہ پڑھو جو آسان ہو قرآن میں سے۔ اور قرآن پر خبر واحد کے ساتھ زیادتی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ لیکن خبر واحد عمل واجب کرتی ہے پس ہم ان دونوں کے وجوب کے
قائل ہو گئے۔
تشریح علی کا اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ نماز کے اندر قرآت قرآن کی کتنی مقدار فرض اور رکن ہے؟ سو ہمارے علماء کا مذہب : ہے کہ مطلقا قرآت قرآن فرض ہے چنانچہ کسی ایک آیت کو پڑھ لیا تو رکن قرآت ادا ہو جائے گا۔ رہا سورۃ فاتحہ کا پڑھنا اور اس کے ساتھ سورت ملانا تو یہ دونوں ہمارے نزدیک واجبات میں سے ہیں۔
حضرت امام شافعی نے کہا کہ سورۃ فاتحہ کا پڑ ھنار کن ہے اور امام مالک فاتحہ اور سورت ملانا دونوں کو رکن کہتے ہیں۔ امام مالک کی دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول لا صلاة الابفاتحة الكتاب وسورة معها ہے یعنی بغیر فاتحہ اور سورت کے نماز نہیں ہوگی اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ شان فرض کی ہوتی ہے نہ کہ واجب کی۔ اس کے ہم معنی امام ترندگی نے ابوسعید خدری رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ سے روایت کی اب مفتاح الصلوة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم ولا صلاة لمن لم يقر أبالحمد لله وسورة في فريضة اور غیرھا یعنی نماز کی کنجی طہارت (وضو) ہے اور ماورا ، نماز کو حرام کرنے والا اللہ اکبر کہتا ہے اور اس کو حلال کرنے والا اسلام ہے جس شخص نے فرض یا غیر فرض میں الحمد للہ اور سورت نہیں پڑھی اس کی نماز نہیں ہوئی۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل حدیث رسول الله لا صلوۃ الا بفاتحة الکتاب ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فاقرء وا ما تيسر من القرآن ہے اس آیت سے اس طور پر استدلال ہوگا کہ من القرآن مطلق ہے ابد المطلق يجرى على اطلاقہ کے قاعدہ سے جس اونی مقدار پر قرآن ہونا صادق آئے اس کا پڑھنا فرض ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہی مقدار مامور بہ ہے اور چونکہ خارج نماز قرآت قرآن فرض نہیں ہے اس لئے نماز کے اندر فرض ہو نا متعین ہوگا۔ امام مالک اور امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں حضرات کی پیش کردہ روایات اخبار احاد سے ہیں اور اخبار احافظنی ہوتی ہیں اور اصول فقہ میں یہ بات مذکور ہے کہ رکن دلیل قطعی سے ثابت ہوتا ہے نہ کہ دلیل ظنی سے البتہ دلیل ظلنی عمل واجب کرتی ہے اس لئے ہمارے علماء نے کہا کہ یہ دونوں واجب ہیں اور چونکہ خبر واحد کے ذریعہ کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے ان احادیث سے کتاب اللہ (فاقرء و اماتيسر من القرآن ) پر زیادتی بھی نہیں ہوسکتی۔
Section on the description of prayer. Page 44. Ashraf al-Bidayah sharh Urdu Hidayah volume 2. The proof of the opponent (Imam Shafi'i) is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no prayer except with Surah al-Fatihah.' And our proof is that Allah the Exalted said: 'Recite what is easy of the Quran.' And it is not permissible to add to the Quran with a khabar wahid. But a khabar wahid necessitates action (wujub). So we adopted the obligation (wujub) of both (Fatihah and the additional surah). Explanation: There is disagreement about how much Quran recitation is fard and rukn in prayer. Our scholars' madhhab is that absolute Quran recitation is fard. So if one recites any one verse, the rukn of recitation is fulfilled. As for reciting Surah al-Fatihah and joining a surah with it, both are wajib in our view. Imam Shafi'i said that reciting Surah al-Fatihah is rukn, and Imam Malik said that both Fatihah and joining a surah are rukn. Imam Malik's proof is the saying of the Prophet: 'La salata illa bi-Fatihati al-kitabi wa suratin ma'aha' meaning there is no prayer without Fatihah and a surah. And it is apparent that this is the status of fard, not wajib. Similar to it, Imam Tirmidhi narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'The key to prayer is purification (wudu), its tahrim is takbir, its tahlil is salam, and there is no prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd (Fatihah) and a surah in an obligatory prayer or other than it.' Imam Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of the Messenger of Allah: 'La salata illa bi-Fatihati al-kitab.' And our proof is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Fa-qra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran.' The deduction from this verse is that 'min al-Quran' is general (mutlaq). According to the principle 'al-mutlaq yajri 'ala itlaqih', whatever amount Quran is applicable to, reciting it becomes fard because this amount is commanded. And since reciting Quran is not fard outside prayer, it becomes specifically fard within prayer. The response to Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i's proof is that the narrations they presented are ahad (solitary) narrations, and ahad narrations are zanni. And in usul al-fiqh, it is mentioned that a rukn is proven by definitive evidence (qati), not by speculative evidence (zanni). However, speculative evidence necessitates action (wujub). Therefore, our scholars said that both are wajib. And because it is not permissible to add to the Book of Allah via khabar wahid, these hadiths cannot add to the Book of Allah (Fa-qra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran).
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the obligation of Quran recitation in prayer. The text opens by stating the proof of the opponent (Imam Shafi'i) from the hadith 'La salata illa bi-Fatihati al-kitab' (No prayer except with the Fatihah of the Book). Then it presents the Hanafi proof from the Quranic verse 'Fa-qra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' (So recite what is easy of the Quran). The Hanafi argument is that the word 'ma tayassara' is general, so any amount that qualifies as Quran suffices for the fard. The principle 'al-mutlaq yajri 'ala itlaqih' (the absolute term runs according to its absoluteness) is applied. Therefore, reciting any verse fulfills the fard obligation. However, the recitation of Surah al-Fatihah and an additional surah is considered wajib (obligatory but not fard) because the evidence for them is from ahad hadiths, which are zanni (speculative) and cannot establish a rukn (which requires qati evidence). The response to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik is that their hadiths are ahad and thus only establish wujub, not fardiyyah. Additionally, khabar wahid cannot add to the Quran. Thus, the Hanafi position is that any Quran recitation is fard, while Surah al-Fatihah and an additional surah are wajib.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An obligation proven by definitive evidence (qati), such as the Quran or mutawatir sunnah. Here, any recitation of Quran is fard.
واجب (wajib): An obligation proven by speculative evidence (zanni), such as khabar wahid. Here, reciting Fatihah and an additional surah is wajib.
ركن (rukn): An integral part of an act of worship; omission invalidates the act. Hanafi: rukn must be proven by qati evidence.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary hadith transmitted by one or a few chains, considered zanni in proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is only required for the imam, not the muqtadi.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, any Quran recitation fulfills the fard, but reciting Surah al-Fatihah and an additional surah are wajib, established by zanni evidence.

The Ruling on Saying Amin for Imam and Muqtadi in Prayer
Dispute on whether the imam says Amin after Fatihah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that both the imam and muqtadi say 'Amin' aloud, and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument based on the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Both imam and muqtadi say 'Amin' aloud—the Hanafi position is directly supported by the hadith that the imam says it.

This lesson explores a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding the saying of 'Amin' after Surah al-Fatihah in audible prayers. While both schools agree that the muqtadi (follower) should say 'Amin', they differ on whether the imam says it. The Hanafi school, relying on explicit hadith and the response to the Maliki proof, adopts the position that both say it. By working through this lesson, you will understand the proofs on each side and the practical consequence of the difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding the imam and the muqtadi saying 'Amin' after reciting Surah al-Fatihah in audible prayers.
The Hanafi position is that both say it audibly.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Determine which school or narration opposes the Hanafi view and what they rule instead.
Imam Maliki holds that only the muqtadi says 'Amin'; a weak narration from Abu Hanifa also agrees.
3
Analyze the opponent's dalil
Examine the primary proof cited by the Maliki school—the hadith 'When the imam says wa la d-dallin, then say Amin' and the argument from division of roles.
The Maliki claim is that the hadith divides tasks: imam recites, muqtadi says Amin.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school rebuts the Maliki proof by citing the continuation of the same hadith and additional supporting narrations.
The key phrase is 'fa inna al-imama yaquluha'—for the imam says it.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of this disagreement in actual congregational prayer.
In Hanafi practice, the imam says 'Amin' aloud; in Maliki practice, the imam remains silent.

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ سورۃ فاتحہ کے ختم پر جب امام ولا الضالین کے تو امام اور مقتدی دونوں کو آمین کہنا چاہئے ۔ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ فقیہ مقتدی آمین کہے امام آمین نہ ہے۔
امام مالک کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے اذا قال الامام ولا الضالين فقولوا امین مسلم نے پوری حدیث اس طرح روایت کی ہے انما جعل الامام ليؤتم به فلا تختلفوا عليه فاذ اكبر فكبروا واذا قرأ فانصتواو اذا قال ولا الضالين فقولوا امين تن امام تو اس لئے بنایا گیا کہ اس کی اقتداء کی جائے سو تم اس سے اختلاف مت کرو پس جب وہ تکبیر کے تو تم تکبیر کہو اور جب وہ پڑھے تو تم خاموش رہو اور جب و ہ ولا الضالین کے تو تم آمین کہو۔ امام مالک نے اس حدیث سے اس طرح استدلال کیا ہے کہ حضور میں نے تقسیم فرمائی چنانچہ امام کے حصہ میں قرآت کا اتمام ہے اور مندی کے حصہ میں آمین ہے اور چونکہ تقسیم شرکت کے منافی ہے اس لئے آمین کہنے میں امام اور مقتدی دونوں شریک نہیں ہوں گے بلکہ
صرف مقتدی آمین کہے گا ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ حدیث ہے اذا امن الامام فامنوا فانه من وافق تامينه تامين الملائكة غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه ، جب امام آمین کہے تو تم بھی آمین کہو کیونکہ جس کا آمین کہنا موافق پڑی ملائکہ کے آمین کہنے کے اس کے پچھلے گناہ پخش : ئیے جائیں گے۔ امام مالک کی پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث کے آخر میں ہے فان الامام يقولها یعنی امام بھی آمین بنتا ہے پاک معلوم ہوا کہ اس حدیث میں تقسیم اور بوار و مراد نہیں ہے۔
ہمارے مذہب کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے جس کو حضرت مسیب نے ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے روایت کیا ہے قال قال رسول الله اذا قال الامام ولا الضالين فقولوا امين فان الملائكة تقول أمين وان الامام يقول أمين فمن وافق تامينه تامين الملائكة غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه ( رواد عبد الرزاق في مصنفہ )
امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ امام آمین نہ کے بلکہ فقط مقتدی آمین کہے گا۔ اور دلیل اس روایت کی یہ ہے کہ امام داعی ہوتے ے اور مقتدی سننے والا اور آمین سنے والا کہتا ہے نہ کہ دائی جیسا کہ نماز کے علاوہ باقی دوسری دعاؤں میں عادت ہے۔ اور حضور ہ کے قول اذا امن الامام فامنوا میں امام کو آمین کہنے والا اس لئے کہا گیا کہ اس نے سورۂ فاتحہ پڑھ کر آمین کا سبب پید کر دیا اور مسبب کو مباشر کے نام کے ساتھ ذکر کرنا جائز ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ بنی الامیر المدینہ میں بنا ء کی نسبت امیر کی طرف مسبب ہونے کی حیثیت سے ہے۔ فوائد لفظ آمین کے ہمزہ کو بعض لوگوں نے محدود پڑھا ہے اور بعض نے محصور پڑھا ہے محدود پڑھنے کی صورت میں تو آمین ہی رہے گے اور مقصور پڑھنے کی صورت میں آمین ہوگا ۔ مگر یہ واضح رہے کہ دونوں صورتوں میں وزن فصیل ہی کا ر ہے گا ۔ پس محدود ہونے کی صورت میں الف اشباع کا ہوگا محدود ہونے کے استشہاد میں مجنوں کا یہ شعر پیش کیا جاتا ہے ویرحم الله عبداً قال امینا اس میں آمین مدو استعمال ہوا ہے آخر کا الف کبھی اس میں اشباع ہی کا ہے۔
Ruling on saying Amin for the imam and the muqtadi... Sayings of the jurists and proofs. And when the imam says 'wa la d-dallin', he should say Amin, and the muqtadi should say it too, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin.' And there is no support for Malik in his (peace be upon him) saying: 'When the imam says wa la d-dallin, then say Amin' from the perspective of division, because he said at the end: 'for the imam says it.' Translation: And when the imam says 'wa la d-dallin', then the imam himself says Amin, and the muqtadi also says Amin, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin.' And Imam Malik has no proof in the Prophet's saying 'When the imam says wa la d-dallin, then say Amin' in terms of division, because at the end of the hadith he said: 'for the imam says it.' (Page 45) Ashraf al-Hidayah sharh Urdu Hidayah volume 2, Section on the description of prayer. There is no inference because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said at the end of this hadith: 'for the imam says it.' Explanation: The issue is that at the end of Surah al-Fatihah, when the imam says 'wa la d-dallin', both the imam and the muqtadi should say Amin. Imam Malik says that only the muqtadi says Amin, the imam does not say it. Imam Malik's proof is this hadith: 'When the imam says wa la d-dallin, then say Amin.' Muslim narrated the full hadith as: 'The imam is appointed only to be followed, so do not differ from him. So when he says takbir, say takbir; when he recites, be silent; and when he says wa la d-dallin, say Amin.' Imam Malik deduced from this hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made a division: the imam's portion is completing the recitation, and the muqtadi's portion is Amin. And since division is contrary to sharing, both are not partners in saying Amin; rather, only the muqtadi says Amin. Our proof is this hadith: 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin, for whoever's saying Amin coincides with the saying of the angels, his previous sins will be forgiven.' The response to Imam Malik's presented hadith is that at the end of this hadith it says: 'for the imam says it', i.e., the imam also says Amin. So it becomes known that there is no division or other intent in this hadith. Our madhhab is also supported by the hadith which Hadhrat Musayyib narrated from Abu Hurayrah (may Allah be pleased with him): He said, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When the imam says wa la d-dallin, say Amin, for the angels say Amin, and the imam says Amin. So whoever's saying Amin coincides with the angels' saying Amin, his previous sins will be forgiven.' (Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq in his Musannaf.) There is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifah that the imam does not say Amin, but only the muqtadi says Amin. The proof of this narration is that the imam is the supplicant (da'i) and the muqtadi is the listener, and Amin is said by the listener, not the supplicant, as is customary in other supplications outside prayer. And in the Prophet's saying 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin', the imam is called the one saying Amin because he created the cause of Amin by reciting Surah al-Fatihah, and it is permissible to mention the effect (musabbab) with the name of the direct doer (mubashir), like when a building is built by the amir in Madinah, the building is attributed to the amir as the one who caused it. Benefits: Regarding the word 'Amin', some people recite it with madd (elongation) and some with qasr (shortening). In the case of madd, it remains 'Amin'; in the case of qasr, it becomes 'Amin'. But it should be clear that in both cases, the pattern is fa'eel. So in the case of madd, the alif is for prolongation. As evidence for madd, the poem of Majnun is cited: 'wa yarhamu Allahu abdan qala amina' in which 'Amin' is used with madd. The final alif in it is for prolongation.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether the imam should say 'Amin' after Surah al-Fatihah. The text first states the Hanafi position: both imam and muqtadi should say Amin, based on the hadith 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin.' It then mentions that Imam Malik held that only the muqtadi says Amin, based on a different hadith that appears to divide roles. The Hanafi response is that the same hadith ends with 'for the imam says it', indicating that the imam also says Amin; thus the division is not exclusive. The text also narrates a weak report from Imam Abu Hanifah that only the muqtadi says Amin, with the reasoning that the imam is the supplicant and the muqtadi is the one who responds with Amin. However, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that both say Amin. The passage concludes with a discussion on the pronunciation of 'Amin' with madd or qasr, noting that both follow the pattern of fa'eel.

Key Terms
آمین (Amin): A word meaning 'O Allah, respond' said after reciting Surah al-Fatihah.
مقتدی (muqtadi): The follower in prayer, i.e., the person praying behind the imam.
امام (imam): The prayer leader.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the imam saying 'Amin' after Surah al-Fatihah in an audible prayer?
A) The imam must not say Amin; only the muqtadi says it.
B) The imam should say Amin silently, and the muqtadi says it aloud.
C) Both the imam and the muqtadi should say Amin.
D) Only the muqtadi says Amin, and the imam remains silent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, relying on explicit hadith, rules that both the imam and the muqtadi say 'Amin' aloud after Surah al-Fatihah in audible prayers.

Ruling on Saying Amin: Hanafi vs Maliki
Hanafi refutation of Maliki position on Amin after Fatihah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on saying Amin and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using the full hadith text.

Core Idea
Both imam and follower say Amin; the hadith that seems to exclude the imam actually includes him.

The simple act of saying 'Amin' after Surah al-Fatihah is the subject of a well-known inter-madhhab dispute. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that both the imam and the follower say Amin, and the Maliki view that only the follower does. We will analyse the key hadith evidence and see how the Hanafi school harmonises apparently conflicting narrations.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding saying Amin after al-Fatihah in congregational prayer.
The ruling is that both imam and ma'mum say Amin.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which school or imam disagrees, and what exactly do they hold?
Imam Malik holds that only the ma'mum says Amin.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What hadith does Imam Malik use to support his position, and how does he interpret it?
The hadith: 'When the imam says wa la al-dallin, say Amin.' He interprets it as a division of roles.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut the Maliki argument using the same hadith and additional evidence?
The full hadith includes 'fainna al-imama yaqulaha' (for the imam says it).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in how prayer is performed between the two schools?
In Hanafi prayer, the imam says Amin audibly; in Maliki prayer, only followers say Amin.

Source Text

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ سورۃ فاتحہ کے ختم پر جب امام ولا الضالین کے تو امام اور مقتدی دونوں کو آمین کہنا چاہئے ۔ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ فقیہ مقتدی آمین کہے امام آمین نہ ہے۔
امام مالک کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے اذا قال الامام ولا الضالين فقولوا امین مسلم نے پوری حدیث اس طرح روایت کی ہے انما جعل الامام ليؤتم به فلا تختلفوا عليه فاذ اكبر فكبروا واذا قرأ فانصتواو اذا قال ولا الضالين فقولوا امين تن امام تو اس لئے بنایا گیا کہ اس کی اقتداء کی جائے سو تم اس سے اختلاف مت کرو پس جب وہ تکبیر کے تو تم تکبیر کہو اور جب وہ پڑھے تو تم خاموش رہو اور جب و ہ ولا الضالین کے تو تم آمین کہو۔ امام مالک نے اس حدیث سے اس طرح استدلال کیا ہے کہ حضور میں نے تقسیم فرمائی چنانچہ امام کے حصہ میں قرآت کا اتمام ہے اور مندی کے حصہ میں آمین ہے اور چونکہ تقسیم شرکت کے منافی ہے اس لئے آمین کہنے میں امام اور مقتدی دونوں شریک نہیں ہوں گے بلکہ صرف مقتدی آمین کہے گا ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ حدیث ہے اذا امن الامام فامنوا فانه من وافق تامينه تامين الملائكة غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه ، جب امام آمین کہے تو تم بھی آمین کہو کیونکہ جس کا آمین کہنا موافق پڑی ملائکہ کے آمین کہنے کے اس کے پچھلے گناہ پخش : ئیے جائیں گے۔ امام مالک کی پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث کے آخر میں ہے فان الامام يقولها یعنی امام بھی آمین بنتا ہے پاک معلوم ہوا کہ اس حدیث میں تقسیم اور بوار و مراد نہیں ہے۔
ہمارے مذہب کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے جس کو حضرت مسیب نے ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے روایت کیا ہے قال قال رسول الله اذا قال الامام ولا الضالين فقولوا امين فان الملائكة تقول أمين وان الامام يقول أمين فمن وافق تامينه تامين الملائكة غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه ( رواد عبد الرزاق في مصنفہ )
Explanation of the issue: At the end of Surah al-Fatihah, when the imam says 'wa la al-dallin', both the imam and the follower should say Amin. Imam Malik says that only the follower says Amin, not the imam. Imam Malik's evidence is this hadith: 'When the imam says wa la al-dallin, then say Amin.' Muslim narrated the full hadith as: 'The imam is appointed only to be followed, so do not differ with him. When he says takbir, say takbir; when he recites, be silent; and when he says wa la al-dallin, say Amin.' Imam Malik argued from this hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made a division: the imam's portion is completing the recitation, and the follower's portion is Amin. Since division precludes partnership, both should not share in saying Amin; rather, only the follower says Amin. Our evidence is this hadith: 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin, for whoever's saying Amin coincides with the angels' saying Amin, his previous sins will be forgiven.' The response to Imam Malik's hadith is that at the end of that hadith it states: 'For the imam says it' (i.e., the imam also says Amin), so it is clear that this hadith does not intend division and exclusion. Our madhhab is also supported by the hadith narrated by Musayyib from Abu Hurayra: 'The Messenger of Allah said: When the imam says wa la al-dallin, say Amin, for the angels say Amin, and the imam says Amin. So whoever's saying Amin coincides with the angels' saying Amin, his previous sins will be forgiven.' (Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq in his Musannaf)
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding the ruling on saying Amin after Surah al-Fatihah in congregational prayer. The Hanafi position, as stated in the matn, is that both the imam and the follower (ma'mum) should say Amin. Imam Malik holds that only the follower says Amin, not the imam. The Maliki proof is a hadith in Sahih Muslim that commands the followers to say Amin when the imam says 'wa la al-dallin', implying that the imam does not say it; they also argue that the hadith indicates a division of roles between imam and follower. The Hanafi response is that the same hadith, in its full version recorded by Muslim, includes the phrase 'fainna al-imama yaqulaha' (for the imam says it), thus proving that the imam also says Amin. The Hanafi school further supports its position with an additional hadith from Abd al-Razzaq's Musannaf, narrated by Abu Hurayra, which explicitly states that both the imam and the angels say Amin. The Hanafis argue that the Maliki interpretation ignores this part of the hadith. The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is that both say Amin, as this is consistent with the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the general principle that the imam's actions are a model for the congregation. This dispute has a practical consequence: in Hanafi congregational prayers, the imam says Amin audibly enough for those behind him to hear, while in Maliki practice, only the followers say Amin. The passage uses pure hadith evidence (dalil naqli) and shows how the Hanafi school handles a potentially contradictory hadith by harmonizing its parts.

Key Terms
آمین (Amin): A word meaning 'O Allah, accept (our supplication)', said after Surah al-Fatihah in prayer.
امام (imam): The leader of congregational prayer.
مقتدی (muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the imam
B) Only the ma'mum
C) Both the imam and the ma'mum
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that both the imam and the follower say Amin, supported by the full text of the hadith from Sahih Muslim and additional narrations.

Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa's Other Riwayah on Amin
Discussion of a riwayah where Abu Hanifa says only ma'mum says Amin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasoning behind the minority Hanafi view that only the ma'mum says Amin, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A minority Hanafi view: only the ma'mum says Amin; the majority and mufta bihi is that both say it.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the saying of Amin in prayer. Although the established Hanafi ruling is that both the imam and the ma'mum say Amin, a riwayah from Imam Abu Hanifa holds that only the ma'mum says it. We will examine the rational argument (dalil aqli) presented for this minority position and understand why the majority view prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Note the majority Hanafi view (both say Amin) and the minority riwayah (only ma'mum says Amin).
The majority view is the mufta bihi; the minority is a nawadir transmission.
2
Examine the minority's proof
The proof is based on analogy: the imam is the supplicant (da'i), and in general supplication the supplicant does not say Amin to his own du'a.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof).
3
Analyze the analogy
Understand how the reasoning applies: the imam recites Fatihah (a supplication), so he is the da'i, and the follower says Amin.
Compare with non-prayer du'a: the one making du'a does not say Amin.
4
Interpret the hadith
The hadith 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin' is reinterpreted metaphorically: the imam is called the say-er of Amin because he causes it.
Similar to 'the governor built the mosque' when he ordered it.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and why
The majority view is relied upon because explicit textual evidence overrides analogy, and it is the established practice.
This riwayah is recorded but not acted upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ امام آمین نہ کے بلکہ فقط مقتدی آمین کہے گا۔ اور دلیل اس روایت کی یہ ہے کہ امام داعی ہوتے ے اور مقتدی سننے والا اور آمین سنے والا کہتا ہے نہ کہ دائی جیسا کہ نماز کے علاوہ باقی دوسری دعاؤں میں عادت ہے۔ اور حضور ہ کے قول اذا امن الامام فامنوا میں امام کو آمین کہنے والا اس لئے کہا گیا کہ اس نے سورۂ فاتحہ پڑھ کر آمین کا سبب پید کر دیا اور مسبب کو مباشر کے نام کے ساتھ ذکر کرنا جائز ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ بنی الامیر المدینہ میں بنا ء کی نسبت امیر کی طرف مسبب ہونے کی حیثیت سے ہے۔
There is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that the imam does not say Amin; rather, only the follower says Amin. The proof for this narration is that the imam is the supplicant (da'i) and the follower is the listener, and the listener says Amin, not the supplicant, just as is customary in other supplications outside prayer. And the Prophet's saying 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin' called the imam a 'say-er of Amin' because he, by reciting Surah al-Fatihah, created the cause for Amin, and it is permissible to refer to the effect by the name of the direct agent, as in 'built by the governor of the city' where building is attributed to the governor as the cause.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Although the established Hanafi ruling is that both imam and ma'mum say Amin, there is a riwayah (narration) from Imam Abu Hanifa that the imam does not say Amin, only the ma'mum does. The reasoning given is based on analogy with general supplication: the imam is the one making the supplication (da'i), and the follower says Amin to affirm the supplication. In normal practice, the supplicant does not say Amin to his own du'a; rather, the listeners say it. To reconcile this with the hadith 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin', they interpret the imam's 'saying Amin' as a metaphorical attribution: because the imam recites the Fatihah and thereby causes the Amin, he is called the one who says Amin, even though in reality he does not utter it. This is similar to saying 'the governor built the mosque' when in fact he ordered the construction. However, this riwayah is not the relied-upon position (mufta bihi); the dominant Hanafi view is that both say Amin, based on explicit hadith evidence that the imam says it. The fact that this minority opinion is recorded shows the depth of ijtihad within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
داعی (da'i): The one who makes supplication; in this context, the imam is the supplicant
مسبب (musabbib): The effect or indirect agent; here, the imam is the cause of Amin

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi ruling regarding who says Amin in prayer?
A) Only the imam
B) Only the ma'mum
C) Both the imam and the ma'mum
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi ruling is that both imam and ma'mum say Amin in prayer, despite a minority riwayah from Abu Hanifa that only the ma'mum does.

Correct Pronunciation of 'Amin': Madd and Qasr
Linguistic analysis of 'Amin' pronunciation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the permissible pronunciations of 'Amin' (madd and qasr) from the prohibited tashdid, and explain the ruling for each.

Core Idea
Pronounce 'Amin' with madd or qasr, never with tashdid.

The word 'Amin' is recited after Surah al-Fatiha in prayer. Classical scholars analysed its correct pronunciation, finding two permissible variants (long and short alif) and one grave error (doubling the 'm'). This lesson parses the linguistic evidence from Arabic poetry to clarify the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two permissible pronunciations
From the passage, list the two ways the hamza of 'Amin' is pronounced: with madd (lengthening of alif) and with qasr (shortening). Note that both follow the pattern 'fa'eel'.
The Arabic term for madd is مد, for qasr is قصر.
2
Recognise the prohibited pronunciation
The passage warns against tashdid (تشدید), which is doubling the 'm' in 'Amin'. This is considered a grave error (khata' fahish).
Tashdid changes the word's meaning and structure.
3
Examine the poetic evidence for madd
The story of Majnun Layla includes the line 'wa yarhamu Allahu abdan qala Amina' – here 'Amin' is pronounced with madd. Understand that this shows classical usage.
The poem's context reinforces that madd is authentic.
4
Examine the poetic evidence for qasr
Jubayr ibn Adbat's poem 'Amin fa zaada Allahu ma baynana bu'da' uses qasr. Note the unusual word order (Amin before the supplication) to emphasize acceptance.
Both madd and qasr are equally valid.
5
Derive the fiqh ruling
Based on the evidence, pronouncing 'Amin' with madd or qasr is permissible (mubah); pronouncing with tashdid is prohibited (haram) and invalidates the recitation in prayer.
If done unintentionally, sajdah al-sahw may be required.

اس کو اپنی حاجت کے لئے پکارا خدا کرے ہماری دوری میں اور بھی اضافہ ہو اور اے خدا تو اس دعا کو قبول کرلے۔ اس میں آمین کا لفظ پہلے آیا ہے اور دعا بعد میں ہے حالانکہ ترتیب واقعی اس کے خلافف چاہتی ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ شاعر کو قبولیت دعا کا زیادہ اہتمام ہے پس اہتمام ہونے کی وجہ سے لفظ آمین کو مقدم کر دیا۔ جمیل عفی عنہ
Benefits: Some people read the hamza of the word 'Amin' with madd (lengthening), and some read it with qasr (shortening). When reading with madd, it remains 'Amin', and when reading with qasr, it becomes 'Amin' (with different spelling). But it should be clear that in both cases the measure (wazn) is 'fa'eel'. So in the case of madd, the alif is for prolongation. To prove madd, the poem of Majnun is cited: 'wa yarhamu Allahu abdan qala Amina' (May Allah have mercy on a servant who said 'Amin'). In this, 'Amin' is used with madd; the final alif is for prolongation. This poem has a story: When Majnun's heart became filled with love for Layla and he was distracted, his father took him to perform Hajj. At the Kaaba, the father asked him to pray for removal of love for Layla. Instead, Majnun prayed for union with Layla. The father beat him, so Majnun then recited: 'Ya rabbi la taslabni hubbaha abadan wa yarhamu Allahu abdan qala Amina' (O Lord, do not take away her love from me forever, and may Allah have mercy on the one who says Amin to this prayer). That was for madd. For qasr, the second poem is presented: 'Amin fa zaada Allahu ma baynana bu'da' (Amin, so Allah increased the distance between us). The evidence is that 'Amin' comes with a short alif (qasr). This poem is by Jubayr ibn Adbat. He recited it when a person refused to give him a camel. The full poem: 'Taba'ada anni fahlu idh da'awtuhu Amin fa zaada Allahu ma baynana bu'da' (The stallion distanced himself from me when I called him; Amin, so Allah increased the distance between us). In this, the word 'Amin' is placed before the supplication, which is unusual, but because the poet emphasized acceptance, he placed it first. May Allah forgive the author.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic footnote (fa'ida) discussing the correct pronunciation of the word 'Amin'. The author notes that some pronounce the hamza with madd (lengthening, i.e., 'Amin' with a long alif) and some with qasr (shortening, i.e., 'Amin' with a short alif). Both pronunciations are permissible, but the word's pattern (wazn) remains 'fa'eel'. When madd is used, the final alif serves as a lengthening (ishba'). Two classical Arabic poems are cited to support each pronunciation: first, the famous story of Majnun Layla, where he says 'wa yarhamu Allahu abdan qala Amina' (with madd); second, a poem by Jubayr ibn Adbat where 'Amin' is pronounced with qasr. The passage then explains the context of these poems. The key point is that tashdid (doubling of the 'm' in 'Amin') is a grave error, as later stated. The author also notes an unusual word order in the second poem where 'Amin' precedes the supplication, explaining that the poet prioritized acceptance of the supplication. This linguistic lesson underscores the importance of correct recitation in prayer.

Key Terms
مد (madd): Prolongation of the vowel; here, pronouncing the alif of 'Amin' as a long vowel
قصر (qasr): Abbreviation; here, pronouncing the alif of 'Amin' as a short vowel
تشدید (tashdid): Doubling of a consonant; here, mistakenly doubling the 'm' in 'Amin'

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) With qasr (short alif)
C) With tashdid (doubled 'm')

Key Takeaway
Pronounce 'Amin' with madd or qasr, never with tashdid.

Saying Amin Silently in Prayer: Hanafi Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof on silent Amin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying Amin in prayer and explain the two proofs (hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and the nature of du'a) that support it.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, both imam and ma'mum say Amin silently because it is a supplication, and supplications are made quietly.

This passage addresses a common point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: the volume of saying Amin in congregational prayer. The author affirms the Hanafi position that Amin is said silently by both the imam and the followers, and provides two proofs: a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and the general principle that supplications are best made in secret.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying 'Amin' after Surah al-Fatiha in prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that it is Sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) to say it silently (sirr).
The ruling is derived from the sources below.
2
Locate the first dalil: hadith of Ibn Mas'ud
The author references a hadith narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that indicates the Prophet ﷺ said Amin silently. This is the primary transmitted proof.
The exact wording is not quoted here but is known from other Hanafi sources.
3
Locate the second dalil: Amin is a du'a
The author argues that Amin is a supplication (du'a), and the basis of supplication is concealment (ikhfa'), as humility and sincerity are better preserved. This is derived from Quranic guidance and general practice.
This is a rational proof (istidlal) based on the nature of du'a.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the imam says Amin aloud (jahr) in prayers where recitation is aloud (jaliya). The Hanafi school maintains silence for both imam and ma'mum.
This difference is based on different interpretations of the same sources.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In Hanafi congregational prayers, the congregation does not hear the imam's Amin; in Shafi'i practice, the imam's Amin is audible.
This ruling does not affect the validity of the prayer but is a matter of preferred practice.

Source Text

Both the imam and the follower will say Amin silently. And the correct pronunciation of Amin has two aspects: madd and qasr, and tashdid in it is a grave error. He said: They say it silently due to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that we narrated, and because it is a supplication, so its basis is on concealment (ikhfa'). Translation: He said that all these people say Amin softly due to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that we narrated, and because Amin is a supplication, so its foundation is on concealment. And in Amin there are two ways: madd and qasr, and tashdid in it is a grave error. Explanation: According to us, it is Sunnah for the imam and the followers to say Amin silently. Imam al-Shafi'i is of the view that Amin is said aloud.

Commentary
This passage gives the final ruling on the volume of saying Amin in prayer. According to the Hanafi school, both the imam and the ma'mum say Amin silently (sirr). The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (not quoted in full here but referenced) and the principle that Amin is a supplication (du'a), and supplications are typically performed quietly to ensure humility and sincerity. The passage also reiterates the earlier linguistic points about madd and qasr being correct, and tashdid being wrong. It contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that Amin is said aloud (jahr) in prayers where the recitation is aloud (jaliya). The practical consequence is that in Hanafi congregational prayers, the congregation will not hear the imam's Amin, as it is said silently. This ruling is based on the principle that the prayer should be free from any disturbance, and Amin is a supplication, not a Quranic recitation.

Key Terms
سرا (sirran): Silently; in a low voice such that only the speaker can hear himself
جہر (jahr): Aloud; in a clear audible voice
آمین (Amin): A word said after Surah al-Fatiha meaning 'O Allah, respond'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Saying Ameen Silently: Hanafi Stance and Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute with hadith criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying Ameen silently and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the criteria of hadith criticism.

Core Idea
Ameen is a supplication, and supplications are best said secretly—this is the Hanafi proof.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: should the imam and followers say Ameen aloud or silently after reciting Surah al-Fatihah? The Hanafi school rules it is sunnah to say it silently, while the Shafi'i school holds it should be aloud. The author provides both proofs and resolves the conflict through hadith criticism and a linguistic argument based on the nature of supplication.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding Ameen: it is said silently by both imam and muqtadi. Note that this is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah).
2
Identify the Hanafi proofs
Locate the two main proofs: (1) the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud listing four things the imam says silently, including Ameen; (2) the Qur'anic principle that supplication should be made secretly (khufyah).
The first proof is a specific textual evidence; the second is a general principle.
3
Follow the opponent's argument
State the Shafi'i position: Ameen is said aloud. Identify their proof: the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr that the Prophet raised his voice when saying Ameen.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school rebuts the Shafi'i proof: the hadith of Wa'il is rendered unreliable because his son Alqama narrated it with a contradictory wording ('lowered his voice'), causing the narration to be rejected due to internal contradiction.
This is a method of jarh wa ta'dil (hadith criticism).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Conclude the practical difference: in Hanafi congregations, Ameen is said silently; in Shafi'i congregations, it is said aloud. Also note the linguistic issues of madd/qasr and tashdid.
The thamarah (fruit) is the actual practice in prayer.
