Refuting the Bedouin Hadith: The Status of Ta'dil al-Arkan
Refuting the Bedouin Hadith as proof for fardiyyah of ta'dil al-arkan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state how the Hanafi school rebuts the Bedouin Hadith to argue that ta'dil al-arkan is not fard.

Core Idea
The Prophet called the deficient prayer ‘prayer’, so the deficiency cannot be fard—only a lesser category.

The Bedouin Hadith is often cited by those who claim that ta'dil al-arkan (proper sequence and stillness) is fard. In this passage, the Hanafi author shows that the hadith actually proves the opposite: because the Prophet still called the deficient prayer ‘prayer’, the deficiency does not invalidate it, and thus it cannot be a fard. This is a crucial example of how a single hadith can be read differently depending on usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing claim
Some argue that the Bedouin Hadith proves ta'dil al-arkan is fard because the Prophet criticized the deficiencies. Understand what they claim.
2
Analyse the Prophet's labeling
The Prophet explicitly called the deficient prayer 'prayer'. Note that if a true rukn (like ruku') is omitted, the act is not called prayer. Therefore, the deficiency here does not nullify the prayer.
Compare with omitting a pillar.
3
Apply the Hanafi refutation
The hadith says 'You have decreased from your prayer', not 'Your prayer is invalid'. The decrease indicates a deficiency, not nullification. Hence, the missing element (ta'dil) cannot be fard.
Fard elements, if omitted, make the act invalid.
4
Conclude the status
Since the deficiency does not invalidate, ta'dil al-arkan is not fard. It may be wajib or sunnah, depending on further evidence.
The passage does not specify the exact positive ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفی ماروی الخ سے حدیث اعرابی کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اعرابی نے نماز کی شکل میں جو کچھ کیا تھا حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو نماز کے ساتھ موسوم کیا ہے چنانچہ اسی حدیث اعرابی کے آخر میں یہ الفاظ مروی ہیں وما نقصت من هذا شياء فقد نقصت من ملائک یعنی تو نے جو کچھ ان چیزوں میں کمی کی تو تیری نماز میں کمی ہو گئی۔ پس اگر تعدیل ارکان کو ترک کرنا مفسد نماز ہوتا ہے تو آپ اس کو صلوٰۃ (نماز) کے ساتھ موسوم نہ فرماتے جیسا کہ اگر رکوع یا سجدہ کو ترک کر دیا گیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے اور اس کو نماز نہیں کہا جاتا پس معلوم ہوا کہ ترک تعدیل سے نماز میں نقصان تو آتا ہے مگر نماز فاسد نہیں ہوتی اور ظاہر ہے کہ فرض کی یہ شان نہیں ہے پس حدیث اعرابی سے بھی تعدیل ارکان کی فرضیت ثابت نہیں ہوتی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ قومہ اور دوسجدوں کے درمیان جلسه با تفاق مشائخ طرفین کے نزدیک سنت ہیں اور رہا رکوع اور سجدہ میں طمانیت کا حکم سو اس کی تخریج میں اختلاف ہے چنانچہ امام ابو عبد الله الجرجانی کی تخریج یہ ہے کہ طمانیت بھی مسنون ہے اور امام کرخی نے تخریج کی کہ یہ واجب ہے حتی کہ امام کرخی کے نزدیک ترک طمانیت سے کہو کے دو سجدے واجب ہوں گے جرجانی کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ طمانیت تکمیل رکن کے لئے مشروع کی گئی ہے اور جو چیز تکمیل رکن کے واسطے مشروع ہو وہ سنت ہوتی ہے لہذا یہ طمانیت بھی سنت ہوگی۔ اور امام کرخی کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ طمانیت رکن مقصود نفسہ کے لئے مشروع کی گئی ہے اور جو چیز ایسی ہو وہ واجب ہوتی ہے اس لئے یہ طمانیت واجب ہوگی۔
And from 'Wa fi marawi': this is a response to the Hadith of the Bedouin. The gist of the response is that the Bedouin did something in the form of prayer, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) called it prayer. Thus, at the end of this Hadith of the Bedouin, these words are narrated: 'And whatever you have decreased from these things, you have decreased from your prayer.' So if abandoning ta'dil al-arkan (proper sequence) invalidates prayer, then the Prophet would not have called it prayer. Just as if ruku' or sujud is abandoned, the prayer becomes invalid and is not called prayer. So it is known that abandoning ta'dil causes deficiency in prayer, but the prayer is not invalidated, and it is clear that this is not the characteristic of an obligation (fard). So the Hadith of the Bedouin does not prove the obligatoriness of ta'dil al-arkan. The author of Al-Hidayah said: 'Qawmah (standing after ruku') and the sitting between the two prostrations are, by agreement of the scholars of both sides, sunnah. As for the ruling of tuma'ninah (stillness) in ruku' and sujud, there is a difference in its deduction. Thus, the deduction of Imam Abu Abdullah al-Jurjani is that tuma'ninah is also sunnah. Imam al-Karkhi deduced that it is wajib, so much so that according to Imam al-Karkhi, abandoning tuma'ninah makes two extra prostrations (sajdatay al-sahw) wajib. The reason for al-Jurjani's statement is that this tuma'ninah is legislated for the completion of the pillar, and what is legislated for the completion of the pillar is sunnah; therefore this tuma'ninah is sunnah. The reason for al-Karkhi's statement is that this tuma'ninah is legislated for the pillar itself intended, and what is such is wajib; therefore this tuma'ninah is wajib.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the nature of tuma'ninah (stillness) during ruku' and sujud. The author first refutes an opposing view that uses the Bedouin Hadith to claim that ta'dil al-arkan (proper sequence) is fard (obligatory). The refutation shows that the Prophet (peace be upon him) still called the Bedouin's deficient prayer 'prayer', proving that the deficiency does not invalidate the prayer, so it cannot be fard. Then the author quotes Sahib al-Hidayah stating that qawmah and jalsah are sunnah by consensus, but regarding tuma'ninah there is ikhtilaf. Imam al-Jurjani considers it sunnah (legislated for completion of the pillar), while Imam al-Karkhi considers it wajib (legislated for the pillar itself) and even says abandoning it necessitates sajdatay al-sahw. The passage does not explicitly state which view is mufta bihi, but the inclusion of al-Karkhi's view as a strong position is notable. Hanafi students should know that this ikhtilaf exists and that omitting tuma'ninah does not invalidate salah according to al-Jurjani, but according to al-Karkhi it requires compensation (sajdatay al-sahw) and is sinful.

Key Terms
تعدیل ارکان (ta'dil al-arkan): Performing the pillars of prayer with proper sequence and stillness.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary hadith not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the Hanafi refutation of the Bedouin Hadith regarding ta'dil al-arkan?
A) The hadith is weak and cannot be used.
B) The hadith proves that ta'dil al-arkan is fard.
C) The hadith proves that ta'dil al-arkan is not fard because the deficient prayer was still called prayer.
D) The hadith is about a different issue.

Key Takeaway
The Bedouin Hadith does not prove that ta'dil al-arkan is fard; it only indicates a deficiency, not nullification.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Tuma'ninah: Sunnah or Wajib?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tuma'ninah: sunnah vs wajib with illah analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Imam al-Jurjani's and Imam al-Karkhi's views on tuma'ninah and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
Tuma'ninah is either sunnah (Jurjani) or wajib (Karkhi); both agree it is not fard, but the consequence differs: wajib requires sajdatay al-sahw if omitted.

After refuting the fardiyyah claim, the passage from Al-Hidayah turns to the specific ruling of tuma'ninah (stillness) in ruku' and sujud. It first notes that qawmah (standing after ruku') and jalsah (sitting between prostrations) are sunnah by consensus. For tuma'ninah, however, there is a well-known ikhtilaf between two later Hanafi authorities: Imam al-Jurjani considers it sunnah, while Imam al-Karkhi considers it wajib, even requiring sajdatay al-sahw for its omission.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed sunnah of qawmah and jalsah
Recognize that the scholars of both sides agree that qawmah and jalsah are sunnah, not fard or wajib.
This is a point of consensus within the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the two positions on tuma'ninah
Imam al-Jurjani says tuma'ninah is sunnah; Imam al-Karkhi says it is wajib. Understand that both are later Hanafi scholars, not from Zahir al-Riwayah.
Imam al-Jurjani and Imam al-Karkhi are known for their usul and takhrij.
3
Understand the illah behind each view
Jurjani: Tuma'ninah is legislated to complete the pillar (ruku' or sujud); what completes a sunnah act is itself sunnah. Karkhi: Tuma'ninah is for the pillar itself; what is intended for the pillar is wajib.
Key distinction: completion vs. essential part.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to Jurjani, omitting tuma'ninah does not require sajdatay al-sahw and is makruh. According to Karkhi, omitting it requires sajdatay al-sahw and is sinful if deliberate.
This difference affects actual practice in salah.
5
Note the mufta bihi view
Later Hanafi fatwa tends to adopt the wajib view, but the passage does not explicitly prefer one. As a mufti, one should know both views and the evidence.
The later school (mutakhkhirin) often leans toward Karkhi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفی ماروی الخ سے حدیث اعرابی کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اعرابی نے نماز کی شکل میں جو کچھ کیا تھا حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو نماز کے ساتھ موسوم کیا ہے چنانچہ اسی حدیث اعرابی کے آخر میں یہ الفاظ مروی ہیں وما نقصت من هذا شياء فقد نقصت من ملائک یعنی تو نے جو کچھ ان چیزوں میں کمی کی تو تیری نماز میں کمی ہو گئی۔ پس اگر تعدیل ارکان کو ترک کرنا مفسد نماز ہوتا ہے تو آپ اس کو صلوٰۃ (نماز) کے ساتھ موسوم نہ فرماتے جیسا کہ اگر رکوع یا سجدہ کو ترک کر دیا گیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے اور اس کو نماز نہیں کہا جاتا پس معلوم ہوا کہ ترک تعدیل سے نماز میں نقصان تو آتا ہے مگر نماز فاسد نہیں ہوتی اور ظاہر ہے کہ فرض کی یہ شان نہیں ہے پس حدیث اعرابی سے بھی تعدیل ارکان کی فرضیت ثابت نہیں ہوتی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ قومہ اور دوسجدوں کے درمیان جلسه با تفاق مشائخ طرفین کے نزدیک سنت ہیں اور رہا رکوع اور سجدہ میں طمانیت کا حکم سو اس کی تخریج میں اختلاف ہے چنانچہ امام ابو عبد الله الجرجانی کی تخریج یہ ہے کہ طمانیت بھی مسنون ہے اور امام کرخی نے تخریج کی کہ یہ واجب ہے حتی کہ امام کرخی کے نزدیک ترک طمانیت سے کہو کے دو سجدے واجب ہوں گے جرجانی کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ طمانیت تکمیل رکن کے لئے مشروع کی گئی ہے اور جو چیز تکمیل رکن کے واسطے مشروع ہو وہ سنت ہوتی ہے لہذا یہ طمانیت بھی سنت ہوگی۔ اور امام کرخی کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ طمانیت رکن مقصود نفسہ کے لئے مشروع کی گئی ہے اور جو چیز ایسی ہو وہ واجب ہوتی ہے اس لئے یہ طمانیت واجب ہوگی۔
And from 'Wa fi marawi': this is a response to the Hadith of the Bedouin. The gist of the response is that the Bedouin did something in the form of prayer, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) called it prayer. Thus, at the end of this Hadith of the Bedouin, these words are narrated: 'And whatever you have decreased from these things, you have decreased from your prayer.' So if abandoning ta'dil al-arkan (proper sequence) invalidates prayer, then the Prophet would not have called it prayer. Just as if ruku' or sujud is abandoned, the prayer becomes invalid and is not called prayer. So it is known that abandoning ta'dil causes deficiency in prayer, but the prayer is not invalidated, and it is clear that this is not the characteristic of an obligation (fard). So the Hadith of the Bedouin does not prove the obligatoriness of ta'dil al-arkan. The author of Al-Hidayah said: 'Qawmah (standing after ruku') and the sitting between the two prostrations are, by agreement of the scholars of both sides, sunnah. As for the ruling of tuma'ninah (stillness) in ruku' and sujud, there is a difference in its deduction. Thus, the deduction of Imam Abu Abdullah al-Jurjani is that tuma'ninah is also sunnah. Imam al-Karkhi deduced that it is wajib, so much so that according to Imam al-Karkhi, abandoning tuma'ninah makes two extra prostrations (sajdatay al-sahw) wajib. The reason for al-Jurjani's statement is that this tuma'ninah is legislated for the completion of the pillar, and what is legislated for the completion of the pillar is sunnah; therefore this tuma'ninah is sunnah. The reason for al-Karkhi's statement is that this tuma'ninah is legislated for the pillar itself intended, and what is such is wajib; therefore this tuma'ninah is wajib.

The author first refutes an opposing view that uses the Bedouin Hadith to claim that ta'dil al-arkan (proper sequence) is fard (obligatory). The passage does not explicitly state which view is mufta bihi, but the inclusion of al-Karkhi's view as a strong position is notable. Key Terms
طمانیت (tuma'ninah): Stillness and calm in each posture of prayer, especially in ruku' and sujud.
تخریج (takhrij): Deduction of a ruling from a principle or from the statements of early scholars.

Key Takeaway
Tuma'ninah is either sunnah or wajib in the Hanafi school; the relied-upon view is that it is wajib, requiring sajdatay al-sahw if omitted.

Description of Sujud: Hand Placement and Sufficing with Nose or Forehead
Describing sujud posture and the ruling on using only nose or forehead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah posture of sujud and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on sufficing with the nose alone.

Core Idea
Sujud requires the forehead and nose together; sufficing with nose alone is excused only according to Abu Hanifa.

The sujud (prostration) is a pillar of salah, and its proper posture is established by the sunnah. This lesson covers the recommended hand and face placement as narrated from the Prophet ﷺ, and then examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: whether it is permissible to prostrate on only the nose or whether both nose and forehead are required.

Guided Path
1
State the sunnah posture of sujud
Identify the description of sujud from the hadith: hands flat on the ground, face between palms, elbows raised, etc.
This is the recommended method, not the obligatory minimum.
2
Identify the proof for the posture
Locate the dalil from Wa'il ibn Hujr and Bara' ibn 'Azib that describe the Prophet's sujud.
These are ahadith with zanni thubut.
3
Determine the obligatory elements of sujud
From the text, extract what is fard (forehead/nose) versus sunnah (hands, knees). Note al-Quduri's view on the feet.
The rukn is placing part of the face (forehead or nose) on the ground.
4
Analyze the dispute on sufficing with nose or forehead
Abu Hanifa allows sufficing with nose alone (though makruh). The Sahibayn require an excuse for nose-only sujud.
Their evidence is the hadith of seven bones, which specifically includes the forehead.
5
Determine the practical consequence
According to Abu Hanifa, prayer is valid if only the nose touches (without excuse). According to Sahibayn, it is invalid unless there is an excuse.
The safer practice (mufta bihi) is to place both nose and forehead.

Description of Sujud (method): And he should place his hands on the ground because Wa'il ibn Hujr described the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): He prostrated and leaned on his palms and raised his buttocks and placed his face between his hands and his hands parallel to his ears, because it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) did so. Translation: And he should place his hands on the ground because Wa'il ibn Hujr described the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): He prostrated and leaned on his palms and raised his buttocks and placed his face between his hands and his hands parallel to his ears, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did that. Explanation: This phrase describes the manner of sujud: he should place both hands on the ground, and the face between the palms, and both hands parallel to the ears. The proof is the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr. He said: 'He prostrated and leaned on his palms and raised his buttocks.' And from Wa'il ibn Hujr it is also narrated: 'I watched the Prophet (peace be upon him) and when he prostrated, he placed his hands parallel to his ears.' Also, Abu Ishaq says: I asked Bara' ibn 'Azib (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Where would the Prophet (peace be upon him) place his forehead when he prostrated?' He said: 'Between his palms.' Ruling on prostrating on the nose and forehead, and the ruling on sufficing with one of them, statements of jurists and proofs. He said: And he should prostrate on his nose and forehead because the Prophet (peace be upon him) persisted on that. If he suffices with one of them, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Sahibayn) said: It is not permissible to suffice with the nose except due to an excuse, and this is a narration from him (Abu Hanifa) as well. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones,' and he counted the forehead among them. For Abu Hanifa, sujud is realized by placing some part of the face that is commanded, except the cheek and chin are excluded by consensus, and what is mentioned in the narration is the face in the well-known view. Placing the hands and knees is sunnah for us because sujud is realized without them. As for placing the feet, al-Quduri mentioned that it is fard in sujud.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed description of sujud (prostration) in the Hanafi school. It begins by stating the sunnah method: hands placed on the ground, palms flat, fingers together, face between the hands, and hands parallel to the ears. The proof comes from the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr, who observed the Prophet's prayer and described his posture. Additional evidence from Bara' ibn 'Azib confirms the forehead is placed between the palms. The passage then discusses the ruling on prostrating on the nose and forehead. The sunnah is to place both on the ground. However, if one suffices with only one, there is a dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa permits it (even if makruh), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) do not allow sufficing with the nose alone except due to an excuse. This is based on the hadith commanding prostration on seven bones, specifically mentioning the forehead. Abu Hanifa argues that sujud is achieved by placing any part of the commanded area (the face), excluding the cheeks and chin by consensus. The passage also clarifies that placing hands and knees is sunnah, not fard, because sujud is valid without them. However, placing the feet (toes) on the ground is fard according to al-Quduri. This is a reminder that while the details enhance perfection, the essential obligation is the forehead (or part of the face) and feet.

Key Terms
سجدہ (sajdah / sujud): Prostration, placing the face (forehead and nose) on the ground in prayer.
جبهتہ (jabha / jabhah): Forehead, the part of the face above the eyebrows.
انف (anf): Nose, the part of the face used in sujud along with or instead of the forehead.
یدین (yadayn): The two hands, placed on the ground during sujud as a sunnah.
رکبتین (rukbatayn): The two knees, placed on the ground during sujud as a sunnah.
قدمین (qadamayn): The two feet, specifically the toes, placed on the ground during sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of seven bones, which part of the body is explicitly mentioned as required for sujud, leading the Sahibayn to oppose nose-only sujud?
A) The nose
B) The forehead
C) The hands
D) The feet

Key Takeaway
The sunnah is to place both nose and forehead in sujud; the Hanafi school permits the nose alone only under the lenient view of Abu Hanifa, but the mufta bihi is to combine both.

Sufficing with Nose or Forehead in Sajdah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sufficing with nose vs forehead, including method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on sufficing with only the nose in sajdah and explain the basis of the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
One may suffice with the forehead alone for sajdah, but sufficing with the nose alone is disputed: Abu Hanifa permits with dislike, Sahibayn require an excuse.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents the well-known ruling that prostration should be on both nose and forehead. The author then explores an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: what if someone limits to only one? We will examine the positions, their proofs, and the practical fatwa ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
The matn says one should prostrate on both nose and forehead because the Prophet consistently did so. This is the default wajib practice.
2
Identify the ikhtilaf scenario
If someone limits to one part, there are two cases: only forehead or only nose. The text discusses the latter.
3
Learn Abu Hanifa's position
He holds that sufficing with only the nose is permissible with karahah (dislike). His proof: the general command of sajdah (Quran) and the face includes both.
4
Learn the Sahibayn's position
They hold it is not permissible without an excuse. Their proof: the hadith of seven bones lists forehead but not the nose.
5
Understand the Hanafi response
The author cites another hadith using 'wajh' (face) which includes both nose and forehead, so both are valid. The mufta bihi position is the Sahibayn's view (nose alone not allowed without excuse).

He said: He should prostrate on his nose and forehead because the Prophet (peace be upon him) consistently did so. If he limits himself to one of them, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa. But the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not permissible to limit to the nose except due to an excuse, and this is a narration from him (Abu Hanifa). Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones, and among them he counted the forehead. For Abu Hanifa, prostration is realized by placing a part of the face which is commanded, except the cheek and chin which are excluded by consensus. What is mentioned in the well-known narration is 'the face' (wajh). And placing the hands and knees is sunnah according to us because prostration is realized without them. As for placing the feet, al-Quduri mentioned that it is obligatory in prostration. Commentary: The explanation by Sahib al-Inayah is that the rule regarding the manner of prostration and rising from it is: the limb closest to the ground should be placed first when prostrating, and the limb closest to the sky should be raised first. So the manner of prostration is: first place both knees on the ground, then both hands, then the face. Some said: after placing the hands, place the nose then the forehead. When rising, the order is: first raise the face, then both hands, then both knees. The conclusion of the passage is that prostration should be on both nose and forehead because the Prophet always did so. If one limits to one, there are two cases: (1) only the forehead, (2) only the nose. In the first case, all Hanafi scholars agree on its permissibility; in the second case, according to Abu Hanifa it is permissible with dislike. The two companions said: without excuse, limiting to the nose is not permissible; if there is an excuse, it is permissible. Their proof is the hadith in the six books: from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet said: I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: on the forehead, hands, knees, and tips of the feet. The inference is that the nose is not mentioned, so it is not a place of prostration. Abu Hanifa's proof is that the Quran commands prostration absolutely, and prostration is realized by placing part of the face, as placing the entire face is impossible due to the protrusion of the nose and forehead. The cheek and chin are excluded by consensus because prostration means reverence. So both nose and forehead remain as valid places. Since limiting to the forehead is permissible, limiting to the nose is also permissible. The response to the companions' proof is that in the well-known narration, 'wajh' (face) is mentioned instead of 'jabhah' (forehead), as narrated by Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib that the Prophet said: When a servant prostrates, seven parts prostrate with him: his face, his palms, his knees, and his feet. Here 'face' includes both nose and forehead, so both are equal in prostration.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and a commentary on the manner of prostration. The main ruling from the matn is that one should prostrate on both the nose and forehead. The author then presents the ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is permissible to suffice with either the nose or the forehead, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) say sufficing with the nose alone is not allowed without an excuse. The Sahibayn's proof is the hadith of the seven bones, which lists the forehead but not the nose. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the Quranic command to prostrate is general, and prostration is realized by placing part of the face; the nose and forehead are both valid because the whole face cannot be placed; the cheek and chin are excluded by consensus. The author then clarifies that the method of prostration (from Al-Inayah) follows the principle that the part closest to the ground is placed first and the part closest to the sky is raised first. Thus, knees first, then hands, then face (some say nose then forehead); when rising, reverse order. The response to the Sahibayn's proof points to another hadith using 'wajh' (face), which includes both nose and forehead, establishing their equality in sajdah. The practical ruling: sufficing with only the forehead is agreed upon by all Hanafis; sufficing only with the nose is permissible according to Abu Hanifa (with dislike) but not according to the Sahibayn unless there is an excuse.

Key Terms
جبهة (jabhah): The forehead; one of the seven bones of prostration
وجہ (wajh): Face; in the context of sajdah, includes both nose and forehead
اقتصار (iqtisar): Limiting oneself to one part (nose or forehead) in sajdah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi ruling on sufficing with only the nose in sajdah?
A) Valid without dislike
B) Valid but disliked
C) Invalid without an excuse
D) Invalid with or without excuse

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the forehead is the primary place of prostration; sufficing with the nose alone is only allowed with an excuse.

Salah — Prayer

The Manner of Prostration: Order of Placing and Lifting Limbs
Manner of prostration: order of placing and lifting limbs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the proper order for placing limbs in sajdah and for rising, according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
In sajdah, place knees first, then hands, then face; when rising, raise face first, then hands, then knees.

The latter part of this passage from al-Hidayah explains the sunnah method of performing prostration, based on the principle that the limb closest to the ground is placed first and the limb closest to the sky is raised first. This is a practical guideline for the worshiper.

Guided Path
1
Learn the principle
The author from al-Inayah states: the part nearest the ground is placed first when going down, and the part nearest the sky is raised first when coming up.
2
Apply to sajdah
Going down: knees (lower), then hands, then face (including nose and forehead). Some say nose first then forehead.
3
Apply to rising
Rising: face first (closest to sky), then hands, then knees.
4
Note the status
This is the sunnah method, not wajib. The prayer is valid if done differently but may miss the optimal form.

ناک پر اکتفا کرنا بھی درست نہیں ہوگا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآن پاک میں مطلقاً سجدہ کا حکم دیا گیا ہے اور سجدہ بعض چہرہ رکھنے سے متحقق ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ پورے چہرے کا رکھنا ناممکن ہے اس لئے کہ ناک اور پیشانی ایسی ابھری ہوئی ہڈیاں ہیں جو پورے چہرے کوزمین پر رکھنے سے مانع ہیں بہر حال جب پورے چہرے کا زمین پر رکھنا متعذر ہے تو بعض چہرے کا زمین پر رکھنا مامور بہ ہوگا لیکن گال اور ٹھوڑی بالا جماع خارج ہیں یعنی آیت اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے اگر چہ ان کو بھی شامل ہے لیکن بالا جماع آیت میں مراد نہیں ہیں کیونکہ سجدہ سے مراد تعظیم ہے اور گال اور ٹھوڑی زمین پر رکھنے سے تعظیم مشروع نہیں ہوئی اس لئے یہ دونوں سجدہ کے مفہوم سے خارج ہوں گے۔ پس اب ناک اور پیشانی باقی رہ گئے اور یہ دونوں سجدہ کا محل ہیں اس لئے ان دونوں پر سجدہ کرنا جائز ہے اور چونکہ پیشانی پر اکتفاء کرنا جائز ہے اس لئے ناک پر بھی اکفتار کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ والمذكور فیمار وی الخ سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مشہور روایت میں بجائے جہہ کے وجہ مذکور ہے چنانچہ سفن اربعہ میں حضرت عباس بن عبد المطلب سے مروی ہے انه سمع رسول الله يقول اذا سجد العبد سجد معه سبعة أراب وجهه وكفاه وركبتاه وقدماہ یعنی حضور و کوفرماتے ہوئے سنا کہ بندہ جب سجدہ کرتا ہے تو اس کے ساتھ سات اعضاء سجدہ کرتے ہیں اس کا چہرہ اس کی ہتھیلیاں اس کے گھٹنے اور اس کے دونوں قدم اس حدیث میں وجہ مذکور ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ منہ سے ناک اور پیشانی دونوں مراد ہیں اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ سجدہ کے حکم میں ناک اور پیشانی دونوں برابر ہیں۔
He said: He should prostrate on his nose and forehead because the Prophet (peace be upon him) consistently did so. If he limits himself to one of them, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa. But the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not permissible to limit to the nose except due to an excuse, and this is a narration from him (Abu Hanifa). Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones, and among them he counted the forehead. For Abu Hanifa, prostration is realized by placing a part of the face which is commanded, except the cheek and chin which are excluded by consensus. What is mentioned in the well-known narration is 'the face' (wajh). And placing the hands and knees is sunnah according to us because prostration is realized without them. As for placing the feet, al-Quduri mentioned that it is obligatory in prostration. Commentary: The explanation by Sahib al-Inayah is that the rule regarding the manner of prostration and rising from it is: the limb closest to the ground should be placed first when prostrating, and the limb closest to the sky should be raised first. So the manner of prostration is: first place both knees on the ground, then both hands, then the face. Some said: after placing the hands, place the nose then the forehead. When rising, the order is: first raise the face, then both hands, then both knees. The conclusion of the passage is that prostration should be on both nose and forehead because the Prophet always did so. If one limits to one, there are two cases: (1) only the forehead, (2) only the nose. In the first case, all Hanafi scholars agree on its permissibility; in the second case, according to Abu Hanifa it is permissible with dislike. The two companions said: without excuse, limiting to the nose is not permissible; if there is an excuse, it is permissible. Their proof is the hadith in the six books: from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet said: I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: on the forehead, hands, knees, and tips of the feet. The inference is that the nose is not mentioned, so it is not a place of prostration. Abu Hanifa's proof is that the Quran commands prostration absolutely, and prostration is realized by placing part of the face, as placing the entire face is impossible due to the protrusion of the nose and forehead. The cheek and chin are excluded by consensus because prostration means reverence. So both nose and forehead remain as valid places. Since limiting to the forehead is permissible, limiting to the nose is also permissible. The response to the companions' proof is that in the well-known narration, 'wajh' (face) is mentioned instead of 'jabhah' (forehead), as narrated by Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib that the Prophet said: When a servant prostrates, seven parts prostrate with him: his face, his palms, his knees, and his feet. Here 'face' includes both nose and forehead, so both are equal in prostration.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and a commentary on the manner of prostration. The main ruling from the matn is that one should prostrate on both the nose and forehead. The author then presents the ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is permissible to suffice with either the nose or the forehead, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) say sufficing with the nose alone is not allowed without an excuse. The Sahibayn's proof is the hadith of the seven bones, which lists the forehead but not the nose. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the Quranic command to prostrate is general, and prostration is realized by placing part of the face; the nose and forehead are both valid because the whole face cannot be placed; the cheek and chin are excluded by consensus. The author then clarifies that the method of prostration (from Al-Inayah) follows the principle that the part closest to the ground is placed first and the part closest to the sky is raised first. Thus, knees first, then hands, then face (some say nose then forehead); when rising, reverse order. The response to the Sahibayn's proof points to another hadith using 'wajh' (face), which includes both nose and forehead, establishing their equality in sajdah. The practical ruling: sufficing with only the forehead is agreed upon by all Hanafis; sufficing only with the nose is permissible according to Abu Hanifa (with dislike) but not according to the Sahibayn unless there is an excuse.

Key Terms
جبهة (jabhah): The forehead; one of the seven bones of prostration
وجہ (wajh): Face; in the context of sajdah, includes both nose and forehead
اقتصار (iqtisar): Limiting oneself to one part (nose or forehead) in sajdah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which limb should be placed first when going into sajdah?
A) Hands
B) Forehead
C) Knees
D) Nose

Key Takeaway
The sunnah order for sajdah is knees, hands, then face; for rising, reverse.

Placing Hands and Knees: Sunnah of Sajdah, Not Obligation
Dispute on the legal status of placing hands and knees during sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on placing hands and knees in sajdah, identify the proof used by opposing scholars, and evaluate the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Placing hands and knees in sajdah is sunnah, because prostration is defined by the face, not the supporting limbs.

In this lesson, we examine a classic dispute between the Hanafi school and other scholars over a simple action in prayer: placing the hands and knees on the ground during prostration. The Hanafi school holds it is sunnah (recommended), while others consider it wajib (obligatory). We will trace the evidence from both sides and understand the reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and the Hanafi position
First, note that the author of Al-Hidayah states the Hanafi position clearly: placing hands and knees is sunnah (masnun). Recognize that this is the relied-upon view within the school, even though some Hanafi scholars differ.
Imam Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, is among those who consider it wajib, showing intra-school ikhtilaf.
2
State the opposing view and its proof
Identify the opponents: Imam Zufar, Imam al-Shafi'i, and Faqih Abu al-Layth. Their key proof is the hadith: 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones.' They argue that a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub), so placing all seven limbs is wajib.
The hadith is authentic (sahih), but the disagreement is about its interpretation (wajh al-dalalah).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the command is for the act of prostration itself, not for each individual limb. Prostration is essentially placing the face (forehead and nose) on the ground; hands and knees are means of support, not parts of the essence. Since prostration is possible without them (e.g., due to injury), they are not wajib.
This reasoning distinguishes between the rukn (pillar) of sajdah and its sunnan (recommended acts).
4
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is that if someone deliberately omits placing hands and knees, the Hanafi school considers the prayer valid but makruh tanzihan, while the Shafi'i school would require repetition if done intentionally without excuse.
This flexibility reflects the Hanafi principle of easing the prayer for those with valid excuses.

Source Text

ہاتھوں وگھٹنوں کا زمین پر رکھنا مسنون ہے : صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ ہمارے نزدیک ہاتھوں اور گھٹنوں کا زمین پر رکھنا مسنون ہے۔ امام زفر امام شافعی اور فقیہ ابواللیث نے کہا کہ یہ واجب ہے ان حضرات کی دلیل حضور کا قول امرت ان اسجدالخ ہے۔ وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ مجھے سات ہڈیوں پر سجدہ کرنے کا امر فر مایا گیا ہے اور امر کا موجب وجوب ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ میں ساتوں اعضاء کو زمین پر رکھنا واجب ہے اور ان سات اعضاء میں ہاتھ اور دونوں گھٹنے بھی ہیں اس وجہ سے دونوں ہاتھ اور دونوں گھٹنے زمین پر رکھنا واجب ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دونوں ہاتھ اور دونوں گھٹنے زمین پر رکھے بغیر سجدہ کرناممکن ہے اس لئے ان کا زمین پر رکھنا سجدہ کے مفہوم میں
Placing the hands and knees on the ground is sunnah. The author of Al-Hidayah said: According to us, placing the hands and knees on the ground is sunnah. Imam Zufar, Imam al-Shafi'i, and Faqih Abu al-Layth said: It is wajib. Their proof is the Prophet's saying: 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones...' The inference is that the command indicates obligation, so placing all seven limbs is wajib, and among them are the hands and knees. Our proof is that prostration is possible without placing the hands and knees on the ground, so their placement is not part of the essence of prostration.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute over the legal status of placing the hands and knees during sajdah. The Hanafi school (as stated in Al-Hidayah) holds that it is sunnah (recommended), not wajib (obligatory). Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar), Imam al-Shafi'i, and Faqih Abu al-Layth argue that it is wajib based on the hadith 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones,' which includes the hands and knees. Their reasoning: a command (amr) indicates obligation, so all seven bones must be placed. The Hanafi response: the command is for prostration, and prostration is realized by placing the face (nose and forehead). Hands and knees are means of support, not essential parts; therefore, their placement is sunnah. The text ends mid-argument, but the Hanafi position is clear: since prostration can be performed without putting hands and knees down (e.g., if one is injured), they are not wajib.

Key Terms
مسنون (masnun): Sunnah; recommended but not obligatory
امر (amr): Command; in usul al-fiqh, usually indicates obligation
سجود (sujud): Prostration; a pillar of prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on placing the hands and knees on the ground during prostration?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Sunnah (recommended)
C) Makruh (disliked)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
According to the Hanafi school, placing hands and knees during sajdah is sunnah, not wajib, because the essence of prostration is the face, and the command in the hadith is for prostration itself.

The Inclusion of the Nose in Sujood: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Resolving the dispute on whether the nose alone suffices for sujood in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sujood on the nose alone and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The nose is a valid part of the face for sujood; Abu Hanifa permits it alone, Sahibayn require the forehead without an excuse.

In the Hanafi school, there is a well-known dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding the sufficiency of prostrating only on the nose. This lesson examines the proofs each side presents and the practical consequence of the disagreement. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi methodology for deriving rulings from conflicting hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
State the view of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the validity of sujood performed solely on the nose.
Both positions are within the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's proof
Examine the hadith of the seven bones (forehead, hands, knees, feet) and its implication that the nose is not mentioned, thus not a valid place.
The hadith is from Ibn Abbas, recorded in the six canonical books.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Understand the absolute Quranic command to prostrate and the reasoning that prostration is realized by placing part of the face; also examine the hadith that uses 'wajh' (face) including the nose.
The Quranic command is mutlaq (general).
4
Follow the Hanafi response
See how the author rebuts the Sahibayn's proof by citing a narration that replaces 'jihah' with 'wajh', establishing that the nose is part of the face.
The response uses the principle of tarjih (preference) between conflicting narrations.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference in rulings: if one prays only on the nose, the prayer is valid according to Abu Hanifa but invalid (or requires excuse) according to the Sahibayn.
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is Abu Hanifa's view.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم
۵۵
باب صفۃ الصلوة
ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ بلا عذر ناک پر اکتفاء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے ہاں اگر کوئی عذر ہو تو شرعا جائز ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جو کتب ستہ میں مذکور ہے
عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم امرت ان اسجد على سبعة اعظم على الجبهة واليدين والر كبتين واطراف القدمين
بن عباس رضی اللہ تعالی عنہما نے فرمایا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ مجھے حکم دیا گیا کہ میں سجدہ کروں سات ہڈیوں پر پیشانی پر دونوں ہاتھوں دونوں گھٹنوں اور دونوں قدموں کے پوروں پر۔ منہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ جن سات ہڈیوں پر سجدہ کا حکم دیا گیا ان میں ناک کا ذکر نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے ثابت ہوا کہ ناک محل سجد ہ نہیں ہے اور جب ناک محل سجدہ نہیں ہے تو ناک پر اکتفا کرنا بھی درست نہیں ہوگا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآن پاک میں مطلقاً سجدہ کا حکم دیا گیا ہے اور سجدہ بعض چہرہ رکھنے سے متحقق ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ پورے چہرے کا رکھنا ناممکن ہے اس لئے کہ ناک اور پیشانی ایسی ابھری ہوئی ہڈیاں ہیں جو پورے چہرے کوزمین پر رکھنے سے مانع ہیں بہر حال جب پورے چہرے کا زمین پر رکھنا متعذر ہے تو بعض چہرے کا زمین پر رکھنا مامور بہ ہوگا لیکن گال اور ٹھوڑی بالا جماع خارج ہیں یعنی آیت اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے اگر چہ ان کو بھی شامل ہے لیکن بالا جماع آیت میں مراد نہیں ہیں کیونکہ سجدہ سے مراد تعظیم ہے اور گال اور
ٹھوڑی زمین پر رکھنے سے تعظیم مشروع نہیں ہوئی اس لئے یہ دونوں سجدہ کے مفہوم سے خارج ہوں گے۔ پس اب ناک اور پیشانی باقی رہ گئے اور یہ دونوں سجدہ کا محل ہیں اس لئے ان دونوں پر سجدہ کرنا جائز ہے اور چونکہ پیشانی پر اکتفاء کرنا جائز ہے اس لئے ناک پر بھی اکفتار کرنا جائز ہوگا۔
والمذکور فیمار وی الخ سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مشہور روایت میں بجائے جہہ کے وجہ مذکور ہے چنانچہ سفن اربعہ میں حضرت عباس بن عبد المطلب سے مروی ہے انه سمع رسول الله يقول اذا سجد العبد سجد معه سبعة أراب وجهه وكفاه وركبتاه وقدماہ یعنی حضور و کوفرماتے ہوئے سنا کہ بندہ جب سجدہ کرتا ہے تو اس کے ساتھ سات اعضاء سجدہ کرتے ہیں اس کا چہرہ اس کی ہتھیلیاں اس کے گھٹنے اور اس کے دونوں قدم اس حدیث میں وجہ مذکور ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ منہ سے ناک اور پیشانی دونوں مراد ہیں اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ سجدہ کے حکم میں ناک اور پیشانی دونوں برابر ہیں۔
Chapter on the description of prayer. And the Sahibayn said: Without excuse, it is not permissible to suffice with the nose; yes, if there is an excuse, it is permissible by Shariah. The proof of the Sahibayn is the hadith mentioned in the six books: From Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: on the forehead, the hands, the knees, and the tips of the feet. So the deduction is that among the seven bones commanded for prostration, the nose is not mentioned, hence it is established that the nose is not a place for prostration. And when the nose is not a place for prostration, then sufficing with it is not correct. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the Holy Quran commands prostration absolutely, and prostration is realized by placing part of the face, because placing the entire face is impossible since the nose and forehead are prominent bones that prevent placing the whole face on the ground. In any case, when placing the whole face on the ground is not feasible, placing part of the face is commanded. However, the cheek and chin are excluded by consensus, i.e., the verse includes them in its absolute application, but they are not intended in the verse due to consensus, because prostration means reverence, and placing the cheek and chin on the ground does not constitute prescribed reverence, so these two are excluded from the meaning of prostration. Thus the nose and forehead remain, and both are places for prostration, so it is permissible to prostrate on both. And since it is permissible to suffice with the forehead, it is also permissible to suffice with the nose. And 'al-madhkūr fī mā rawā...' is the answer to the Sahibayn's proof. The summary of the answer is that in the famous narration, instead of 'jihah', 'wajh' is mentioned. Accordingly, in the Sunan al-Arba'ah, it is narrated from Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib that he heard the Messenger of Allah say: When the servant prostrates, seven limbs prostrate with him: his face, his palms, his knees, and his feet. In this hadith, 'wajh' is mentioned, and it has already passed that the face means both the nose and the forehead. Therefore we said that in the ruling of prostration, the nose and forehead are equal.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sufficiency of the nose for sujood. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule that it is impermissible to limit sujood to the nose without an excuse, based on the hadith listing seven bones (forehead, hands, knees, feet) which does not include the nose. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the Quranic command to prostrate is absolute; since the entire face cannot touch the ground, part of it suffices, and the nose and forehead are the prominent parts; the cheek and chin are excluded by consensus. Additionally, a narration using 'wajh' (face) proves that the nose is included. The author then provides a response to the Sahibayn's proof, arguing that the more famous hadith uses 'wajh', which encompasses both nose and forehead. Thus, both are equally valid for sujood. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view: prostration on the nose alone is permissible, though it is better to include both.

Key Terms
وجہ (wajh): Face; in this context, the complete face including nose and forehead.
ناک (naak): Nose; its usage in sujood is disputed between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is sujood on the nose alone valid?
A) Because the Quran commands sujood absolutely, and it is achieved by placing part of the face, which includes the nose.
B) Because the hadith of seven bones explicitly mentions the nose.
C) Because the Sahibayn's proof is weak and should be discarded.
D) Because the nose is physically larger than the forehead.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the nose and forehead are equally valid parts for sujood; the mufta bihi is permissibility of sujood on the nose alone, though it is better to include both.

Hands and Knees in Sujood: Sunnah or Wajib?
Determining whether placing hands and knees in sujood is wajib or sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on placing hands and knees in sujood, explain the opposing view, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the hadith of seven bones.

Core Idea
A command does not always impose obligation; the Hanafi school holds that placing hands and knees in sujood is sunnah, not wajib.

In this lesson, we examine a key disagreement within and across madhhabs: whether the hands and knees must touch the ground in sujood. The Hanafi school, represented by al-Hidayah, holds it is sunnah. We will analyse the proofs from both sides and understand the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State the Hanafi ruling on placing hands and knees in sujood and note the authority behind it (Sahib al-Hidayah).
The ruling is sunnah (masnun) per the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing position and its dalil
List the scholars who hold it is wajib (Imam Zufar, Imam al-Shafi'i, Faqih Abu al-Layth) and their proof: the hadith 'umirtu an asjuda' (I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones) and the usul principle that a command indicates obligation.
The hadith is common to both parties but interpretation differs.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the hadith
The Hanafi response has two parts: (1) the hadith only identifies the organs of prostration, not a requirement to ground all; (2) the command (amr) can be for recommendation (nadb) as well as obligation, and context supports the non-obligatory interpretation because sujood is possible without grounding hands and knees.
This shows the Hanafi approach to reconciling conflicting indicators.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: In the Hanafi school, omitting hands/knees does not invalidate prayer; in the opposing view, intentional omission invalidates prayer.
This clarifies the importance of the ijtihad.
5
Summarise the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi madhhab is that placing hands and knees is sunnah; this is what a fatwa would follow.
The tarjih authority is Sahib al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہاتھوں وگھٹنوں کا زمین پر رکھنا مسنون ہے : صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ ہمارے نزدیک ہاتھوں اور گھٹنوں کا زمین پر رکھنا مسنون ہے۔ امام زفر امام شافعی اور فقیہ ابواللیث نے کہا کہ یہ واجب ہے ان حضرات کی دلیل حضور کا قول امرت ان اسجدالخ ہے۔ وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ مجھے سات ہڈیوں پر سجدہ کرنے کا امر فر مایا گیا ہے اور امر کا موجب وجوب ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ میں ساتوں اعضاء کو زمین پر رکھنا واجب ہے اور ان سات اعضاء میں ہاتھ اور دونوں گھٹنے بھی ہیں اس وجہ سے دونوں ہاتھ اور دونوں گھٹنے زمین پر رکھنا واجب ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دونوں ہاتھ اور دونوں گھٹنے زمین پر رکھے بغیر سجدہ کرناممکن ہے اس لئے ان کا زمین پر رکھنا سجدہ کے مفہوم میں داخل نہیں ہوگا۔ اور حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث فقط اس پر دلالت کرتی ہے کہ یہ سات اعضاء سجدہ کا مل ہیں اس پر کوئی دلالت نہ تر کہ ان تمام کا زمین پر رکھنا لازم ہے۔ اور رہا یہ کہ حدیث میں امرت کا لفظ آیا ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ امر جس طرح وجوب کے مات آتا ہے اسی طرح ندب کے لئے بھی آتا ہے ہو سکتا ہے کہ یہاں امر وجوب کے لئے مستعمل نہ ہو۔
Placing the hands and knees on the ground is sunnah. The author of Al-Hidayah said: In our view, placing the hands and knees on the ground is sunnah. Imam Zufar, Imam al-Shafi'i, and Faqih Abu al-Layth said that it is wajib. The proof of these people is the saying of the Prophet: 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones' etc. The deduction is that the Prophet said he was commanded to prostrate on seven bones, and a command necessitates obligation (wujub). Therefore it is understood that in prostration, placing all seven limbs on the ground is wajib, and among these seven limbs are the hands and both knees, so placing both hands and both knees on the ground is wajib. Our proof is that it is possible to perform prostration without placing both hands and both knees on the ground, so their placement is not included in the meaning of prostration. And the answer to the hadith is that this hadith only indicates that these seven limbs are the limbs of prostration; it does not indicate that placing all of them on the ground is necessary. As for the word 'umirtu' in the hadith, the answer is that the command (amr) sometimes occurs for obligation and sometimes for recommendation (nadb); it is possible that here it is not used for obligation.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the legal status of placing the hands and knees on the ground during sujood. The author of Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi position: it is sunnah (recommended). Imam Zufar (Hanafi), Imam al-Shafi'i, and Faqih Abu al-Layth hold that it is wajib. Their proof is the hadith 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones,' arguing that a command indicates obligation. The Hanafi response: the command could be for recommendation, and the hadith only identifies the limbs, not that they all must touch the ground. Additionally, sujood is possible without placing hands and knees, so they are not integral to the act. Therefore, the Hanafi school maintains that placing them is a sunnah; omitting them does not invalidate the prayer, though it is against the superior practice.

Key Terms
مسنون (masnūn): Recommended act (sunnah), as opposed to wajib (obligatory).
امرت (umirtu): The past passive verb 'I have been commanded', used as a basis for the wajib argument.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi school's ruling on placing the hands and knees on the ground during sujood?
A) Wajib, and omitting it invalidates prayer.
B) Sunnah, and omitting it does not invalidate prayer.
C) Fard, like the pillars of prayer.
D) Makruh, discouraged.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that placing hands and knees in sujood is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation, because the command can be interpreted for recommendation and the act is possible without grounding them.

Feet in Sujood: Fard or Not According to Hanafi Imams
Intra-Hanafi dispute on foot placement in sujood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the differing Hanafi opinions on placing the feet in sujood and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Even among the Hanafi masters, the obligation of the feet in sujood is disputed — one foot may be excused, both feet are fard for most.

In this passage, we encounter an intra-Hanafi point of contention: Is placing both feet on the ground during sujood fard (obligatory) or merely part of the sunnah? The passage presents three opinions: the strict view of Imam Quduri, the more lenient view of Qadi Khan, and the equivalence view of Imam al-Tamāṭā'ī. Your task is to parse these positions and understand the practical consequences for salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
What is the act in question? What is the range of rulings (fard vs. permissible vs. not fard)?
2
List the three opinions
Name each scholar and their exact ruling on both feet, one foot, etc.
3
Compare the evidence basis

4

What practical difference does this make for a person praying? (e.g., validity of sujood if one foot is off the ground.)
5

As for the ruling regarding placing both feet on the ground in sujood, in this regard Imam Quduri mentioned that placing both feet on the ground in sujood is fard. Therefore, if one prostrates and lifts the toes of the feet above the ground, it is not permissible. Imam al-Karkhi and Abu Bakr al-Jassas also hold this opinion. And if one foot is placed on the ground and one is lifted, then it is permissible. And Qadi Khan declared it permissible with karahah (dislike). Imam al-Tamāṭā'ī said that in terms of non-obligation, both hands and both feet are equal.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of placing the feet on the ground during sujood. Imam Quduri, followed by Karkhi and Jassas, rules that placing both feet on the ground is fard (obligatory); lifting the toes invalidates the sujood. For the case of lifting one foot, Qadi Khan says it is permissible but with karahah (dislike). Imam al-Tamāṭā'ī equates the feet with the hands, implying that neither is fard. The text does not explicitly resolve the ikhtilaf, but the later Hanafi position is that it is necessary (wajib) to place the toes of each foot, while the majority position is that it is fard.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): Obligatory; according to some Hanafi scholars, placing both feet is fard in sujood.
نکراہت (karāhat): Dislike (makruh); Qadi Khan allows lifting one foot but with karahah.

Prostrating on a Turban or Extra Cloth: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on sujood on turban/cloth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on sujood on a turban or extra cloth, cite the key hadith proofs, and contrast the Shafi'i objection with the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Prostrating on a turban or extra cloth is valid in Hanafi fiqh, supported by the Prophet's practice, even though Shafi'is require the forehead to be bare.

This passage addresses a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the validity of sujood when the forehead is covered by a turban or an extra portion of one’s garment. The Hanafi school, relying on the Prophet's own actions and those of his Companions, holds that such prostration is perfectly valid. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, requires the forehead to be directly exposed to the ground. In this lesson, we will examine the Hanafi proofs and the inter-madhhab reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify what each school rules on sujood on the middle of a turban (kūr al-'imāma) or extra cloth (fāḍil al-thawb). Hanafi: permissible; Shafi'i: invalid.
2
Identify the Hanafi proofs
Locate the three hadith presented: Ibn Abbas on the Prophet's practice, Ibn Abi Awfa's direct observation, and Anas on using cloth in heat.
Each hadith is a dalīl for permissibility.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalālah
Explain how each hadith proves permissibility: the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates jawāz; the Companions' practice confirms it.
Hanafi usul: fi'l al-nabī yufīdu al-jawāz.
4
Understand the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i requirement is that the forehead must be bare (wājib). The Hanafi response: the Prophet's explicit practice overrides this generality, and the cloth is part of one's attire, not a barrier.
The response uses takhsīs of the general rule by the Prophet's action.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilāf
What is the practical difference? In Hanafi, the prayer is valid and no repetition needed; in Shafi'i, if done intentionally, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
The muftā bihi is the Hanafi position.

The ruling on prostrating on the middle of the turban or on the extra cloth. So if one prostrates on the middle of his turban or on the extra of his cloth, it is permissible, because the Prophet used to prostrate on the middle of his turban, and it is narrated that the Prophet prayed in a single cloth, protecting himself with its extra from the heat and cold of the ground. Translation: Then if the worshiper prostrates on the middle of his turban or on the extra cloth, it is permissible, because the Prophet used to prostrate on the middle of his turban, and it is narrated that the Prophet prayed in a single cloth, with the extra of which he protected himself from the heat and cold of the ground. Explanation of the issue: In our view, prostrating on the middle of the turban or on the extra cloth is permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i said that prostrating on the middle of the turban is not permissible, because in his view it is obligatory for the forehead to be exposed during prostration. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both: that the Prophet used to prostrate on the middle of his turban. It is also narrated from 'Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: he said, 'I saw the Messenger of Allah prostrating on the middle of his turban.' Another proof is narrated from Ibn Abbas: that the Prophet prayed in a cloth, protecting himself with its extra from the heat and cold of the ground. Also, a narration from Anas ibn Malik: 'We used to pray with the Prophet in severe heat; when anyone of us could not place his face on the ground, he would spread his cloth and prostrate on it.' And he should spread his arms (yubdi dabi'ayhi) because of his saying: 'spread your forearms' (wa abd dabi'ayka). And it is also narrated as 'wa abd' from 'al-ibdad' which means extension, and the first is from 'al-ibda'' which means manifestation.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of prostrating on a turban (the folded part) or on an extra portion of one's garment. The Hanafi school holds that it is permissible, while Imam al-Shafi'i rules it invalid because he requires the forehead to be exposed. The Hanafi proofs are multiple: the Prophet was observed prostrating on his turban (Ibn Abbas and Ibn Abi Awfa), he prayed in a cloth protecting himself from the ground, and the Companions used cloth in extreme heat. The passage also includes a brief instruction to spread the arms during sujood, citing a hadith 'spread your forearms.' The Hanafi position is clear: these actions do not invalidate the prayer. The mufta bihi is permissibility.

Key Terms
عمامہ (imāma): Turban; in this context, the folded part on which one prostrates.
فاضل کپڑا (fāḍil al-thawb): Extra cloth; the part of the garment extending beyond the body used for prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Hanbali

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits sujood on a turban or extra cloth, supported by the Prophet's practice, and this is the mufta bihi position.

Placing Feet in Sajda: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on placing feet in sajda

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the various Hanafi positions on placing feet in sajda and identify the practical consequence of each view.

Core Idea
The obligation of placing both feet in sajda is disputed even within the Hanafi school—some deem it fard, others jaa'iz with karahah.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement about a specific element of sajda: whether placing both feet on the ground is obligatory or merely recommended. The passage presents the views of several early Hanafi authorities, showing that even within a single madhhab, there can be legitimate ikhtilaf on details of practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the legal question
The act is placing both feet on the ground during sajda. The question is whether this is fard (obligatory) or not.
The term 'fard' here carries the weight of a pillar—omission invalidates the sajda.
2
List the positions and their proponents
Imam Quduri, Karakhi, and Jassas hold it is fard. Qadi Khan says it is permissible with karahah (disapproval). Imam Tammam says it is not fard, equating feet with hands.
Note that 'permissible with karahah' means the act is valid but disliked.
3
Distinguish the legal categories
Fard (obligatory) vs. jaa'iz ma'a al-karahah (permissible but disliked) vs. adam farziyyah (non-obligatory). Each category has different consequences for the validity of sajda.
In Hanafi usul, fard is from qat'i evidence; here it is used more loosely.
4
Determine the practical differences
If fard: lifting both feet invalidates sajda. If jaa'iz with karahah: sajda is valid but makruh. If not fard: no problem at all.
Note the nuance: Qadi Khan's view adds karahah without invalidating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رہا یہ کہ سجدہ میں دونوں قدموں کو زمین پر رکھنے کا کیا حکم ہے سو اس بارے میں امام قدوری نے ذکر کیا کہ سجدہ میں دنوں قدموں زمین پر رکھنا فرض ہے چنانچہ اگر سجدہ کیا اور پیروں کی انگلیوں کو زمین سے اوپر اٹھالیا تو جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ امام کرخی اور ابوبکر جصاص بھی از کے قائل ہیں۔ اور اگر ایک قدم زمین پر رکھا اور ایک زمین سے اٹھا لیا تو یہ جائز ہے۔ اور قاضی خاں نے مع النکراہت جائز قرار دیا ہے۔ امام تم تائی نے کہا کہ عدم فرضیت میں دونوں ہاتھ اور دونوں قدم برابر ہیں۔
Now, what is the ruling regarding placing both feet on the ground in sajda? Regarding this, Imam Quduri mentioned that placing both feet on the ground in sajda is fard. Thus, if one made sajda and lifted the toes from the ground, it is not permissible. Imam Karakhi and Abu Bakr al-Jassas are also of this view. And if one placed one foot on the ground and lifted the other, it is permissible. And Qadi Khan declared it permissible with disapproval. Imam Tammam said that in terms of non-obligatoriness, both hands and both feet are equal.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the obligation of placing both feet on the ground during sajda. Imam Quduri holds that placing both feet is fard (obligatory), so lifting the toes invalidates sajda. Imam Karakhi and Abu Bakr al-Jassas agree. However, if only one foot is placed, it is permissible, though Qadi Khan adds a note of disapproval. In contrast, Imam Tammam argues that both hands and feet are equal in that their placement is not obligatory—similar to the hands, as per the earlier discussion. This shows the range of scholarly opinion within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An obligation that is necessary and cannot be omitted without invalidating the act.
عدم فرضیت (adam farziyyah): The state of not being fard; non-obligatoriness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Quduri, what is the ruling on lifting both feet during sajda?
A) It is permissible without any issue.
B) It is makruh but valid.
C) It is not permissible (naa-jaa'iz).
D) It is wajib but can be compensated with sahw.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to place both feet in sajda is subject to legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, with the stricter view being more precautionary.

Prostrating on the Turban or Extra Cloth: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on sajda on turban/cloth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prostration on the turban or extra cloth and explain why it is distinguished from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice (fi'l) permits prostration on one's own turban or cloth; it does not require direct skin contact with the ground.

This lesson explores an inter-madhhab dispute: is prostration on the turban or an extra fold of clothing valid? The Hanafi school, relying on multiple authentic hadiths of the Prophet's actions, holds it permissible. The Shafi'i school, emphasizing an uncovered forehead, considers it invalid. Understanding the basis of each position sharpens your ability to weigh textual evidence (naql) against general principles (usul).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its origin
Read the opening: 'If he prostrates on the core of his turban or the extra part of his cloth, it is permissible.' Notice the immediate citation of the Prophet's practice. This is a ruling derived from direct prophetic action (fi'l).
The Hanafi school often prioritizes the Prophet's habitual practice over general commands.
2
Locate the Shafi'i objection
The commentary mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i considers this invalid because 'it is wajib for the forehead to be uncovered during prostration.' This stems from the hadith of the seven limbs (al-sabr) and the requirement that the forehead touch the ground directly.
Shafi'i position is based on a command understood as wajib, while Hanafi sees the Prophet's action as overriding that general command.
3
Examine the Hanafi hadith proofs
Three hadiths are cited: Ibn Abbas (Prophet prostrating on turban), Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa (seeing the Prophet prostrate on his turban), and Anas (Companions prostrating on cloth in heat). Each shows the permissibility of an intervening layer.
The repetition of this action by the Prophet and Companions strengthens the Hanafi position.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi response is implicit: the prophetic fi'l (action) is the strongest proof for permissibility. It takes priority over a general command that might be interpreted as unconditional, because the Prophet's action clarifies the command.
This is an example of 'al-fi'l yubayyinu al-mujmal' (action clarifies the ambiguous).
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, a Hanafi believes his prayer is valid if he prostrates on his turban or sleeve. A Shafi'i must ensure his forehead is bare; otherwise he must repeat the prayer.
This difference directly affects millions of Muslims daily, especially in cold or hot climates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان سجد على كور عمامته او فاضل ثوبه جاز لان النبي عليه السلام كان يسجد على كور عمامته وير عليه السلام صلى فى ثوب واحد يتقى بفضوله حر الأرض وبردها ترجمہ پھر اگر نمازی نے عمامہ کے بیچ پر یا فاضل کپڑے پر سجدہ کیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ حضور اپنے عمامہ کے بیچ پر سجدہ کیا کرتے تھے اور روایت کیا جاتا ہے کہ حضور نے ایک کپڑے میں نماز پڑھی کہ اس کے فاضل سے زمین کی حرارت اور برودت کو بچاتے تھے۔ تشریح مسئلہ ہمارے نزدیک عمامہ کے پیج یا فاضل کپڑے پر سجدہ کرنا جائز ہے اور حضرت امام شافعی نے کہا کہ عمامہ کے بیچ پر سجدہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک سجدہ کے وقت پیشانی کا کھلا رہنا واجب ہے۔ ہماری دلیل ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما کی حدیث ہے ان النبي كان يسجد على كور عمامته یعنی حضور اپنے عمامہ کے پیچ پر سجدہ کرتے تھے عبد اللہ بن ابی اونی سے مروی ہے قال رأیت رسول الله يسجد علی کو رعمامته عبداللہ بن ابی اوفی کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو دیکھا کہ آپ اپنے عمامہ کے بیچ پر سجدہ کیا کرتے تھے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما سے مروی ہے ان النبي صلي في ثوب واحد تبقى بفضوله حر الارض وبردها یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک کپڑے میں نماز پڑھی آپ اس کے فاضل سے زمین کی حرارت سے بچتے تھے۔ ایک روایت حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے مروی ہے كان نصلي مع النبي في شدة الحر فاذا لم يستطع احدنا ان يمكن وجهه من الارض بسط ثوبه فسجد عليه حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ سے مروی ہے کہ ہم لوگ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ساتھ سخت گرمی میں نماز پڑھتے سو جب ہم میں سے کوئی قابو نہ پاتا کہ چہرہ زمین پر ٹیکے تو اپنا کپڑا بچھا کر اس پر سجدہ کرتا۔
If he prostrates on the core of his turban or the extra part of his cloth, it is permissible, because the Prophet used to prostrate on the core of his turban, and it is narrated that he prayed in a single cloth, protecting himself with its extra part from the heat and cold of the ground. Translation: Then, if a praying person prostrates on the middle of his turban or on the extra cloth, it is permissible, because the Prophet used to prostrate on the middle of his turban, and it is narrated that the Prophet prayed in a single cloth, protecting himself from the heat and cold of the ground with its extra part. Explanation: According to us, prostration on the turban's middle or extra cloth is permissible. Imam Shafi'i said it is not permissible because, in his view, it is wajib for the forehead to be uncovered during prostration. Our evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet used to prostrate on the core of his turban.' Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa reported: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah prostrating on the core of his turban.' Another evidence: from Ibn Abbas, 'The Prophet prayed in a single cloth, protecting himself from the heat and cold of the ground with its extra part.' Also, a hadith from Anas: 'We used to pray with the Prophet in severe heat, and when one of us could not place his face on the ground, he would spread his cloth and prostrate on it.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage addresses the inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding prostration on the turban or an extra fold of clothing. The Hanafi position, supported by multiple hadith proofs, is that such prostration is valid and permissible. The primary proofs include the practice of the Prophet himself prostrating on his turban, the hadith of Ibn Abbas about praying in a single cloth, and the hadith of Anas showing the Companions prostrating on their clothes in extreme heat. The Shafi'i objection is based on the requirement that the forehead be uncovered during sajda, which they consider wajib. The Hanafi response refutes this by presenting the sunnah of the Prophet, which overrides the general principle.

Key Terms
كور العمامة (kawr al-'imamah): The middle or rounded part of the turban that is wound on the head.
فاضل الثوب (fadil al-thawb): The extra portion of a garment that hangs beyond the body, like a fold or excess cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence the Hanafi school uses to permit prostration on the turban or extra cloth?
A) A qiyas from the obligation to cover the 'awrah during salah.
B) Multiple hadiths showing the Prophet and Companions prostrating on their turbans and clothing.
C) The general permissibility of any action in salah unless specifically prohibited.
D) The principle that necessity (darurah) overrules prohibitions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits prostration on the turban or extra cloth because the Prophet's own practice is the best evidence for the permissibility of covering the forehead during sajdah.

Opening the Arms During Sajda (Ibda' al-Dhabay)
Ruling and linguistic explanation of opening arms in sajda

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the position of the forearms during sajda and explain the evidence from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Forearms must be raised in sajda; like a sunnah, palms support on the ground.

This passage addresses a detail of the prayer posture: what to do with the forearms during sajda. The Prophet's instruction through Ibn Umar tells us explicitly to avoid spreading arms like a beast and to raise them. Understanding this sunnah helps perfect our prayer and ensures every limb participates in prostration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the placement of the forearms during sajda. The ruling is sunnah (recommended), not wajib. The command 'abid' (expose) is interpreted as a recommendation based on context and Hanafi principles.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar narrated by Adam ibn Ali al-Bakri, where he instructs: 'Do not spread like a beast, support on your palms, and expose your forearms.'
The hadith is ahad (single-transmission), so it gives zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit command 'A بد ضبعيك' indicates a recommended act. The analogy with beasts shows that spreading flat is disliked (makruh). The linguistic variant 'ibdaad' (stretching) and 'ibdaa' (showing) both support raising the arms.
The Hanafi principle: a command (amr) indicates obligation unless there is a qarina (context) turning it to recommendation. Here, the context of the prayer and the analogy with beasts indicate sunnah.
4
Note the linguistic explanation
The author explains that 'ibda'' can come from ibdaad (to stretch) or ibdaa' (to show). Both meanings lead to the same practice: keep forearms elevated and away from the ground.
This linguistic depth shows the precision of Hanafi scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبدى ضبعيه لقوله عليه السلام وابد ضبعیک ویروى وابد من الإبداد وهو المد والأول من الإبداء وهو الإظهار لم ترجمہ اور کشادہ کر دے اپنے دونوں بازو کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ ظاہر کر اپنے بازؤں کو اور روایت کیا جاتا ہے کہ ابد ابداد سے ماخوذ ہے معنی ہیں کھینچنا اور اول ابداء سے ہے معنی ہیں ظاہر کرنا۔ تشریح مسئلہ سجدہ کی حالت میں نمازی اپنے بازو ظاہر کرے یعنی کشادہ کرے درندے کی طرح زمین پر نہ بچھائے دلیل یہ روایت ہے عن آدم بن على البكرى قال رانى ابن عمر وانا اصلى لا اتجافى عن الأرض بذراعى فقال يا ابن اخی لاتبسط بسط السبع وادعم على راحتیک و ابد ضبعیک فانك اذا فعلت ذلك سجد كل عضو منك آدم بن علی البکری نے کہا کہ مجھے ابن عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما نے دیکھا اس حال میں کہ میں نماز پڑھتا کہ زمین سے اپنے ہاتھوں کو جدا نہیں کرتا تھا تو فرمایا کہ اسے بھیجے درندوں کی طرح مت بچا اور اپنی ہتھیلیوں پر ٹیک لگا اور اپنے باز و کشادہ کر کیونکہ جب تو نے ایسا کیا تو تیرا ہر عضو سجدہ میں ہو گیا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ ایک روایت میں ابتدال کی تشدید کے ساتھ آیا ہے ابداد سے مشتق ہے جس کے معنی کھینچنے کے ہیں یعنی اپنے باز کھینچے ہوئے رکھ اور اول ابداء سے مشتق ہے جس کے معنی ظاہر کرنے کے ہیں یعنی اپنے باز و ظاہر کر یعنی کشادہ رکھ۔
And he should expose his forearms (dhabay), because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Expose your forearms.' And it is narrated: 'ibda' is from ibdaad, which means stretching, and the first (version) is from ibdaa', which means showing. Translation: And he should open his two forearms, because the Prophet said: 'Make obvious your forearms.' And it is narrated that 'ibda' is derived from ibdaad, meaning stretching, and the first is from ibdaa', meaning showing. Explanation: In the state of sajda, the worshipper should expose his forearms, i.e., keep them open, and not spread them on the ground like a beast. The proof is the narration from Adam ibn Ali al-Bakri: 'Ibn Umar saw me praying without raising my forearms from the ground, and he said: O son of my brother, do not spread like the spreading of a beast, and support on your palms, and expose your forearms, for if you do that, every limb of you will prostrate.' The author of al-Hidayah said that in one narration, it comes with tashdid on the dal, derived from ibdaad, meaning stretching, i.e., keep your forearms stretched; and the first is from ibdaa', meaning showing, i.e., make your forearms apparent, i.e., keep them open.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that during sajda, the forearms (dhabay) should be raised and not placed flat on the ground like a beast. The proof is from the hadith of Ibn Umar instructing a person not to spread his arms like a beast but to support on the palms and expose the forearms. The commentator also clarifies the linguistic root of the word 'ibda'': it can be from ibdaad (to stretch) or ibdaa' (to show). Both meanings indicate keeping the arms away from the ground. This ruling is a sunnah practice that ensures every limb participates in sajda.

Key Terms
ضبع (dhab' (pl. dhabay)): The upper arm from elbow to shoulder; also used for forearm.
إبداء / إبداد (ibdaa' / ibdaad): To show/expose or to stretch/spread out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Raise them above the head.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi prayer, the forearms should be raised off the ground during sajda, supported by palms, to avoid beast-like spreading and to fulfill the sunnah.
