Keeping the Belly Away from Thighs in Sajda
Ruling with proof on sajda posture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended posture of keeping the belly away from the thighs in sajda and apply the exception for congregational prayer to avoid disturbing others.

Core Idea
Keep belly away in sajda is sunnah, but in congregation it may be suspended to avoid harming neighbors.

This passage addresses a specific posture in sajda: keeping the belly away from the thighs. The Prophet's practice demonstrates this sunnah to a great extent. However, when praying in a crowded row, some Hanafi jurists advise not to spread out to avoid disturbing the person next to you. This lesson explores the ruling, its evidence, and the practical adjustment for congregational harmony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is keeping the belly away from the thighs in sajda. The ruling is sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's practice (hadith) describing how he kept away so much that a goat kid could pass.
Hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The consistent practice (fi'l) of the Prophet indicates the sunnah nature of the act.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi jurists said: if in a row, do not keep away to avoid harming the neighbor.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi is to observe the sunnah when alone; in congregation, avoid if it causes disturbance.
The principle of avoiding harm (la darar) overrides the sunnah in this context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجافي بطنه عن فخذيه لأنه عليه السلام كان إذا سجد جافى حتى أن بهمة لو أرادت أن تمر بين يديه لمرت وقيل إذا كان فى صف لا يجافي كيلا يؤذى جاره ترجمہ اور اپنے پیٹ کو اپنی رانوں سے جدا کرے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم جب سجدہ کرتے تو جدا کرتے حتی کہ اگر بگری کا چھوٹا بچہ آپ کے ہاتھوں کے درمیان سے گذرنے کا ارادہ کرتا تو گذر جاتا اور کہا گیا کہ اگر صف میں ہو تو جدا نہ کرے تا کہ پڑوسی کو ایذاء نہ دے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نمازی سجدہ کی حالت میں اپنا پیٹ اپنی رانوں سے جدا ر کھے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم جب سجدہ کرتے تو جوف دیتے یعنی پیٹ رانوں سے جدا ر کھتے اور کہنیوں کو زمین سے اونچار کھتے حتی کہ اگر بکری کا بچہ آپ کے ہاتھوں کے درمیان سے گذرنا چاہتا تو گذر سکتا تھا۔ اور بعض فقہاء نے کہا کہ اگر صف کے اندر ہو تو ہاتھوں کو جوف نہ دے یعنی ان کو نہ پھیلائے تا کہ برابر والا ایذا محسوس نہ کرے۔
And he should keep his belly away from his thighs, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he prostrated, he kept away so much that if a young goat wanted to pass between his hands, it would pass. And it was said: If he is in a row, he should not keep away, lest he harm his neighbor. Translation: And he should keep his belly separate from his thighs, because the Prophet when he prostrated, he would keep away such that if a small goat kid intended to pass between his hands, it would pass. And it was said: If he is in a row, he should not keep away, so as not to harm his neighbor. Explanation: The ruling is that the worshipper in sajda should keep his belly away from his thighs. The proof is that the Prophet used to make space (tajafi) meaning he kept his belly away from his thighs and raised his elbows from the ground such that a goat kid could pass between his hands. Some jurists said that if one is in a row, he should not spread his hands (make space) so that the person next to him is not disturbed.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended posture of keeping the belly away from the thighs during sajda, as practiced by the Prophet. The extent of separation is described metaphorically: even a goat kid could pass between his arms. However, a conditional ruling is added: if one is praying in a row (i.e., in congregation), one should not separate too much to avoid inconveniencing the neighbor. This shows that the sunnah is adjusted for practical considerations (adab) in congregational prayer. The proof is the Prophet's consistent practice.

Key Terms
يجافي (yujafi): To keep away, to separate (the belly from the thighs).
بهمة (bahmah): A young goat or sheep, used to illustrate the extent of separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Pointing Toes Toward Qibla During Sajda
Ruling to point toes toward qibla during sajda

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pointing toes toward the qibla during sajda and explain the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
Every limb should face the qibla in sajda as much as possible.

During prostration (sajda), the Prophet ﷺ instructed that every limb should be directed toward the qibla. This lesson examines the specific ruling regarding the toes, which is a sunnah act that enhances the completeness of the prayer. The proof is a hadith that commands general orientation, as much as one is able.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states: 'And he should direct the toes of his feet towards the qibla.' This is a recommended (sunnah) act.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith: 'When the believer prostrates, every limb of him prostrates, so let him direct towards the qibla as much as he can.'
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'falyuwajjih' (let him direct) indicates a recommendation, not an obligation, because it is qualified by 'as much as possible' (ma istata'a), showing flexibility.
4
Note the hukm level
In Hanafi fiqh, the act is considered sunnah, not fard or wajib, because the dalil is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and the language allows for ease.

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that during sajda, the toes should be pointed towards the qibla. The proof is a hadith that every limb prostrates, so they should all be oriented towards the qibla. This is a sunnah act that completes the proper posture of sajda. The phrase 'as much as possible' indicates flexibility if one cannot fully face the qibla due to physical constraints.

Key Terms

Posture of Arms in Sujud: Spreading Not Like a Beast
Ruling on spreading arms in sujud with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah posture of the arms during sujud and identify the proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
In sujud, raise your arms and keep them away from the sides—do not spread them flat like a beast.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the recommended positioning of the arms during sujud. It clarifies that the arms should be raised and separated from the ground, contrary to the posture of a predatory animal that spreads its forelegs flat. The proof is based on the instruction of Ibn Umar to a person who was not separating his arms from the ground.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what physical act is being ruled upon and what classification it receives.
The act is the positioning of the arms during sujud. The ruling is sunnah, meaning recommended but not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited to support the ruling.
The proof is a narration from Adam ibn Ali al-Bakri reporting the action and words of Abdullah ibn Umar.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Examine how the dalil proves the ruling.
The imperative forms (لاتبسط, ادعم, ابد) indicate recommended actions. The comparison to a beast shows the posture to avoid.
4
Note the linguistic nuance
Understand the two possible derivations of the word 'abd' and how they affect the meaning.
The root can mean 'to pull' (to keep arms pulled back) or 'to show' (to display arms). Both support the same practical posture.

Translation: And make open your both arms because the Prophet said: show your arms. And it is narrated that ابد is derived from ابداد meaning to pull, and the first is from ابداء meaning to show. Explanation: In prostration, the worshiper should show his arms i.e., open them, not spread on the ground like a beast. Evidence: from Adam ibn Ali al-Bakri who said: Ibn Umar saw me while I was praying, not separating my arms from the ground, so he said: O son of my brother, do not spread like a dog, and support on your palms, and raise your upper arms, for if you do that, every limb of yours prostrates. The author of Hidayah said: In one narration, it comes with tashdid of the taa, derived from ابداد meaning to pull, so keep your arms pulled; and the first is derived from ابداء meaning to show, so show your arms i.e., keep them open.

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for the positioning of the arms during sajdah. The matn commands to 'show' or 'spread' the arms, meaning they should be raised and separated from the sides, not placed flat on the ground like a predatory animal. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar who instructed a person not separating his arms. The commentary also clarifies the linguistic root—whether the word comes from 'abdād' (pulling) or 'ibdā'' (showing). The Hanafi school follows this practice as part of the sunnah of sujud; omitting it is not invalidating but contrary to the recommended form.

Key Terms

ضبع (dhab‘): The upper arm; in the hadith it refers to the part from elbow to shoulder.

Keeping Stomach Away from Thighs in Sujud
Ruling on separating stomach from thighs in sujud with hadith evidence and congregation exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah ruling regarding stomach-thigh separation in sujud, identify the evidence from the Prophet's practice, and explain the exception for crowded rows.

Core Idea
Separating the stomach from the thighs in sujud is sunnah, but relaxed in congregation to avoid harming one's neighbor.

In this lesson, we examine a specific posture within the prayer: the separation of the stomach from the thighs during prostration. This is not an obligatory act but a sunnah that the Prophet (ﷺ) consistently practiced. However, the Hanafi school also provides a practical consideration for those praying in congregation, balancing the sunnah with the need to avoid disturbing one's neighbor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage rules upon: the posture of sujud specifically the separation of stomach from thighs. Identify the hukm level: sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: the Prophet's practice (hadith) that he separated until a small animal could pass between his hands and stomach.
The hadith is mentioned in the passage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling: the explicit description of the Prophet's posture indicates that separation is recommended (sunnah).
The Hanafi school categorizes this as a sunnah act, not wajib.
4
Note the exception for congregation
Identify the additional ruling: when praying in a crowded row, one may reduce or avoid separation to prevent harming the neighbor.
This exception is mentioned in the passage as 'qila' (it was said).

And he separates his stomach from his thighs because the Prophet, peace be upon him, when he prostrated, would separate until a small kid would pass between his hands if it wished. And it was said: if he is in a row, do not separate so as not to harm his neighbor. Translation: And separate your stomach from your thighs because the Prophet when he prostrated used to separate until a small kid of a goat would pass between his hands if it intended. And it is said: if in a row, do not separate so as not to cause discomfort to the neighbor. Explanation: The worshiper in prostration keeps his stomach away from his thighs. Evidence: the Prophet used to keep distance, raising his elbows from the ground. Some jurists said: if in a row, do not spread hands so as not to cause discomfort.

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that during prostration, one should keep the stomach away from the thighs, a practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) so much so that a small animal could pass between his arms and stomach. The commentary also mentions that if one is in a crowded row, this separation may be reduced to avoid disturbing neighbors. This is a sunnah act; the primary evidence is the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ).

Key Terms
يجافي (yujāfī): To separate; here specifically to keep the stomach away from the thighs during prostration.

Tasbih in Sujud: Ruling and Recommendation
Ruling on tasbih in sujud with minimum, recommendation, and imam's limit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tasbih in ruku' and sujud, identify the minimum number, and explain why it is sunnah rather than wajib.

Core Idea
Tasbih in sujud is sunnah, not wajib—three is the minimum, odd numbers recommended, imam limits to avoid aversion.

Tasbih (saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la') in ruku' and sujud is a well-known practice, but is it obligatory or recommended? This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the Hanafi position: it is sunnah, with three as the minimum for perfection. The author also addresses the imam's responsibility not to prolong, and refutes the argument for obligation using the bedouin hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine exactly what act is being ruled upon (tasbih in sujud/ruku') and what the hukm is (sunnah).
The passage explicitly states 'tashihaat ul-ruku' wa al-sujud sunnah'.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence used: the hadith commanding 'falyqul' and the Prophet's omission when teaching the bedouin.
Two conflicting proofs are presented; the bedouin hadith is given priority.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the bedouin hadith proves non-obligation: the Prophet did not mention tasbih in the essential teaching.
This shows tasbih is not part of the obligatory elements of prayer.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing view (some scholars consider it wajib) and their proof (command form and constant practice).
The opposing argument relies on the apparent imperative.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi position prevails: the bedouin hadith clarifies that the command is for recommendation, not obligation.
The mukhtalaf fih is resolved by preferring the more specific evidence.

فرمایا فلیقل۔ اور یہ امر کے صیغے ہیں اور امر کا موجب وجوب ہے لہذا ان اٹھا یہا دونوں کی تسبیحات کو واجب قرار دینا چاہئے تھا جواب اعرابی کو تعلیم دیتے وقت حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو بیان نہیں کیا تھا۔ اس لئے معلوم ہوا کہ ہو گیا۔ تسبیحات رکوع اور سجود کا حکم بطور وجوب نہیں بلکہ بطور استحباب ہے۔
And he says in his prostration: Subhana Rabbiyal A'la three times, that is the minimum because of his saying, peace be upon him: When one of you prostrates, let him say in his prostration: Subhana Rabbiyal A'la three times, that is the minimum i.e., the least of perfection. And it is recommended to increase beyond three in bowing and prostration, ending with an odd number, because he used to end with an odd number. And if he is an imam, he should not increase so that the people do not get bored leading to aversion. Then the tasbihs of bowing and prostration are sunnah, because the text covers them; (the rest unclear). Translation: And in prostration say Subhana Rabbiyal A'la three times, that is the minimum amount because the Prophet said: When someone prostrates, let him say in his prostration Subhana Rabbiyal A'la three times, that is the least amount for complete perfection. It is recommended to increase beyond three but finish on an odd number because the Prophet used to finish on an odd number. If the imam, he should not increase so much that the congregation gets bored and aversion arises. The tasbihs of ruku' and sujud are sunnah because the text (Quran/hadith) includes them; their tasbihs are not legislated (?) so not increased beyond the text. Explanation: Imam Quduri said: say Subhana Rabbiyal A'la three times; three times is the minimum. He wrote that omitting or reducing it is makruh. Evidence: Prophet's saying: When one prostrates, let him say in his prostration Subhana. And increasing beyond three is recommended provided it ends on an odd number. Evidence: the Prophet used to end the tasbihs on an odd number. The well-known hadith 'Indeed Allah is odd and loves odd' is also used. Author of Hidayah says: If one is imam, do not increase so much that people get bored. It is clear that tasbihs of ruku' and sujud are sunnah because the text (Quran) includes ruku' and sujud, not their tasbihs specifically. So it is proved they are not fard. But there is an objection: from not being fard it does not follow that they are sunnah; possibly wajib, as there are two proofs for obligation: first, the Prophet's continuous practice shows obligation; second, he said 'make them' (اجعلوها) for ruku' and 'let him say' (فليقل) for sujud, which are commands implying obligation. So one might consider them wajib. The answer: when teaching the bedouin, the Prophet did not mention them, so it is known that the ruling is not obligation but recommendation.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling of tasbih in sujud. The minimum is three repetitions of 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la'; this is the least to achieve perfection. It is recommended (mustahabb) to add more, but ending on an odd number, following the Prophet's practice. For an imam, he should not prolong so much as to bore the congregation. The passage then addresses the debate: is this tasbih wajib or sunnah? The author concludes it is sunnah, not wajib. The evidence: when the Prophet taught the bedouin (in the famous hadith of the man who prayed poorly), he did not mention the tasbih, only the pillars. Those who argue for obligation cite the Prophet's command and his constant practice. The response is that the Prophet's omission in that teaching indicates it is not obligatory but rather recommended.

Key Terms
تسبيح (tasbīḥ): Here specifically saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' in sujud and ruku'.
أدنى (adnā): The minimum amount for perfection—three repetitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of saying tasbih in ruku' and sujud?
A) Fard (obligatory)
B) Wajib (necessary)
C) Sunnah (recommended)
D) Makruh (disliked)

Key Takeaway
The tasbih in ruku' and sujud is sunnah, not wajib; three is the minimum, and the imam should not prolong to avoid burdening the congregation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Tasbih in Sujud and Ruku: Ruling and Recommended Practice
Explains the tasbih in sujud, minimal and recommended number, and its sunnah status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tasbih in ruku and sujud (sunnah), explain the proof from the Bedouin hadith, and describe the recommended number and imam's limit.

Core Idea
Tasbih in ruku and sujud is sunnah, not wajib, despite imperative commands — because the Prophet omitted it when teaching the Bedouin.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the ruling of the tasbih recited during ruku and sujud. Many assume it is wajib due to the imperative words used by the Prophet. The commentator explains the minimum of three recitations, the recommendation to increase with an odd number, and the crucial evidence from the incident of the Bedouin that proves the sunnah status. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' in sujud and 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azim' in ruku. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah), not wajib.
Sunnah muakkadah means the Prophet consistently performed it, but omission does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'When one of you prostrates, let him say in his prostration: Subhana Rabbiyal A'la three times.' The imperative 'falyuqul' is used.
Also the hadith 'Make it in ruku' with the imperative 'ij'aluha'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the imperative form (amr) normally indicates obligation (wujub). However, this general rule can be overridden by evidence. Here, the Prophet omitted these tasbih when teaching the Bedouin the essentials of prayer.
The omission in a teaching context shows the act is not required, shifting it to sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and Hanafi response
Some scholars (especially non-Hanafis) argue for wujub based on the imperatives. The Hanafi response is that the Bedouin hadith provides contextual evidence that the tasbih is not obligatory.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi tarjih is based on balancing the delils.

کہے اور
ہے جو۔
ہیں۔ اول یہ کہ رکوع اور سجود کی تسبیحات پر حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مواظبت فرمائی ہے جو دلیل وجوب ہے دوم یہ کہ رکوع کی تسبیحات کے بارے میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا اجعلوها اور سجدہ کی تسبیحات کے بارے میں فرمایا فلیقل۔ اور یہ امر کے صیغے ہیں اور امر کا موجب وجوب ہے لہذا ان اٹھا یہا دونوں کی تسبیحات کو واجب قرار دینا چاہئے تھا جواب اعرابی کو تعلیم دیتے وقت حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو بیان نہیں کیا تھا۔ اس لئے معلوم ہوا کہ ہو گیا۔ تسبیحات رکوع اور سجود کا حکم بطور وجوب نہیں بلکہ بطور استحباب ہے۔
Chapter on the Description of Prayer. Tasbih of Sujud. He says in his sujud: 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' three times, and that is the minimum, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'When one of you prostrates, let him say in his prostration: Subhana Rabbiyal A'la three times, and that is the minimum' i.e., the minimum of completeness of the collective. And it is recommended to increase beyond three in ruku and sujud after ending with an odd number, because he (peace be upon him) used to end with an odd number. And if he is an imam, he should not increase to the extent that the people become weary, so that it does not lead to aversion. Then the tasbih of ruku and sujud is sunnah, because the text encompasses them, and their tasbih is not increased beyond the text. [Urdu translation and commentary follows: He says in sujud three times Subhana Rabbiyal A'la, and this is the minimum amount because the Prophet said...]
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This is a ruling passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah, explaining the tasbih in sujud. The matn states: 'He says in his sujud: Subhana Rabbiyal A'la three times, and that is the minimum.' The commentator expands by providing the proof from the Prophet's hadith: 'When one of you prostrates, let him say in his prostration: Subhana Rabbiyal A'la three times, and that is the minimum.' The phrase 'that is the minimum' indicates the minimum degree of completeness for the congregation (adna kamil al-jam'). It is recommended (mustahab) to increase beyond three in both ruku and sujud, but one should conclude with an odd number because the Prophet used to do so. If one is an imam, he should not increase so much that the congregation becomes weary and averse. The ruling that the tasbih is sunnah is derived from the fact that the primary text (Quran and Sunnah) commands ruku and sujud but does not specify these tasbih; thus they are additional and not wajib. The commentator then addresses a possible objection: Since the Prophet consistently recited these tasbih and used imperative forms ('ij'aluha' and 'falyu qul'), one might think they are wajib. The Hanafi response is that when the Prophet taught the Bedouin the essential elements of prayer, he did not mention these tasbih, proving they are not wajib but rather mustahab (recommended).

Key Terms
أدنى كمال الجمع (adna kamil al-jam'): The minimum completeness for the congregation, referring to the minimal tasbih that fulfills the recommended practice.
تسبيحات (tasbihat): The utterances of 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' in sujud and 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azim' in ruku.
استحباب (istihbab): Recommended, a level above mubah and below sunnah muakkadah. The text uses it interchangeably with sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the tasbih in ruku and sujud?
A) It is wajib because the Prophet commanded it.
B) It is sunnah because the Prophet did not mention it when teaching the Bedouin.
C) It is fard because it is part of the prayer.
D) It is makruh to recite more than three times.

Key Takeaway
Tasbih in ruku and sujud is sunnah muakkadah; its omission does not invalidate prayer, and it is recommended to recite at least three times, ending with an odd number.
